DATE: 2026-06-29 21:25:51 | SENDER: Conor O'Mara <COMARA@jefferies.com> | SUBJECT: Notes from call with Micron IR. Lots of discussion on SCAs. Also working on super IO NAND.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CONFERENCE CALL WITH MICRON.

 

Our Fubon team hosted a call with head of Micron IR Satya Kumar this morning. 

 

Here are my notes from the call. 

 

*	SCAs announced in the earnings call is a very important development which will accelerate the business model transformation from a company with limited visibility with annual non binding quarterly contracts to SCAs that go 3-5 years with binding take or pay requirements. Includes financial commitments. 

	*	Micron have completed 16 SCAs with total volume closed 20% of DRAM and 1/3rd of NAND volumes. In sales its 25% of total company sales closed so far. Still discussing additional SCAs. Should be up to 50% of company sales. 
	*	SCAs gives more certainty on demand and volume. It’s a take or pay contract. Auto customers are 3 and 5 for other customers. The SCAs have financial commitments with $22bn in financial commitments $18bn in cash customer deposits held on the Balance Sheet which will be returned weighted to 2H of the contract.
	*	These are not escrow they are cash deposits $18bn with letter of credits $4bn. The cash goes into financing cash flow it doesn’t go into operating cash. Its unrestricted available for any purpose it will accumulate interest. In the later part of the contract this cash will be retuned to the customers. 
	*	Pricing 3 mechanisms with a ceiling and a floor price. The ceiling is price to CYQ2 market price. Havent specified the floor but have said the margins are well above the peak margins of any prior cycle. 
	*	Smaller volumes have fixed pricing
	*	2 of the 16 contracts have floating pricing. 

*	SCAs/LTAs have been around before how are they different this time? Micron acknowledges in the past long term agreements haven’t held. The most fundamental aspects are 

	*	Supply. On supply we have slowing of Moores Law harder to add bits. HBM trade ratio decreases supply. Product complexity is increasing. Its much harder to build supply and build new fabs. 
	*	Demand AI has fundamentally changed demand from mid teens to 20s and we are supply constrained as AI is riding on memory especially as we go to inference the performance of the memory sub system is critical to AI. If we go back into prior downturns there was pull forward not sustainable demand.
	*	Product. The strategic performance of memory has changed for cost per token. Memory is extremely important to customers we are now talking to model companies like Anthropic. We have deep collaboration with customers. The technology roadmap for memory is very different. 

*	The guidance reflects a meaningful slowdown in the rate of price increases. Certain volumes will have known pricing. This is below 25% based on SCA and not all have fixed price 2 don’t have pricing in them. But expect over time 40% of sales of Micron will have band or fixed pricing. The balance of the business not on SCA can vary with the market price. Micron don’t comment on market pricing in the future. 
*	Micron said up to 40% of volumes could be on SCAs with known pricing should expect the ceiling price is close to CYQ2 market price. This is the target beyond that cant comment on whether the contracts remaining to be signed will have the same pricing or not. 
*	Micron hasn’t made a comment on SCA volumes but as invest in capex will have more volumes to sell demand is significantly higher than volumes this will continue in CY27 and CY28. Demand is more than supply even for the SCA portion. The intent of the SCA is to give more certainty for capex planning so its natural to think supply will increase. 
*	Have entered into an agreement with ASML with increased adoption of EUV. The SCA helps to transform the business model of capex planning. 
*	This also allows more predictable financial returns. 
*	FY27 Capex was announced in March and have updated since. In FY27 said capex will be above mid $40bn up from Y27bn in FY26. More than half of this is for facilities. In terms of capacity HBM mix is a key factor and product mix can be different and specific nodes. We normally disclose that later in the year in how CY27 is shaping up. CY 26 DRAM bit shipments are low 20s including HBM and NAND 20% 
*	Demand is definitely above supply and will remain tight in 2027 and into 2028. Agentic AI drives a sharp increase in context windows and KV Cache driving more CPUs. Have to reduce the content in each of these servers to ship more servers. Micron are the pioneers in SOCAMM. Did the 196 and 256 GB have broadest portfolio.
*	Investors do think maybe optimize towards conventional DRAM as HBM margins are lower than DRAM. But its not that simple as clients need matched sets. Micron is working closely with customers on product mix but its not just a simple decision to maximise bits by reducing HBM and increasing conventional like some investors think. 
*	On NAND there are some new applications KV Cache and vector database indexing which requires 50-100M IOPS compared to 5m. This is Storage NEXT from Nvidia Micron is working on this so yes some use cases are looking for SLC. 
*	The other product is KV Cache which cant be kept in DRAM. Keeping for some period of time which is different from normal use of NAND which is there for a long period of time. KV Cache one possibility is fewer bits per cell could improve endurance which could help customer TCO but that has a cost impact. Working on more QLC with better endurance. So maybe some will look at TLC as well. 

 

 

The last questions there on NAND were from me. So Micron is also working on a super IO product like Kioxia. This super IO could be impactful for NAND so Im resending here also why that makes me prefer Kioxia over Sandisk. 

 

 

 3 REASONS WHY I PREFER KIOXIA TO SANDISK. A quarter ago I admitted I was totally wrong on NAND and got onboard. I remain positive. But as I outlined on the call the other night and in meetings for the past few months I prefer Kioxia to Sandisk. 

*	Kioxia is more conservative

DATE: 2026-06-29 21:30:50 | SENDER: Mehdi Hosseini <mehdi.hosseini@sig.com> | SUBJECT: GLW - POSCO Takeaways: Confirming GLW Key Role in CPO Supply Chain
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
JUNE 29, 2026	
 
 
 
 
 
	
	
 
 
 
 
 
CLICK HERE TO VIEW FULL PDF REPORT <https://sig.bluematrix.com/links2/pdf/363b4048-a2f0-4616-808c-cfb0b01746bf> 	
Corning	
SIG ALERT 	
POSCO Takeaways: Confirming GLW Key Role in CPO Supply Chain	
Corning

Symbol: GLW

Rating:  Positive

Price:  $255.69

Risk:  Downside Risk

Market cap.:  $219,641mm

Sector: Technology Hardware

HIGHLIGHTS

*	Following Corning's announcements at the AI Data Center Optical Communications & Interconnect Tech Conference at POSCO Tower Yeoksam in Seoul held last week, we are increasingly confident in GLW's progress toward rolling out competitive FAU (Fiber Array Unit) offerings.

*	As we highlighted in our takeaways of Corning’s Analyst Day (link <https://sig.bluematrix.com/docs/pdf/3340611f-3591-46a0-bf83-08c5a4b95a84.pdf> ), which we reiterated in our 6/24 note (link <https://sig.bluematrix.com/docs/pdf/1a6fbfcf-8a79-43c7-a77e-d8ee8db7aecb.pdf> ), we expect GLW could act as a strategic partner for CPO commercialization through the standardization and manufacturing of the FAU. In this scenario, GLW supplies the FAU for integration into the CPO platform (PIC + EIC + Packaging), an opportunity that also provides customers with alternatives to TSMC's CoWoS-L (COUPE) platform.
*	At the conference, GLW unveiled multiple IP offerings spanning the full FAU stack: Glass Bridge (the optical connector to the PIC), passive optical layer solutions, fiber harnesses, and glass substrates with through-glass vias (TGVs). Glass Bridge directly links photonic integrated circuits (PICs) and optical fibers, bridging a size mismatch of several dozen times between on-chip waveguides (hundreds of nanometers) and fiber cores (1-8 micrometers). It uses wafer-based ion-exchange waveguide technology to create optical pathways within glass, enabling high-density optical I/O at the PIC front end while simplifying fiber-to-chip alignment. The initial product targets core pitches of 30 micrometers or greater and coupling loss below 2 dB and is being co-developed with multiple partners, including GFS. The broader CPO solution layers in fiber harnesses with FAUs integrated into the CPO Optical Engine, CPO-optimized fibers, connectors, fiber management hardware, and a glass-substrate packaging architecture with TGVs and flip-chip-mounted photonic devices.
*	Corning also presented GlassWorks AI, its end-to-end optical connectivity platform for AI data centers, covering infrastructure within data centers, between racks, and across campuses, spanning optical fibers, cables, connectors, FAUs, and alignment components.

DATE: 2026-06-30 01:04:27 | SENDER: Morgan Stanley Research <resweb@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: IDEA: Infineon Technologies AG (IFXGn.DE): Structural Breakout Story Playing Out
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Infineon Technologies AG (IFXGn.DE) 	
Structural Breakout Story Playing Out	 
Read Full Report <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/66a7e21a-7154-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae?t=1782792130:2338:7753:527593380b83&m=1&ch=CDF Research ISG#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> 	 
(PDF: 17 Pages) 	
Europe 	
Stock Rating   Overweight
Price Target   €91.00

Lee Simpson, Shawn Kim, Nigel van Putten, Amelia M Scicluna	 
June 30, 2026

	
We continue to view Infineon as the key data centre beneficiary, but think it is unlikely for the upcoming site visit to offer a guidance update. We expect an in-line print, with resilient order book momentum, an industrial recovery profile, and commentary on AI data centre strength. 
Key takeaways	 

*	IFX’s FY3Q26 print should be broadly in line with guide. 
*	Order book resilience, better pricing, channel refill in autos, and improving industrial demand, are supporting the setup into Q4. 
*	The Dresden site visit is unlikely to trigger an immediate data centre target upgrade, but should improve visibility on capacity expansion plans. 
*	Litigation remains complex and jurisdiction-specific, but does not alter our view that IFX and Innoscience are key competitors in GaN. 
*	We remain OW, PT €91 as we continue to like the longer term story and think the stock remains undervalued given data centre earnings potential. 

Preview to earnings	 
Company / Focus KPI	 Focus KPI Surprise	 Likely impact to consensus EPS	 
Infineon Technologies AG (IFXGn.DE) 	
FY26 Revenue and GM% Guide	 	 In-line	 
	 Largely unchanged	 
View our takeaways <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/66a7e21a-7154-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae/#tkr=IFXGn.DE> 	
* Direction of next 12-month consensus EPS	 
Source: Company data, Morgan Stanley Research	 

Near-term surprise unlikely, but long term DC upside keeps us OW. The structural breakout story is playing out, and while we remain confident that Infineon will be the clear data centre beneficiary, we think the next print is unlikely to offer a guidance surprise. Last quarter, management raised FY revenue and margin guidance to reflect improving cyclical dynamics. We think it is too soon to expect another guidance uptick but remain positive on the long-term story and earnings potential. We expect the site visit to focus on power semi capacity and product offering, in particular strength in GaN, which would reaffirm our view of Infineon's key role in the DC power semi transition. However, we think this visit will be more of a qualitative discussion as opposed to an opportunity for management to update data centre guidance. We continue to like the long-term story and agree that data centre guidance is too conservative, however we expect little surprise this quarter.

Expecting an in-line print. Infineon reports FY3Q26 results on 5 August. We expect the company to deliver in-line numbers with guidance supported by resilient order book momentum, a modestly improving industrial recovery profile, and robust SiC demand, including incremental support from AI data centre applications. Pricing should become a more visible tailwind from Q4 FY26 onward, implying a constructive setup for the next-quarter guide. We also expect distribution channel inventory normalisation to support automotive sales through FY26, while pricing continues to firm, particularly in microcontrollers.

Dresden site visit: a signal of data centre strength but unlikely to offer new numbers. AI data centre demand remains robust, with customers placing orders earlier to secure capacity ahead of strengthening end demand. Infineon’s Dresden site visit on 1 July is unlikely, in our view, to bring an upward revision to next year’s data centre sales target; that is more likely to come with the FY26 print in November. However, we expect the event to provide greater visibility on the operational initiatives underway to expand capacity against demand that continues to exceed current targets. We expect commentary to focus on front-end wafer capacity but to include discussion on the progress with back-end alignment too (in Hungary). We also expect management to address the trajectory of GaN demand, the status and commercial relevance of GaN patent infringement claims, Infineon’s competitive positioning in vertical power delivery, and any potential FY28+ implications from possible 800V timing delays.

GaN litigation update. Infineon and Innoscience (covered by Daisy Dai) remain engaged in a multi-jurisdictional patent dispute across Germany, the US and China relating to gallium nitride power semiconductors. To date, the Munich Regional Court has issued multiple infringement judgments in Infineon’s favour, including injunctions restricting the manufacture, marketing and sale of infringing GaN products in Germany, alongside damages awards. In the US, the ITC found infringement of one Infineon patent and issued a limited exclusion order on certain Innoscience products, although some patent claims were invalidated and redesigned products were found non-infringing. By contrast, Innoscience has secured rulings in China, including injunctive relief against certain Infineon GaN products, primarily mid-voltage designs; Infineon continues to argue that proceedings remain ongoing, particularly for high-voltage designs, which represent the more material part of its business. Overall, the litigation remains active across jurisdictions, with rulings to date creating market-specific commercial restrictions rather than a global prohibition. The ultimate impact will depend on product design, patent validity challenges, appeals and related proceedings. Notwithstanding this, we continue to see Infineon and Innoscience as the key competitors in GaN for first-stage 800V server designs.

A reminder of our thesis: OW, PT €91. We continue to view Infineon as undervalued given the company's full stack power semi solutions for the data centre and our increasing confidence in Inf

New Research


Ad Agencies - five themes from Cannes <https://specialistsales.cmail19.com/t/d-l-wluhujd-hjyuihouk-r/> 
The Cannes Lions International Festival of Creativity took place last week, with 500 speakers sharing their views and visions for the future of the marketing industry. We highlight several themes that emerged from the presentations, with AI taking centre stage in topics that spanned: humans vs machines, the two-audience problem and the merits of effectiveness vs efficiency. Meanwhile, the growing importance of Creators in marketing briefs was another salient theme, as was the evolving role of agencies in the age of AI. We elaborate on these topics in the short email linked below and present our analysis of the Cannes Lions Grand Prix winners by holding group.

CTS Eventim (Buy) - fact from fiction <https://specialistsales.cmail19.com/t/d-l-wluhujd-hjyuihouk-y/> 
1) ANALYSIS: The data shows CTS Eventim taking share in Europe, not losing it. In this report, we challenge several misconceptions about the European live music market, concluding that US players are structurally ill-suited to the region, and that the AI threat is substantially overstated. We see several catalysts in H2 and reit our Buy rating. 2) VS CONS: no f’cast changes, but +1-6% & +2-7% above cons on revs & EBITDA. 3) VALUATION (FY27e): trades on GFC-trough multiples – 8x EV/adj EBITDA (target 15x), P/E 14x, FCF yield (ex WC) 6-7%, divi c4%, c1x ND/EBITDA – and an unwarranted 50% discount to Live Nation (Buy, $195 PT). 


Software & Internet


Anthropic - flexing pricing power over Amazon (Neutral)
The model lab has renegotiated a key part of its Amazon partnership, shifting how Amazon pays to use Anthropic's models.  Starting next year, Amazon will be charged based on tokens processed rather than compute hours - a change that could materially raise Amazon's costs. The shift has already prompted some Amazon engineers to "distill" Anthropic models to cut costs ahead of the new token-based pricing taking effect. Amazon relies on Anthropic to power a range of their products, including Alexa for shopping, the Kiro coding tool, and the Quick workspace assistant - they will be evaluating cheaper alternatives, including their in-house Nova models. 

Meta (Buy) - restricting usage of Claude and Code over distillation fears 
Meta is clamping down on how engineers in its applied AI engineering division use Anthropic's Claude Code and OpenAI's Codex, according to internal guidelines reviewed by The Information. The central worry is that outputs from these rival models could inadvertently seep into Meta's own training data — a form of "distillation" that could violate the tools' usage agreements and trigger, in the words of one internal memo, "serious escalations with partner companies.". The platform has drawn a sharp line since May, prohibiting the use of external model outputs to test Meta's models, using AI to hunt for bugs, or placing any AI-generated material inside infrastructure containers that the in-house model being tested can access. Meta is on track to spend billions of dollars on internal AI use alone this year. Having aggressively pushed AI adoption internally, it's now reining in escalating costs - including by capping employees' token usage and shifting development work onto MetaCode to reduce reliance on expensive external tools. 

AI regulation - Sen. Warner drafts first AI agent regulation bill
Senator Mark Warner will unveil draft legislation regulating the AI agent ecosystem. The bill mandates a strict "duty of loyalty," barring agents from favouring commercial partners over users. Crucially for the big tech/internet platforms, it prohibits networks with over 50m users from blocking registered 3P agents, potentially threatening walled gardens and human-driven ad monetisation. The FTC will oversee registration alongside NIST interoperability standards. While near-term passage is highly unlikely ahead of the midterms, this establishes Washington's first structural regulatory framework for the rapidly expanding agentic AI economy.

Uber (Buy) – Robotaxi pilot in Phoenix with Waymo ended
Waymo AVs are no longer available via the Uber app in Phoenix, vehicles will remain in use to make deliveries with DoorDash. Phoenix was Uber’s first pilot market with Waymo and was very limited in deployment (low teen number of AVs that were available on the Uber app versus Waymo having 500 AVs on its own app). As it stands the partnership between the two in both Austin and Atlanta still stand. While the stock u/p on this yday, it shouldn’t be a major surprise given most were not expecting this particular agreement to last very long given how small it was in scale. We remain confiden

Tech sell-off complete? After seeing two intra-month pullbacks, of ~7% and 5%, yesterday’s rally feels like it has legs. We may have a Tech sector ‘Everything Rally’. While Semis and Hardware have stretched positioning, the market jitters may first see a sharp rally followed by a rotation. The Fear / Greed monitor closed in the Extreme Fear region on Friday so there is room for stocks to move on sentiment, and positioning, before we are likely to have another consolidation period. While we have discussed SPX seasonality, NDX’s best month over the last 10 years has been July, averaging a 4.35% return with a 90% hit rate. August is also positive (+1.68%; 70% hit rate) and then September is typically the worst month of the year for the NDX.

Former Distinguished Research Scientist at NVIDIA Believes Physical AI Faces Challenges but Sees Progress in Robotics Development <https://research.alpha-sense.com?alertEventId=e3030d56-95ed-41a9-b092-a165f545f22d51443865410&documentId=EC-1000000-222857&source=email_alert&category=main_doc> 	
NVDA  •  Former  •  Expert Insight  •  2 pages  •  30 Jun 2026 	
Call Summary 

1.	The conversation covered trends and challenges in physical AI and robotics, including data and model strategies, hardware and sensor considerations, and the competitive landscape among U.S., Chinese, and other global players. The expert discussed timelines for deployment, key bottlenecks, and the roles of major companies and suppliers in the evolving ecosystem.
2.	Former Distinguished Research Scientist with deep experience in physical AI, robotics, and model/data development, particularly at a leading global technology company.
3.	The expert believes the physical AI space is still in early stages, with significant technical challenges remaining before large-scale deployment is possible.
4.	They are cautiously optimistic about progress in the next 3-5 years for non-humanoid robots, but see humanoid deployment as taking longer due to hardware and generalization challenges.
5.	The expert sees the integrator or platform provider as potentially having the strongest moat in the future, but notes it is too early to be certain.
6.	Physical AI development is advancing along both data (egocentric, UMI, teleop) and model (VLA, world model) axes, with no clear winner yet among approaches.
7.	World models offer more generalization but struggle with complex, dexterous, or long-horizon tasks, while VLA models are more robust for specific applications.
8.	NVIDIA is heavily invested in egocentric data and world models, collaborating with various partners and benefiting from industry-wide adoption of its chips.
9.	Chinese companies are catching up quickly in robotics, especially in hardware and data collection, but U.S. companies currently lead in intelligence and model sophistication.
10.	The main bottlenecks to a 'ChatGPT moment' for robotics are generalization and robustness, with data quality and model co-development being critical.
11.	Deployment of wheel-based robots with grippers is expected within 12-18 months, while humanoid robots will take longer to scale due to hardware and reliability issues.

Call Summary 

1.	The conversation covered trends and challenges in AI server manufacturing, supply chain dynamics, and the evolving influence of hyperscalers and vendors. It also addressed emerging technologies such as co-packaged optics and liquid cooling, and their potential future impact on the ecosystem.
2.	Senior manager with approximately seven years of experience in server industry, specializing in new product introduction (NPI) and product operations for rack-scale AI systems, interfacing with OEMs, ODMs, and hyperscalers.
3.	The expert sees the current environment as highly dynamic, with rapid acceleration in technology deployment and significant supply chain challenges, but expects constraints to ease and capacity to ramp up significantly in the near term.
4.	They believe that while hyperscalers' bargaining power has diminished somewhat due to new technology demands, vendors like NVIDIA currently hold significant influence, though this may rebalance as competitors mature.
5.	Speed to market is the primary challenge, with compressed timelines putting strain on design, supply chain, and manufacturing processes.
6.	Supply chain shortages persist, especially in memory, storage, power infrastructure, and cables, but are expected to ease as investments and yields improve.
7.	There is no significant shift in manufacturing location or EMS/ODM usage, though some consolidation among ODMs may occur based on capability.
8.	NVIDIA currently dominates the GPU market with strong vendor relationships and early technology investments, but competitors are catching up, potentially leading to more balanced competition in the future.

Market Summary

• Markets: Global equities are rebounding strongly into quarter-end, led by a recovery in mega-cap technology after recent underperformance. Technical indicators suggest large-cap technology has stabilized while broader market leadership continues to rotate.

• AI Investment: Investor focus remains firmly on AI, with enthusiasm shifting from cloud-only infrastructure toward on-device AI capabilities. Advances in local AI processing (privacy, routing, summarization) could reduce reliance on hyperscale computing while creating new opportunities across the AI ecosystem.

• Semiconductors: AI-driven demand continues to support memory, advanced packaging, and semiconductor supply chains. Positive pricing trends, tight HBM supply, and increased investment plans across Asia remain supportive for the sector.

• Telecommunications: Satellite-based connectivity is emerging as a competitive threat to traditional wireless operators following new strategic partnerships and spectrum-related acquisitions. Companies with valuable satellite spectrum assets are increasingly viewed as strategic beneficiaries.

• Technology Positioning: Hedge funds continued reducing exposure to mega-cap technology even as software fundamentals remain resilient, suggesting recent weakness has been driven more by positioning than deteriorating fundamentals.

• Market Positioning: U.S. equity inflows remain exceptionally strong despite elevated valuations. Overall positioning has moderated toward neutral, although investor sentiment remains optimistic and leverage in certain areas remains elevated.

• Volatility & Risk: Options markets indicate increased demand for downside protection, with negative market gamma suggesting heightened volatility potential. Record financing costs and concentrated positioning warrant caution despite constructive market momentum.

• Regional Themes: Japan: AI-related investment continues to support growth, while persistent yen weakness reflects limited policy intervention; China: Policy remains focused on manufacturing and AI rather than consumer demand, favoring semiconductors while keeping consumer-linked sectors under pressure.

• Sector Outlook: Software, semiconductors, transportation, financials, and AI infrastructure remain key leadership areas, while telecommunications face competitive disruption and energy has experienced notable fund outflows.

• Near-Term Outlook: As markets enter Q3, attention shifts to earnings season. Seasonal trends, continued AI investment, and resilient economic expectations support a constructive near-term outlook, although elevated expectations, crowded positioning, and market concentration argue for selective risk management.

 

Market Positioning

• U.S. equity fund inflows remain exceptionally strong.

• Hedge funds continued reducing exposure to mega-cap technology while maintaining broader technology exposure.

• Overall equity positioning has moderated toward neutral.

• Investor sentiment remains optimistic despite recent volatility.

 

Flows & Technicals

• Strongest quarterly performance for the S&P 500 in six years.

• Market breadth has improved beneath the surface despite narrow leadership.

• Historically, strong Q2 gains have often been followed by positive second-half performance.

• Hyperscalers have underperformed recently, increasing the probability of catch-up performance if earnings remain supportive.

 

Risk Factors

• Elevated market concentration remains a structural concern.

• Negative market gamma and higher put activity point to increased volatility risk.

• Record financing costs and leveraged positioning increase market fragility.

• AI spending expectations remain elevated, leaving limited room for disappointment during earnings season.

 

Key Themes to Watch

• Q2 earnings and AI spending commentary.

• Hyperscaler capital expenditure outlook.

• Semiconductor pricing and memory supply dynamics.

• Satellite disruption in telec

DATE: 2026-06-30 09:01:05 | SENDER: Farid, Marcio A [GIR] <marcio.farid@alerts.publishing.gs.com> | SUBJECT: GS on China: What do local clients think about the economy? Local marketing takeaways, June 2026
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Good morning, 

  

GS China Economics team met with onshore clients in Beijing and Shanghai over the past week, with the following overall feedback: 1) local clients appeared more cautious on China’s near-term growth momentum, 2) Policy easing expectations also remain subdued, 3)  Discussions also focused on fragile consumer confidence, mixed local government incentives to expand investment, implementation risks around the new cross-border investment rules; and the AI capex outlook. 

  

*	* More cautious on near-term growth momentum: absent more visible policy easing, they worry GDP growth could slow to below 4.5% yoy in coming quarters.  

*	* Weaker April <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQLefwCWZGyat30xtFRiAnhtUFQmoRCHdJg7-1l7_KqvP8x_MvBJAADAFHS8nLL4uHrXWF0IWqfBK4ZvRUboCp3wLOuf-gL_3A599SPrxWsIRB9RWLo3Mbg-BhDm-tRECl6nembF5UbHohO-F8y4n87cXqLJwkkbpWUE7TBDG5JcgScN6Gt9ET9n4qVlk4-Vyj68j2Sk9V8UoVCTfOmc2H7TfdywploIjPgnXa0elFuyN5uzms0bNkWBt__Yw1DISv-S6qANLUS6IVsmde9ITGz1Vm7-21aX1zvvrhrhdd4UBQkFZw9Ka1w1%26id=d5344981-dd95-4589-97bc-2ed7ba44f145%26utm_medium=sm/1/0100019f18673a15-dd932575-412a-4ffd-ae68-fe0aa5180c3c-000000/YVoHRK95Q_Jv929qt46lgdGyfieO6feWM_hLZIzbMx8=452> -May <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQKVUafMuFa8cOhckv-8aqW9w15WyhD6yn8eLxOqr4NgabWjPaUPAADAQVV36dOqgw4-EoK0px65Ufa1GOB6y7gU4SOFIDeTPNtK1Yb4DXNknjm7Msc_acFz8fn7-poDbhYATXR1QGT1mOQAo_nl6WaHkcpI__ZeSgw-W2z8TiRJyKb0psuQnroaP1oFSm65jmh1jLulPP6JTD637pFSfe8-gFvrhPZhj0Ia9ug2OZhOTY7fZem1-yJZAq-3e0xmx4v2Hlyy5fSErH829GE6PdbYVHcZNwHsCbJXfkHjp2Mpu3yD3pddTR50%26id=ea7a03d8-f960-4bc1-9770-73814b4e5507%26utm_medium=sm/1/0100019f18673a15-dd932575-412a-4ffd-ae68-fe0aa5180c3c-000000/-24BaIr2p10nIs1VoQLNrGfdOECv9YH3F0EySi8we94=452>  activity data have left onshore investors more cautious on China’s near-term macro outlook. 
*	* Exports continue to support headline activity, but domestic demand has softened notably (moreover, the boost from exports has not translated into a stronger labor market or meaningful profit improvement, limiting the pass-through from external demand to domestic growth). 
*	* Some investors noted that real export growth slowed to 4.5% yoy in April-May from 15.2% yoy in Q1 <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQKIGYif95uLYfnVJBVw5yNxVnwdmhAnPwhYmobslSpA1de2jri7AADAXNnZorwJS5StRo94Nl4dO5VeY03i73DAlEWnS7BNGU6vr3nRsQJDbkXItpk5NMyIx-zNl3L_1xgmffw_p7JzRbXNjDf-DQpPwhb-N74icGuJ7o7J3f6w2sCzu6DeTmPwKnncv1-mhTHi95qDuv6M-Z0KtTqJwtGmortZmnevCaoeJwTqUtZenAWu89hCflInrfnqgTWdS4gjeDIRdZ7Bw7xU3h2J1Yiv4RgmpsddNXzQE1p_B6728P4EzwEoi4qk%26id=414d0c8f-c01f-4d36-9d48-ef7e22f7608a%26utm_medium=sm/1/0100019f18673a15-dd932575-412a-4ffd-ae68-fe0aa5180c3c-000000/aWK0xLx0v7wbh9hD-HXWngD8FFj3y-O2aLRr-t6frNI=452> ; absent more visible policy easing, they worry GDP growth could slow to below 4.5% yoy in coming quarters.

SCHILSKY’S SNAPSHOT 


- Why Internet Stocks Can’t Work: Internet investor sentiment is currently as low as I’ve seen it in over the past four years. Consistently, I hear from investors that ‘XYZ stock can’t work because…’ without any related discussion of what could make the stocks work. As a result, I’ve decided to compile the most commonly cited reasons I’ve heard as to why Internet stocks can’t work. In theory, if any of these overhangs start to lift, these stocks may begin to work. In theory… I go stock-by-stock below. Please tell me what you think. 

- UBER-Waymo Rides No Longer Available in Phoenix (re: GOOGL): Is this the beginning of the end of the UBER-Waymo partnership <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13510952&ad=4535072418&h=se56vvs&sig=UFeBFEnlyyrlF61c7usC2TDktWb&v=2&url=https://waymo.com/blog/2023/10/the-waymo-driver-now-available-on-uber-in-phoenix/> ? A one-off? Something else? UBER IR confirmed the Waymo-Phoenix news in an email to me: “We can confirm that we have elected to terminate the Phoenix pilot as it has reached the natural end state…” TechCrunch <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13510952&ad=4535072418&h=xeE-TS-&sig=NJg75guGdDX66EdcEwlQAwDi6BI&v=2&url=https://techcrunch.com/2026/06/29/waymo-and-uber-quietly-part-ways-in-phoenix/?secureweb%3Dbplus64> verified my reporting – and augmented it: “Uber said it is readying the launch of a separate autonomous vehicle partnership in the city, but did not name the partner.” UBER traded down -1% yesterday. 

- CMCSA Spin Off: Right Move, Surprising Timing: From Sebastiano’s CMCSA Spin Off: Right Move, Surprising Timing <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13510952&ad=4535072418&h=00rX1wn&sig=W4a69mS7O8kxoRHS9VLH0Y7L5og&v=2&isig=VZjUEfjpxZ81YPTTjzbB8rNyc3o&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/ltaord5b/GPS-5351318-0/00a3f86f-0bfa-452c-9a9c-a6043f79d7c2> : “Agree with the outcome, somewhat surprised by the timing…Increased odds of cable M&A over the long term. Separating content from connectivity raises the odds of cable M&A longer term, in our view. Given competitive pressures from fiber, fixed wireless access (FWA), and LEO satellite broadband, we expect cable to continue consolidating from here.” Reuters <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13510952&ad=4535072418&h=OxHqqSL&sig=ElFR8pvPzAQHuoFaJi0YwwwIZFZ&v=2&url=https://www.reuters.com/world/nbcuniversal-may-enter-video-game-business-after-comcast-split-sources-say-2026-06-29/> reported: “NBCUniversal is eyeing opportunities in digital gaming and new entertainment franchises…” RBLX? NEWS – DESK COLOR – RESEARCH HIGHLIGHTS 


Why Internet Stocks Can’t Work: 


Internet investor sentiment is currently as low as I’ve seen it in over the past four years. Consistently, I hear from investors that ‘XYZ stock can’t work because…’ without any related discussion of what could make the stocks work. As a result, I’ve decided to compile the most commonly cited reasons I’ve heard as to why Internet stocks can’t work. In theory, if any of these overhangs start to lift, these stocks may begin to work. In theory… 

*	META: ROIC on Zuckerberg’s Superintelligence Lab spend is currently highly negative. Without any new products and/or model releases, investors do not yet know if META’s AI efforts will lead to a product cycle that looks like Reels – or one that looks like the Metaverse. Plus, there remains a significant equity issuance overhang post-GOOGL. 
*	AMZN: Take your pick of possible overhangs: a potentially weakening US consumer, 2026/2027 Capex estimates going much higher (driven materially by higher component pricing), increasing competition amongst hyperscalers and neoclouds, a desire to compete in space via Leo, a potential equity issuance, etc. AMZN remains the most frustrating Internet stock for the most investors. 
*	GOOGL: Post-equity issuance, investors have ratcheted expectations for FY27 Capex estimates mean

Pre-Market News.

 

AI + Jobs: The FT notes that companies investing most heavily in AI are adding workers faster than their peers, according to new research that challenges predictions of broad AI-driven job losses. White-collar worker #’s increased ~10% overall at companies that used AI most intensely in the first two years after they first adopted the technology, the research found, with gains across occupation types and seniority levels.

 



 

CMCSA: Reuters noted <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511019&ad=4535116764&h=OxHqqSL&sig=EocAa41Dd0Pltf4nJO1xE729vGE&v=2&url=https://www.reuters.com/world/nbcuniversal-may-enter-video-game-business-after-comcast-split-sources-say-2026-06-29/>  last night that NBCUniversal is considering gaming and entertainment franchises for growth after the split. The cable and connectivity business, meanwhile, is ripe for technological investments ‌that could take advantage of the massive surge in data centers and AI.

 

CNXC: A small call center business that’s likely off the radar for most, but continues the IT Services and Contact Center pain that we’ve continued to see. Down ~25% in the pre-market following a Q2 revenue, EBITDA, and operating income misses, guides below the Streets for Q3, and cuts across the board.

 

“We are definitely seeing increased financial pressure on our clients as they try and cope with their own investment needs and their current operating environments. This has created demand for more of our automation solutions, but also increased the urgency of moving work offshore and caused certain clients to prioritize spend across their client base, resulting in reduced spend overall.”

 

NVDA: SA notes <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511019&ad=4535116764&h=tUHziHY&sig=IzRCn95O9bO3NIrWgIAiFAvLnL0&v=2&url=https://x.com/SemiAnalysis_/status/2071840399627288746>  that their accelerator model estimate has NVDA DC compute revenue ~20% higher compared to consensus expectations for 2H FY’27. Rubin will have a big ramp after being pushed out due to earlier HBM4 issues that are now resolved and front end wafer supply is now built up.

 



 

TMUS: The German business outlet Handelsblatt noted <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511019&ad=4535116764&h=HF5Hgqp&sig=EQ3X68SaDTrd9xCQxti4A7i42ZJ&v=2&url=https://www.handelsblatt.com/technik/it-internet/fusion-telekom-forciert-plaene-fuer-mega-holding-elon-musk-als-treiber/100236142.html>  last night according to insiders, Deutsche Telekom CEO is pushing ahead with the merger with its US subsidiary TMUS. Insiders tell Handelsblatt that one plan being considered would see a holding company headquartered in Ireland or Switzerland, while other sources tell Handelsblatt that regardless, Bonn, Germany, will remain the company's operational center. The insiders tell Handelsblatt that the plans are being spurred by the possibility -- seemingly raised by an analyst, that SPCX might target T-Mobile US.

 

xAI: Last night announced <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511019&ad=4535116764&h=5C8RZkF&sig=4n8Vw85mpTQxFqaokCzjyLxRCqq&v=2&url=https://docs.x.com/tools/mcp>  the hosted X MCP server, giving AI agents like Grok and Cursor instant, no-configuration access to real-time data from the X platform.

 

- - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - -

Thoughts on Yesterday / Discussions. 

 

A lot of head scratching moves yesterday to say the least … all of which were accompanies by a lack of true answers or what feels like really big stretches.

 

A few notables that received a lot of inbounds in terms of the magnitude vs. the direction … PANW having an EPS level move and making continued fresh ATHs | the rip in Semicaps (albeit folks not complaining), following an investment # from SK Hynix and Samsung that felt in-line with Friday’s chatter | the move in ALGM | the squeeze in RBLX following better platform CCU data from Animal Hospital … ev

DAILY STRATEGY: Main Point – High vol and high correlations create an opportunity to hedge the Price Momentum factor via single-name options. YTD AI Winners have witnessed increasingly negative sensitivity to financial conditions. Those AI baskets have significant downside risk if financial conditions tighten. The 2yr yield breaking above 4.2%, which would be associated with core inflation coming in too high (above 0.21% MoM) would be negative for YTD AI thematic basket winners. Mag 7 relative performance is negatively correlated with Semis. Long Mag 7 is a way to hedge against downside risk in Semis, AI thematic basket winners and Price Momentum. The Morgan Stanely (MS) Broad AI index (+73% absolute YTD) has witnessed an increasingly negative beta to financial conditions recently. The negative beta to financial conditions has moved toward extreme levels relative to history for the MS Broad AI basket. The negative sensitivity to financial conditions has become most intense since investors started to shift away from pricing in an easing bias from the Fed ~2 months ago. That is when 2yr yields started to reprice higher. The same dynamic holds true for the MS Global CPU basket (+165% absolute YTD), and the MS Global Memory baskets (358% absolute YTD). Charts below.

DATE: 2026-06-30 09:16:35 | SENDER: Joshua Meyers - Specialist Sales - US TMT <joshua.meyers@jpmorgan.com> | SUBJECT: JPM: Chips for Breakfast - GLW Thoughts, Korea AI Mega Plan, Japan Components
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
GLW Thoughts, Korea AI Mega Plan, Japan Components 


Joshua Meyers 
+1 617 310 0767 
joshua.meyers@jpmorgan.com <mailto:joshua.meyers@jpmorgan.com>  

  


Some quick thoughts on Korea from trading…KOSPI closed +1% to 8,476.48, trading higher for the first time in three days despite another volatile session on the final day of the month and quarter. The index whipsawed between a strong intraday advance and sharp weakness before finishing firmly in positive territory. Foreigners extended their cash selling streak to eight consecutive sessions, while local institutions and retail investors continued to absorb supply. Tech (+2%) outperformed as investors continued to position around Korea's AI investment initiatives, with semiconductor equipment and front-end wafer-fab-exposure names remaining preferred beneficiaries. And early thoughts on the US market from JPM Market Intelligence Head Drew Tyler…Futs are a touch above unchanged following yesterday’s rally, with markets behaving as though period-end dynamics have now completed. With the major US holiday coming up, keep an eye on low liquidity moves in the region. Bond yields are flat to down 1bp with the curve flattening. USD is stronger, looking erase all of yesterday’s losses. Cmdtys are stronger with crude flat into today’s US / Iran discussions, Metals seeing a bid, and Ags outperforming the other cmdty complexes. In Eqys, Semis are mixed, Mag7 are flat, Cyclicals are generally leading Defensives with exceptions being Energy (lower) and Healthcare (higher). Today’s macro data focus is on JOLTS 

 


Expectations for the coming few quiet weeks: Warsh’s appears tomorrow at the ECB Sintra conf. We also get US manufacturing ISM @ 10am, and on Thursday at 8:30am the US jobs report. On Monday we get US services ISM at 10am, and on Wed 7/8 the FOMC meeting notes, then US CPI at 8:30am on July 14. Then earnings… should be an interesting earnings season after the more conservative “wartime guides” of 1Q… I’ll be marketing in Chicago on July 8 and in Toronto on July 9, and with Harlan in New York on July 13~14; let me know if you want to try and meet! 

 


Just quickly on the +41% 1MO GLW move (the stock is up 24% just this week), a lot of folks yesterday were insinuating that announcement of the GlassWorks AI Platform and in particular of Glass Bridge were principally responsible for the most recent move. I got a lot of TAM questions. The move is puzzling to us from a fundamental standpoint, in part because this product was announced none months ago and demonstrated at ECOC. Joe doesn’t presently see any reason to view it as incremental to the $10b photonics MAP by 2030. We would love to hear where people disagree.

Key Highlights 



Memory Market Update: Korea's AI Mega-investment Plan A Near-term Overhang, but Bullish Long-term. Here <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511082&ad=4535144709&h=6hCTWLN&sig=ECsXwJQO0tVBvSnzoY8pRw4dFQV&v=2&isig=8F7OIwO6gSfoia1a0pV9wlWjMur&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/-2r0cjdm/GPS-5350909-0.pdf/da2444a2-e834-4dac-ad94-f2ae91621ce3>  
Jay Kwon recaps Korea's national AI investment briefing, where Samsung Group and SK Group jointly announced KRW4,755t (~US$3.1t) in long-term capex through 2040, in service of the government’s tripartite pan for semiconductors, AI datacenters, and robotics. The scale implies doubling current installed DRAM capacity within 5 years, pulling in the Yongyin fab ramp by 7~12 years, developing the Chungcheong region and facilitating a huge longer-term investment roadmap. Jay reads the chairmen's messaging as a decisive signal to debottleneck supply shortages, with memory execs explicitly flagging that supply is only ~50% of demand and worsening — underpinning a multi-year upcycle thesis that's positive for SPE, power infrastructure, and semi EPC names. On the negative side, the Apple-MU pricing dispute is crystallizing market anxiety around unsustainable profit-sharing dynamics, and a consumer class-action lawsuit has been filed in the US against the three major DRAM makers for alleged price-fixing — while no government investigation is involved yet, Jay flags this warrants close monitoring given the early-2000s DRAM cartel precedent. Jay expects AI/server-centric demand bipolarization to continue into 2H26-27, with LPDDR pricing remaining favorable, and sees the US$3t investment ultimately generating US$12-20t in cumulative revenue opportunity for Korean memory makers.

This material is a product of Jefferies Equity Sales and Trading Department. It is not a product of Jefferies Research Department, and it should not be regarded as research or a research report. Refer to additional disclaimers at the end of this email

FDS expectations into tomorrow

*	ASV vs Margin focus? ---- Buyside survey response focused on ASV over margins ------ surprised us a bit in that a little ASV upside feels like a base case vs margins are the delta (the lever or the problem)
*	So does an ASV beat (+4Q reiteration) and in-line margins win the day? --- the buyside bias was a clear yes VS the Desk sees the incremental negative operating leverage as a potential drag on the stock, #s, thesis…

 

 

As a segue to the broader discussion…..

 

The following chart feels like the best representation of Cap Markets investing over the past 2 months, and more specifically, 2 weeks…

…While its not exactly clear what kicked this dispersion off in late May…

…The past 2 weeks is undoubtedly technical --- most acutely attributable to the Exchange space as patient 0

Incredible - In the past 9 Trading sessions, TROW has outperformed BLK by 16%....



 

One more for good measure 

…since APO announced ADS 2Q redemptions less than 1 week ago….

…(results of which we viewed as in-line/to only slightly worse than peers – met with modest pushback in ADS’ self-described relative software immunity)

Incredible – in the past 5 Trading sessions, CRBG has outperformed APO by 12% 



 

So – what exactly is going on here??

…As a starting point – I think there is more capital that has been deployed in Cap Markets than ever before 

*	Outsized dispersion = a source of real alpha generation – both on an absolute basis and especially relative to other Sub-Sectors in recent years
*	Strong trends = a proxy for market strength, an access point to unthinkable capital issuance needs (AI….) and also the broader proliferation by end user (retail), geography (globalization), and product type (from electronification, to alts, to now perps)
*	Re-Rate potential = a trendline that has gone from cyclical to structural – with winners surprisingly capable of busting through presumed multiple caps
*	AI winner potential = from AI enhanced expense leverage to AI related capital formation benefits to other benefits of scale, insulated market/product/distribution moats and less traditional disintermediation risk 

…As a second step – the ‘AI Effect’ itself

*	A) the crowding effect related to our starting point assumption of AI risk vs AI immunity --- impossible to defend the former in the first inning of the cycle – and so positioning understandably gets exaggerated
*	B) then our generic ‘understanding’ of AI risk morphs into stuff we hadn’t really considered; from the 10k foot Citrini report to the monetary risk of tokenmaxxing to the great cash optimization debate, agentic effects, means of distribution, etc etc

…To part 3 – which is where we are now

*	Where AI is as much real as it is representation of emerging technological change and structural risk ---- that once again, has proven impossible to refute
*	We get the headline catalyst ---- we watch and we debate --- then we defend with a rational perspective on the logic of foreseeable business risk 
*	Until we then grapple with the ‘what if’, ‘too hard to disprove’ phenomenon that plays out wayyyyy beyond the actual question at hand. Ie the realistic efficacy of perps = having such a massive 4th derivative effect on APO, BLK etc etc

RESEARCH:

SNDK <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511305&ad=4535204566&h=ZwlG6rs&sig=EojDeLWiUY1Xry9OxuJu3BYF5H7&v=2&url=https://www.bernsteinresearch.com/brweb/ViewResearchStreamer.aspx?cid%3DR%25252fr0a9rCzwWNeN67TP0wakZrkzr8BYeyH1OgqX7LLBmTcuRTu%25252b0Mo9QhYeKD0sc%25252f>  - Mark Newman raises SNDK PT to $3000 (vs. $1,700 prior), FY27E EPS now at $243 (+28% vs cons), new LTAs provide structural lift. The debate has centered on whether LTAs can structurally reduce NAND cyclicality and support a higher earnings multiple. Mark believes these LTAs are fundamentally different from prior cycles given multi-year duration (3-5 years), price floors, and upfront customer financial commitments that provide increasing downside protection over time. His base case calls for FY27/FY28 EPS of $243/$272, or roughly 28%/27% above Street, while his bull case reaches $350/$400, or 84-87% vs cons. He applies an 11x FY28 EPS and 14x through-cycle earnings, which equates to a 7.5x bull case FY28 EPS. Mark runs a 72% peak to trough ASP decline through his numbers with new LTA assumptions, gets to $214 in FY30E EPS, showing significant downside protection vs older LTA structures. A business with higher growth visibility and cyclicality that has been minimized deserves to trade at a more premium multiple in his view. Mark rates SNDK outperform with a $3,000 PT. 

 

Energy & Transition <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13511305&ad=4535204566&h=l3po4V1&sig=VYUkThviUPsCYoPApdCjrK1kG2k&v=2&url=https://www.bernsteinresearch.com/brweb/ViewResearchStreamer.aspx?cid%3DPWePlT3416092L770odbdm6ncxpspuiy3yyyxutd7blt23rv44lupdj34qsz2ikeqceigxpbmbpfgzeqe4roaipg3inf4u1%26amp;pn%3Dpn%26amp;ct%3DR%26amp;downloadid%3DHUPXKQANL7BH665N0A1WNDNRIENWEI%26amp;h%3D1%26amp;f%3D1%26amp>  – Sunaina Ocalan thinks Virtual Power Plants could great opptys for ENPH and GEV. Sunaina dives into Virtual Power Plants (VPP) and discusses the potential opportunities they can create for ENPH & GEV. Recently, Sunrun, Tesla, and Renew Home announced a framework agreement to deliver up to 6.8 gigawatts (GW) of flexible energy capacity to hyperscalers and utilities. These offerings come from VPPs, which aggregate distributed energy resources (i.e., rooftop solar, EV chargers, and smart thermostats) and act as a flexible energy resource. Since most distributed energy resources are small, many do not meet the size and reliability required to participate in the grid. FERC Order No. 2222 (issued in September 2020) aims to ease and standardize rules around DER and VPP participation in regional energy markets. Sunaina believes that the implementation of this order can support the continued growth and integration of VPPs into U.S. electricity markets, creating opportunity for Enphase’s product offering as well as for GEV’s electrification business.

Former Director at AMD Views TSMC's CoWoS as Leading Advanced Packaging Technology Over Intel's EMIB <https://research.alpha-sense.com?alertEventId=63c90904-850c-4707-bbbe-ec56f6b6371021443916500&documentId=EC-1000000-223106&source=email_alert&category=main_doc> 	
TSM  •  Customer  •  Expert Insight  •  2 pages  •  30 Jun 2026 	
Call Summary 

1.	The conversation explored the dynamics of advanced semiconductor packaging vendor selection, focusing on the technical, operational, and strategic considerations between leading packaging technologies. It covered the evaluation of TSMC's CoWoS versus Intel's EMIB, qualification processes, switching costs, and the durability of TSMC's competitive position.
2.	Former director with over six years of experience at a leading semiconductor company, focused on AI infrastructure, server-class silicon validation, competitive analysis, and hyperscale platforms, with direct involvement in technical and platform strategy discussions related to advanced packaging supplier evaluation.
3.	The expert views TSMC's CoWoS as the gold standard in advanced packaging, with unmatched reliability, performance, and partnership, making it difficult for competitors to displace in the near to medium term.
4.	The expert is skeptical about Intel's ability to compete at scale in advanced packaging until it can attract significant external customer volume and demonstrate proven success with its latest technology nodes.
5.	Switching advanced packaging suppliers is seen as a complex, costly, and underestimated process, particularly due to the extensive re-qualification required.
6.	TSMC's CoWoS packaging technology is considered highly innovative and reliable, with no real competitor for high-end AI and HPC chips during the expert's tenure.
7.	Performance, reliability, and close partnership were the primary criteria for packaging vendor selection, with cost being a minor factor due to its small share of total system cost.
8.	Intel's EMIB was not seriously considered due to competitive conflicts and perceived technical and manufacturing risks; cost advantages were not compelling enough to offset these concerns.
9.	Switching packaging suppliers involves significant silicon redesign and a lengthy re-qualification process, often underestimated by outsiders and requiring months of engineering effort.
10.	TSMC's dominant position is reinforced by massive capital investment, technological leadership, and a non-competitive stance with its customers, making its moat difficult to erode in the next 5-10 years.

Market Intelligence: US Morning Update 
	
30 June 2026 | 8:42AM EDT | Research | Equity 	
	
	
Click "here <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2Fcontent%2Fproducts%2Fd036cb0f-b058-490d-9e12-e7b8862ebdfd.html/1/0100019f1891ee82-5f312a33-e993-479d-b6b4-a482e655c732-000000/2PoCMQQxEgmiKy9MDBWhsqtQfRegnyCiytthq0dpTCU=452> " to listen to the US Morning Call.

Stocks in Asia were mostly higher on Tuesday, except in Hong Kong where weakness in internet stocks persisted. However, tech-oriented Japan, Korea and Taiwan posted gains on positive cues from US markets. Sentiment in China was also bolstered by an increase in official manufacturing and non-manufacturing PMIs (see "China: Both official manufacturing and non-manufacturing PMIs rose in June <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQIJzz0sZ6qv1m_lJsncj2YgD8IGcxAK-gTJdI2QGZ2KG0rHg2i1AACwN7kHw7y_DVDYySqugiaAffaRHJALdA2F5b0xlVxETQlmbgQh79I3hYWPNHZcAPTnvJv9MsuKPDsBxIVZ9OE_Etz-0-msUSiL8s3N-bYKsxjNN-wvX3uOpifJ9DW6oJdHacfox0xY135pHnfMgpeItduX0Zi_mLF_6UCdLi9rM_Ttlv_GWTrrr5qcZcajwdOz2IVouBSKY3YUtbYEUfaMbj1m16GARz7vKMq0vhMoCAY*%26id=863ea4d5-ab92-47d7-8881-684744d229f6%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1891ee82-5f312a33-e993-479d-b6b4-a482e655c732-000000/CgFW0LeZlmDZLBHYCSl3GPO9snhmgTrhdBoCccRskO8=452> "). In Japan, industrial production rose for a second consecutive month (see "Japan: May Production Rises for Second Straight Month, In Line With Market Forecast <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQJvtrRJ0votW1t3GoU6-EZH-A79uxATBTBoE-Bmdnn57lMauVLuAACwkYZJ9xh_Q1sAWtDo5xjMHSc9qblQEK2zim4N1KO_im8vIT1c7-F6I-sMYkWR_20PRcZFu87tCTZudYo-BeVBeqI_3zzOivxkjoN3etLKo-rTSir4zahhOXGhMnTcpYzTsr1ayo5-a2K8T8zOT5Re6NdizawyHv56V3lJgAnqdlHTFaXtKvU1D2CmjiNAajJOmIBqrpbtDq7h1iJYBcmyBcRhVB66EuonNsby5G5jadA*%26id=d9362d8d-e88c-4096-a4f8-29a5e4d0b141%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1891ee82-5f312a33-e993-479d-b6b4-a482e655c732-000000/vwhB2w0xjc1oLkaK58oTMHhUQEh0e2cGgQx4_M2Px3U=452> '), while it declined in Korea, alongside weak consumption and mixed investment data (see "South Korea: A Surprise Contraction in IP, Weak Consumption, and Mixed Investment in May <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQKOgvoNYh1rga-BsSoTe1SnSIfXYxDJVC-vx3lKQGhRhDZ7OWaYAACwwwhBRaM5FpJKE8CDrbvZCSSxrysXzui24JVnZSTLwP8LLQyMQopKv_WRr3JSFh2wtLgw9-who4DSoJQgP-bPaoF2JrdLGajHfz6oycVgIe7KpRGS7epMQGmUf3v7WVHqQgIXvog0Be6LOWwx5Vug6_j5WSRv0Bz7bqgW6aY7Afk6bW7EN-wa95G6SNyeNi3uvCfW9c-f2ulSaAB69u0agYgk3swLa6UCsxk8xd93UHM*%26id=63346bed-22b3-48c9-ab78-1f0fd77a35c4%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1891ee82-5f312a33-e993-479d-b6b4-a482e655c732-000000/MhV3GBeH2P62VRdJD58XQw-ZKcr52RmRg_xdMqfst4E=452> "). 

European equities are also trading higher amid tech strength and weaker-than-expected inflation in France. Our economists nudged down Euro area headline and core inflation forecasts (see "Euro Area: French Inflation Below Expectations; Revising Down Our Area-Wide Tracking <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQKTIC-rzp7LUStIIqTCkH0V8LsOLhBOHZDpsPlLip8oA_3R1DmNAACwkCdhmoBYVqEnjqqmqMDH7Avw7-mHVGVTGSIt2FDuh9Auq2Mj1ORf2JK3YIVOewlRcjf-YyqFhXkWsAvx2tNyHS-COrBHQHYh-vWTfCjXFW-SQLaZG8a6iq3zhKgJy9LUtlih5aAvy1Cs19jhyqm1eKN0h7gg6fHEljrOi2Kc7W96-Wl6OKiIMChQ8IN-KQC3-6rDy1MfcLY-MLCPVka9E-M33llPo4UFosFhryhy-7g*%26id=0bb03342-8eec-490a-b868-256158c8253c%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1891ee82-5f312a33-e993-479d-b6b4-a482e655c732-000000/WCzlRBUHMvnRBvgXOlyzYb-vSpXm5d-KHw0Jdr4eiOg=452> "). They continue to expect the ECB to hike in September, but note that the hurdle for a hold is now low given reduced inflationary pressures from energy prices (see Jari Stehn's "ECB—Hike or Hold? <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQJXnMCQSKHIcQuMK5gU7XM4KTe6TRAtdQpu6gAti57zNAPXXh92AACwlaYm0CLUn5E3hF7lMae_vFhIMJdyOkFxKgdVrtrNAVKnFPe1nLsZnargNzUdBHkFr2sN6m3xWqEU9trx2g41y09mQiptUPkYthruNKabUq-8sD8Y1ULyMsdKgTEvTMv4C_h5eAbeF6hQ7Mf_04-ko0W4y089oxzO4N8ZJVqRPCvaEeQBduDf3EUPFgzLHRB8rJKiA5DpQw0YE9qF0U1T_4gksNHvMBYQBddyn8XtiIM*%26id=7071bde2-6c4e-412b-af5e-de3b324c75ec%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1891ee82-5f312a33-e993-479d-b6b4-a482e655c732-000000/fc520HFcIOSehccQG5GO2BpVb5p6GmtaEZpgbD--zk8=452> "). 

Yields on 10-year US Treasuries remain anchored at 4.37%, while front month Brent oil edged up, but remains below $75/bbl amidst a swift ramp up in Hormuz flows (see "Oil Comment: Gulf Exports: 2 Steps Forward, 1 Step Back <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQK1hjFkZ7f2DGyBxAx53P1lc9YajhCzJ2HRQF14tkgIwmKAIAPpAACw-rtwHCX5xJugyRsiEeq7QjLt_6brxujKdFJjmSXrFdn_oeghOBTWuL5FdNjhocSwgPPCuQig_2yLIhGD

Research Updates:

AD AGENCIES: FIVE THEMES FROM CANNES <https://sales.cmail20.com/t/d-l-wluhhil-dyiuuktjju-k/>  - The Cannes Lions International Festival of Creativity took place last week, with 500 speakers sharing their views and visions for the future of the marketing industry. We highlight several themes that emerged from the presentations, with AI taking center stage in topics that spanned: humans vs machines, the two-audience problem and the merits of effectiveness vs efficiency. Meanwhile, the growing importance of Creators in marketing briefs was another salient theme, as was the evolving role of agencies in the age of AI. We elaborate on these topics in the short email linked below and present our analysis of the Cannes Lions Grand Prix winners by holding group. 

 

HONEYWELL TECHNOLOGIES: FAIRLY VALUED POST AEROSPACE SPIN <https://research.cmail19.com/t/d-l-wlukdhy-dhkkdhiliy-y/>  – On Monday, Honeywell completed the separation of its Aerospace business to leave the remaining company, Honeywell Technologies, as an automation pure play. In our in-depth report during May, we laid out pro forma medium-term estimates for Honeywell Technologies which were broadly consistent with the targets through FY29 that were subsequently provided by the company at its investor day on 11 June. In this note, we are establishing formal estimates for Honeywell Technologies that are not materially different from our pro forma framework. We are also establishing a DCF-based twelve-month price target of $214 which is consistent with our pro forma valuation. Given modest potential downside of 6% versus the current price we remain with a Neutral rating.

 

US MACRO: <https://sales.cmail20.com/t/d-l-wluhhil-dyiuuktjju-u/>  IS WARSH LOOKING TO EUROPE FOR INSPIRATION? <https://sales.cmail20.com/t/d-l-wluhhil-dyiuuktjju-u/>  - Kevin Warsh's new committee on the Fed's balance sheet is an opening to reassert what the Fed has spent a decade trying to separate: the link between the size and composition of the balance sheet and the level of interest rates. Europe has already shown how well a "demand-led floor" can work, and the Fed is quietly drifting that way — weekly Treasury buybacks, destigmatised repo, and a Treasury willing to put TGA cash to work have all cut the risk of fresh repo crises. But the more radical prize lies further north: Sweden's Riksbank still runs a "corridor" system, using liquidity-draining operations to hold overnight rates without remunerating every last reserve. If Warsh pushes the Fed down a similar path — active buybacks, reserve management purchases, open market operations and a shift toward an overnight repo rate as the signalling tool — the pay-off is a leaner balance sheet and scope to set short-term rates lower through the cycle. 

 

NORWEGIAN CRUISE: NEW CHIEF MARKETING OFFICER APPOINTED - NCLH has appointed Lee Applbaum as Chief Marketing Officer, effective July 6, 2026. Applbaum brings 25+ years building global consumer brands; he was global CMO at Patrón Spirits and Bacardi (Tequila Patrón and Grey Goose) and former CMO of Wheels Up. His focus at NCLH will be brand strategy, guest engagement and demand generation. The appointment fills a key seat in the senior-team rebuild under Chidsey, perhaps earlier than expected. However, for NCLH it is all down to execution which is still to be proven. We wrote about the opportunity at NCLH in our recent Hitchhiker's Guide, linked here. Trades on 9.7x 26E EV/EBITDA. Let us know if you would like to discuss Norwegian or cruise further.

 

UBER: PILOT WITH WAYMO IN PHOENIX ENDED – Waymo AVs are no longer available via the Uber app in Phoenix, vehicles will remain in use to make deliveries with DoorDash (Buy). Phoenix was Uber’s first pilot market with Waymo and was very limited in deployment (low teen number of AVs that were available on the Uber app versus Waymo having 500 AVs on its own app). As it stands the partnership between the two in both Austin and Atlanta still stand. Shouldn’t be a major surprise given most were not expecting this particular agreement to last very long given how small it was in scale, but may be considered blow to Uber’s position in the value chain so shares likely off this AM. Trades on 11x FY27 EV/EBITDA.

Evolving Use and Spending on Medicines in the U.S.
Navigating Patient Access Barriers and Cost Pressures
U.S. Medicine Use Trends 2026 webinar
Date: July 15, 2026
Time: 10 a.m. – 11:30 a.m. ET
REGISTER NOW <https://app.constellation.iqvia.com/e/er?utm_campaign=2026_UseofMedicines2026Webinar_INSTITUTE_SM&utm_medium=email&utm_source=Eloqua&s=460529241&lid=33799&elqTrackId=60EAB7980535F1581C2109FC3AF64D1E&elq=759e5e88eb064a2f8b200c7a9284d552&elqaid=31667&elqat=1&elqak=8AF5542D19FA358AB08935A86C758AAB0B20EA6AEC73DBEA98B1F9B602A4354AB561>  
The U.S. prescription medicine landscape is changing rapidly, shaped by rising use of innovative therapies, shifting vaccination trends, changing benefit designs and continued pressure on patient costs.

Join this webinar to explore the key trends defining medicine use and spending in 2025, including dynamics in obesity, immunology, oncology and other high-growth areas. The discussion will also examine access challenges and how policy may shape patient access, net spending and stakeholder decision-making over the next five years.

*	Amanda Frost, Vice President, Research, Pharmaceutical Care Management Association (PCMA)
*	Luke Greenwalt, Vice President, Thought Leadership & Innovation, IQVIA U.S.
*	John O’Brien, CEO, National Pharmaceutical Council

Asia Pacific 	
Industry View   Attractive

Tiffany Yeh, Charlie Chan, Daniel Yen, CFA, Daisy Dai, CFA, Lucas Wang, Ethan Jia & 1 more...	 
June 30, 2026

	
Key takeaways	 

*	Rising precious metal prices and a severe test pin capacity shortage point to likely price hikes for probe cards and test sockets, passing costs on to customers. 
*	Very strong June results look likely in view of probe card and test socket demand, driven by a robust AI/HPC ramp and incremental DDIC momentum. 

With precious metal prices continually rising and a severe shortage in test pin capacity, our supply chain checks suggest that probe card and test socket vendors are likely to raise prices, passing costs on to customers — similar to other segments in the semi industry.

Reiterate OW on MPI and WinWay: With capacity tight and new supply taking time to ramp, we believe probe card and test socket vendors have pricing power. We also think MPI and WinWay are likely to post very strong June results, driven by robust AI/HPC ramp and even DDICs.

MPI's share price has lagged amid weak CPO sentiment; however, we see no change in insertion test demand as optical engines remain necessary regardless of what new technology FAU is adopting. We view 43x 2027e EPS as an attractive entry point to capture the 105% 2025–2028e earnings CAGR.

WinWay should start fully ramping the new capacity to fulfill strong backlog starting in June. Valuation is 39x 2027e EPS vs. our 2025–2028 EPS CAGR projection at 111%. DATE: 2026-06-30 12:20:10 | SENDER: MNI <mktbrief@marketnews.com> | SUBJECT: MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Independence Still On Shaky Ground - Judge
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXZxukI6aJhchl1Hw~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CC8ehptJe2eJOIQ> 	 <https://emedia.marketnews.com/marketnewsintl/mni-pr-01-25.png?t=1> 	


MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Independence Still On Shaky Ground - Judge

By Evan Ryser
Jun 30, 2026


WASHINGTON - A pair of U.S. Supreme Court rulings Monday on the president's ability to fire officials at independent agencies do not guarantee future Federal Reserve independence and leave Governor Lisa Cook vulnerable to further attempts to remove her, Columbia Law School professor Kathryn Judge told MNI.

"The news is helpful in protecting Federal Reserve independence, but the decisions by no means guarantee ongoing independence, either as a legal matter or as a matter of democratic legitimacy," she said in an interview. 

Cook can remain in her job while her case challenging Trump’s attempt to fire her proceeds in district court, the Supreme Court said. That fight will take some time, and the justices left the door open for round two if the Trump administration wants to try again to get rid of Cook, Judge said. 

"There's a number of novel legal issues that are at play in the president's effort to fire Lisa Cook," she said. "There's no case law or precedent to look to." 

The court's other decision Monday in Trump v. Slaughter, allowing the president to fire officials at other independent agencies for any reason, "makes it all the more challenging by suggesting there are significant constitutional considerations, but also historical considerations that shape how cause should be understood."

The question of whether Trump could fire or demote Fed Chair Kevin Warsh remains unsettled, at a time when inflation is high yet the president is calling for rate cuts, Judge said. 

"One of the key issues that does remain open is whether Trump can demote a chair to becoming a pure governor, and there was nothing in today's opinions that resolved those issues, and if anything, the Slaughter case potentially makes it easier for a president to demote a chair."

CHANGING SURROUNDINGS

The Slaughter ruling gave the president sweeping new authority over approximately two dozen multi-member agencies that Congress intended to be independent, and leaves Fed independence on shakier ground than it has been in over 90 years, Judge said.

It wasn't until the court's 1935 decision in Humphrey’s Executor v. United States -- now overturned in Slaughter -- that Congress put in protections for Fed officials in the Banking Act of 1935. Previously, Congress had removed the "for cause" protection that members of the Fed board of governors enjoyed under the Federal Reserve Act because they didn't think it was constitutional. 

"The Fed really rose to independence alongside and in tandem with the rise of independent agencies generally," said Judge, who is working on a book about how the Banking Act of 1935 reformed the Federal Reserve System. 

"It's important not just as a legal matter, but as a matter of democratic legitimacy, for the public to believe, and for Congress to believe that there is a reason for the Fed to remain independent. The rationale of expertise and long-term decision making that the Fed has traditionally relied on is no longer going to suffice," Judge said. 

Champions of Fed independence should emphasize the Fed's unique structure to make a convincing argument, she said. 

"It's important to lean in to the distinct characteristics, and in particular the Fed's distinct decentralized structure, and the way that the reserve banks can promote accountability in helping the public to understand why the Fed deserves the special treatment that it seems to be getting." (See: MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Regional Banks Key To Independence - Judge <https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXZxukI6aJhchl1HA~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CC8ehptJe2eJOIQ> )

REGULATORY POWERS

Whether the exception the court carved out for the Federal Reserve this week extends to monetary policy functions only or shields the central bank more broadly from presidential control remains uncertain, Judge said.

"The Federal Reserve today looks very different than the First or Second Bank of the United States, and in particular it has a whole variety of regulatory responsibilities that are very similar to regular responsibilities being carried out by the Comptroller of the Currency and by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation," she said.

"One of the interesting and challenging questions going forward will be how the Federal Reserve Board carries out those powers, consistent with protecting its independence over monetary policy."

sales@marketnews.com <https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXZxukI6aJhchl1Gg~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CC8ehptJe2eJOIQ>

DATE: 2026-06-30 12:48:30 | SENDER: Nochomovitz, Yigal (Citi) <yigal.nochomovitz@investmentresearch.citi.com> | SUBJECT: CADL: Pipeline in a Product Thesis Advances as AURORA Ph3 Initiates On Schedule in NSCLC

CADL's initiation of the Ph3 AURORA trial in non-squamous NSCLC arrives in line with prior 2Q26 guidance, with the first site now activated. While enrollment pace will be a key metric to monitor, we view the Parexel CRO partnership as materially de-risking for the credible execution of the trial across ~150 global sites. We remain constructive on aglatimagene‘s potential in non-squamous NSCLC based on the positive Ph2a extended follow-up data, where mOS reached 25.4 months vs. docetaxel’s (SoC) ~10–12 months, a ~2x survival advantage which was supported by the ~25% of treated patients experiencing durable survival despite prior ICI failure (here and figure below). With continued execution supporting mgmt’s pipeline in a product thesis, and with the prostate BLA filing on track for 4Q26, we see further upside for the stock relative to the current trading level, which does not appear to fully reflect the compounding optionality across both programs. 
 	
Flash | Citi Research 	
Candel Therapeutics Inc (CADL.O) | Buy / High Risk 
Pipeline in a Product Thesis Advances as AURORA Ph3 Initiates On Schedule in NSCLC 
CITI'S TAKE 

CADL's initiation of the Ph3 AURORA trial in non-squamous NSCLC arrives in line with prior 2Q26 guidance, with the first site now activated. While enrollment pace will be a key metric to monitor, we view the Parexel CRO partnership as materially de-risking for the credible execution of the trial across ~150 global sites. We remain constructive on aglatimagene‘s potential in non-squamous NSCLC based on the positive Ph2a extended follow-up data, where mOS reached 25.4 months vs. docetaxel’s (SoC) ~10–12 months, a ~2x survival advantage which was supported by the ~25% of treated patients experiencing durable survival despite prior ICI failure (here <https://www.citivelocity.com/rendition/eppublic/documentService/dXNlcl9pZD1BQWYwUVBJOTlxZkxUc0ZaZUlxcmdGaXAxbGRHazlyXyZlbWFpbF9zZW5kX2lkPTQxMzcyNzY4MTAmdj0x/Y2xpZW50U3lzdGVtSWQ9UkRFX0ZBVkUmYmxhc3RLZXk9MTI2NTcxOTImRU5BQkxFX1JFTkRJVElPTl9JRlJBTUVfUEVSU09OQUxJWkFUSU9OPU4mdmVuZG9yPUNpdGkgVmVsb2NpdHkmZG9jX2lkPTMwNDEzODUyJnBsYXRmb3JtPTg0JmNsaWVudEJsYXN0SWQ9MzA0NDA1MDQ>  and figure below). With continued execution supporting mgmt’s pipeline in a product thesis, and with the prostate BLA filing on track for 4Q26, we see further upside for the stock relative to the current trading level, which does not appear to fully reflect the compounding optionality across both programs. 

	

The primary endpoint of AURORA is OS. As a reminder, the trial is enrolling ~500 metastatic Stage IV non-squamous NSCLC patients who have progressed on pembrolizumab and platinum chemotherapy. Patients will be randomized 1:1 to aglatimagene + valacyclovir with continued pembro vs. SoC docetaxel. Secondary end points will assess change from baseline in NSCLC symptom assessment questionnaire total score (NSCLC-SAQ), time to deterioration of NSCLC-SAQ, change from baseline of QoL scores (EORTC-QLQ-30), and other laboratory parameters.







Figure 1. Aglatimagene demonstrates durable survival in Ph2a NSCLC patients with progressive disease post-ICI 
 <https://www.citivelocity.com/rendition/eppublic/documentService/dXNlcl9pZD1BQWYwUVBJOTlxZkxUc0ZaZUlxcmdGaXAxbGRHazlyXyZlbWFpbF9zZW5kX2lkPTQxMzcyNzY4MTAmdj0x/Y2xpZW50U3lzdGVtSWQ9UkRFX0ZBVkUmYmxhc3RLZXk9MTI2NTcxOTImRU5BQkxFX1JFTkRJVElPTl9JRlJBTUVfUEVSU09OQUxJWkFUSU9OPU4mYW5jaG9yPWh0bWxfaW1hZ2VfMCZkb2NfaWQ9MzA0NDA1MDQmcGxhdGZvcm09ODQmY2xpZW50Qmxhc3RJZD0zMDQ0MDUwNA>

Separately, AWS is raising fees +20% on select GPU workloads which can translate to a 1-2 point benefit to 2H26 AWS growth. AWS acceleration will be driven by addition of OpenAI models on Bedrock, ramp up of capacity for the $38bn OpenAI commitment, and an early ramp of the $100bn Anthropic commitment (views <https://insight.email.bofa.streetcontext.com/platform/al?a=1000000000036595&ad=1000000003878585&h=ZxOgWnV&sig=1Lzy2sLb0j6uWM0gRtRubEE0CZ9&v=2&url=https://rsch.baml.com/r?q%3D2tRXZj7ywJlMyIQvhyoY!w%26e%3Dbofa.insight%2540bofa.com%26h%3Din8utQ> ). 


HOT TOPIC: THOUGHTS ON LEVERED ETFs… Levered ETF AUM has reached $180bn… with the total beta-adjusted “rebalance impact” now $27bn per 1% move in the S&P 500. That’s tripled from March 2026 lows. Much of this is driven by Semis (see Exhibit 16), with larger impacts on stocks with less liquidity or higher vol (see Exhibit 22). So, are they a threat to the market? Stress testing a worst-case scenario, a rebalance would represent 30% of volumes on a -20% 1-Day SPX decline (Exhibit 20). Which would be unlikely to drive a runaway price spiral like VIX experienced in 2018. The analysis starts on page 7 of this PDF of the: GEVI <https://insight.email.bofa.streetcontext.com/platform/al?a=1000000000036595&ad=1000000003878585&h=H1p6AO5&sig=8ySM66Ywo1ytaCNpYbEpAKiHPUF&v=2&url=https://rsch.baml.com/r?q%3DZaHBbsUwS8VMyIQvhyoY!w%26e%3Dbofa.insight%2540bofa.com%26h%3DpDCqNQ> . 

 

“TAKE PROFITS IN S&P AND SECULAR GROWTH”… that’s the headline from Strategist Savita Subramanian’s Mid-Year 2025 update linked below… she thinks the S&P 500's lofty multiple has been justified by Asset-Lightness, Capital discipline and Earnings quality. Corporates navigated a jump in Rates by pulling cash forward and shortening duration risk via buybacks, cost-cutting and efficiency measures. Plus, she says that Equity supply/demand dynamics peaked in bullishness in 2025, with liquidity coming from every channel: easy central banks, accelerating earnings, individual/institutional investor inflows, US government inflows and a spike in take-privates amid a dearth of IPOs… today, these levers are REVERSING. She likes Cyclicals over Secular Growth, they offer “Value Characteristics” and perform well during tightening cycles: S&P Update <https://insight.email.bofa.streetcontext.com/platform/al?a=1000000000036595&ad=1000000003878585&h=QLMS_YR&sig=Nc0VhO5hAEJijbhrBXbOM7Dgz9e&v=2&url=https://rsch.baml.com/r?q%3D70IVNyCGUmtMyIQvhyoY!w%26e%3Dbofa.insight%2540bofa.com%26h%3DY-O!cw> .
