End of Month Market Intelligence: rally, interrupted (barely) 
	
30 June 2026 | 12:51PM EDT | Research | Equity 	
	
	
US stocks are trading higher Tuesday but still on pace for a ~1+% decline for the month of June (for the S&P 500 as of Jun-30 at ~1:00PM) as investors have been digesting a surprisingly hawkish tilt from the Fed set against an encouraging reopening of the Strait of Hormuz (and subsequent plunge in oil prices) and all against a backdrop of still-strong ytd gains for equities (the S&P 500 is up 9.4% since Dec-31) and ahead of 2Q earnings season.

 	 

fade it further or buy (what's left of) the dip? 

The modest move lower in the S&P 500 for June comes even as more stocks have traded up than down this month led by strong gains in the Semis complex. And this strength in the tip-of-the-spear of Tech (compute power) comes even as every one of the Mag-7 stocks has lost considerable ground this month with a median stock loss of ~7% for the group.

The 'broadening' of market returns away from the 'one big trade' to encompass a range of stocks from HALO to Healthcare this month is for many alpha seekers encouraging news. Peter Oppenheimer reiterated our view that stocks are entering into a period of more diverse returns in a Jun-16 Strategy note, "The Post Modern Cycle – Navigating the Capex Boom <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQLPjydxvPb-vlW7fO1Jff_XrIUqxhAFQ7ySdIGBgIrkMF6psyR2AACwmh_kg6Ikd2b-aeF-0SEioZTQo7xBifCAiP4jMHcb_YRSeQBY_gfMy_mbTi4qYRsBxBL45A-GJWbLPQ64rArslE58ewP_L8d2xV2xMQR2oBDoH6SbJG3tGf-yV1szJh7eFlJYEwLrU5FEbwco_VJBADTWopVh_D5091qR5jzZX7hPkifUcR4fNYXk7aR2RVXnMmzKn5_ICAMnZC36Fvk13lQDNiKP89dA2ZNEkUEgM2Y*%26id=b23480b7-0fac-4222-b8bc-cbb92da1cc73%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1976124e-7e602691-4de4-4cc1-8d9d-930fc4a5476d-000000/f3cEcQZ6WMpWM9TEgQMRko8hcM5b_lLG6oAphh8CAKs=452> ." The combination of higher private capex demand, to fund the AI boom, and a growing need for governments to borrow is putting upward pressure on the cost of capital, driving higher growth in technology and increasing values of real assets. The result is rising cross-sectional dispersion, increasing the scope for alpha generation.

The upward pressure on cost of capital was a consistent theme throughout the month as yields on 10-year Treasuries entered June at 4.46% shot up 10bp to 4.56% and are closing out June at a still-elevated level of 4.40%. Along the way, new Fed Chair Warsh weighed in on monetary policy as the head of the FOMC for the first time, and delivered a hawkish surprise as David Mericle highlighted in a Jun-17 note, "June FOMC Recap: Hikes Look More Likely but Are Still Not Our Base Case <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQJ7LxY-2VLKU8hUn_osnU_YDVxT-hB84FOF1Ak6hve0egABjDk-AACwYI-Dac5uQNBI3eR-yBYbjvVgQcuyVl0yrOCde9AzeWGDPeLpoIRi_GIsVvVLvHfoR-LlAvPezJr-SKCtP7zpSWLR7Q_l3lrTZJ5UZU4VGDLI1-tp6UrXLJDDzlsvX2olk0Wg_MlcLFUiBbjjzDzzwjf5QrSQFgZDNk2vgmLUAKX7O68RVEqG5cpXpO0FDyvodkRj_g5EFOmdBwfInm_sQQ_M4FHF1EGAbAlc4NXHwxc*%26id=6f2ee376-b871-478a-a4d4-f5629f0b8292%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1976124e-7e602691-4de4-4cc1-8d9d-930fc4a5476d-000000/6x2Ib38Yl3VwLZJje-ebJ5V8aOd2_g3f7BE_iEJN0Ao=452> ." The meeting raises the risk of interest rate hikes later this year. But as Jan Hatzius also highlighted in a Jun-22 note, "More Crude, Less Concern <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQL5VBbvmKDWH34CxnBcIvv3-IaQoRBa353L2uTrbDTE8qxcMDChAACwhpycYe8gOdOWmlhO_5LQBKf0hx45iv6GtoSh925yYMGtomeuavDu9xw5TiLexca3Of55EjRnHtrfgcRYnYBpSik3VGlirj3xPUXD4HUCEo059FTosOgTBbpq1DAPuNjat2OXHl-Jp22bk9xMeXO7W178sLPHCSqSA_2sAZssgQV-dO3YDwtZYMXawmyKDqaJOWg1nyQqgAxINBDEhZsysNjegad_qILGZ5ahRPK1D6U*%26id=d9093e69-d1f0-4908-b629-d5cb36a1af52%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1976124e-7e602691-4de4-4cc1-8d9d-930fc4a5476d-000000/0X45_amrXhwpoZndy9YL1-yCQEHtAbV9El6g6uzP6HY=452> ," the Fed was acting on what is likely to prove to be stale news around energy prices, suggesting that any post-US-Iran war inflation relief is likely to be met by at least some FOMC committee members with a more dovish tone. Indeed, since the Jun-17 FOMC statement and press conference, front-month Brent is down another $7/bbl, nearing its pre-war price level.

Finally, in June, we also got updates on actual inflation with the latest coming last week with the May PCE release (see "USA: Core PCE in Line With Expectations <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQIZfNYcrpfzvkaO3YiuWTwvaIB6FRCcSWpRt3ABLMfN3ysXys8WAACwMs7or5EoH8-sQOuXUi1Y24sahRncv6As7v54ycd1R82lEuMHfCws3rlXs-TPGqRNZj7JD-gwNKf7Cylr_ahShegPa4vb6KkML1GhXC-fJMwr3k1aYoQHITlD504Ft4_VuRiNb7xgA2btzOQ_4XGQl2p6qtzanNNgegl-m-eIpAxpCI-oIlMn4j6

DATE: 2026-06-30 14:13:29 | SENDER: Risom, Skyler (IED) <skyler.risom@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: MS TMT: GOOGL Cloud and Capex estimates higher and PT to $415, 9GW capacity in 2028, better Search growth on AI ROIC
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SALES COMMENTARY | NOT A PRODUCT OF MS RESEARCH AND SHOULD NOT BE REGARDED AS A RESEARCH REPORT | FOR INSTITUTIONAL DISTRIBUTION ONLY 

 

Brian Nowak raises GOOGL Cloud estimates <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/10f16fcc-70cc-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae?t=1782839595:3485:11434:4110bfc5bc64&m=1&ch=Outlook Blastmail#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==>  and increases PT to $415, implying 25x 2027 EPS. He forecasts GOOGL will add 9GW of compute capacity in 2028 and sell 4GW TPU first-party. 

 

*reach out for updated GOOGL Cloud backlog model, GOOGL Capex model, and Hyperscaler Capex per GW model* 

 

GOOGL under pressure in recent weeks from top researcher departures <https://www.latimes.com/business/story/2026-06-29/google-poised-to-lose-two-more-senior-ai-staffers-to-anthropic>  to AI Labs and Mag 7-wide concerns over AI ROIC <https://www.ft.com/content/b90bdfcb-d773-42f7-bb5f-52dbd28b2174> .  

*	GOOGL trading at 18x Brian’s new $19 2028 EPS (a 15% discount to the ~21x long-term NTM avg).

 

Brian thinks that investors missed the implications of AVGO commentary on TPU upside earlier this month, which informs his estimate of 9GW on-prem compute capacity.

*	Joe Moore forecasts that AVGO will ship ~14GW total compute in 2028.  Brian estimates ~60% will be TPU, meaning 9GW.  

 

*	Given compute constraints (see recent $50/W deal <https://www.cnbc.com/2026/06/05/google-to-pay-spacex-920-million-a-month-for-xai-compute-capacity.html> ), Brian thinks that GOOGL will retain ~5GW of AVGO TPUs for its own workloads, so they will sell ~4GW to external customers. 

 

*	He thinks that MediaTek will add another 1GW / 1.5GW in 2027 / 2028.  Bottoms-up TPU capacity work for 2028 yields ~7GW in 2028.  He also expects +2GW of NVDA GPUs in 2028, for a total net addition of 9GW on-prem compute.

 

Catalyst is the next Cloud backlog update: the number was strong in last quarter EPS because of TPU contributions in 2026-2027.  It’s possible that GOOGL will soon include 2028 TPU in their updated backlog.

 



 

 

Brian assumes that ‘Core’ (pre-first-party TPU sales) GOOGL Cloud Revenue monetizes at $15 / $18 per watt in 2027 / 2028, resulting in $152B / $229B of total Core GOOGL Cloud / GCP Revenue.

*	GOOGL Cloud segment estimated to grow +106% / +44% in 2027 / 2028.

 

*	He forecasts first-party TPU sales will generate $62B / $79B of revs for GOOGL Cloud in 2027 / 2028.  Base case assumes 20% GM, so $20B per GW in revenue.

 

 



 

 



 

 

Higher TPU capacity necessitates higher Capex: Brian raises 2027 Capex to $350B given better visibility into 2028 TPU business.

 

And as 50% of incremental capacity is leveraged by the Core, Brian expects further monetization of continuously improving AI products:

*	Total Revs +4% / +1% and EPS +4% / +1% in 2027 / 2028.  
*	Revisions driven by better Cloud growth, as well as faster Search growth (+8% vs +7% prev) from GenAI and engagement improvements.

 

 



 

 

The rout from the ‘spenders’ to the AI Capex beneficiaries has driven elevated Mag 7 pessimism, especially as cheaper Chinese open-source models call Capex spending into question.

 

However, DeepSeek <https://www.scmp.com/tech/big-tech/article/3358868/after-triggering-price-war-deepseek-reverses-course-surcharge-peak-hour-api-use>  will reportedly now impose a surcharge on API usage at peak hours. The quality and price point of DeepSeek models are at the nexus of the perceived threat of foreign open-source models; this hike potentially challenges the very narrative set off by DeepSeek’s core offering.

 

*	More open-source: Meituan claims <https://www.reuters.com/world/china/chinas-meituan-says-new-ai-model-trained-domestic-chips-2026-06-30/>  open-source model LongCat-2.0 (1.6T-parameter) was trained on a 50k-chip cluster of local Chinese chips. 

 

*	More China localization: CXMT, the Chinese chip manufacturer, inked a $3B, three-year DRAM deal with Tencent for servers <https://www.reuters.com/world/china/chinas-cxmt-wins-3-billion-memory-supply-deal-with-tencent-sources-say-2026-06-29/> . AAPL is also apparently lobbying for access to CXMT chips <https://www.ft.com/content/d72a25e2-7bde-4aa9-bd8d-0c4f3d6cb2cb>  as Memory supply remains constrained.

DATE: 2026-06-30 15:06:51 | SENDER: Felipe Monteiro </O=EXCHANGELABS/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE GROUP (FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=247D1BDA87BE4D8189E2DEDD788CADAF-FELIPE.MONT> | SUBJECT: former samsung (30/06)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Expert Call Recap: Semiconductor Cycles, Foundry Dynamics, and Emerging AI Bottlenecks


Call with a former Executive Vice President at Samsung, previously responsible for a large business unit and $40B fab construction, and current CEO of a photonics startup (Abisena). Discussion covers semiconductor industry cycles, capex strategies, foundry competitive landscape, WFE outlook, and critical supply chain bottlenecks in AI infrastructure.


1. Executive Summary


*	The semiconductor industry is experiencing an unprecedented AI-driven demand surge, following the sharpest memory market decline ever in 2023.
*	Despite the surge, memory and foundry players (e.g., Samsung) are exercising caution with capex to avoid another oversupply, focusing on profitability over aggressive capacity expansion.
*	TSMC remains the undisputed leader in leading-edge foundry (85-95% market share), with Samsung a distant but capable second. Intel is seen as having "no chance" to catch up in the next 2-3 years, with internal products even shifting to TSMC.
*	Industry projections for WFE spending reaching $300 billion are considered "completely unrealistic" by the expert, who expects growth past $200 billion but not to the advertised highs due to lack of fab capacity and power constraints.
*	Long-Term Agreements (LTAs) for memory and foundry capacity are dismissed as "complete fucking bullshit" and essentially unenforceable if market conditions turn, with customers like Nvidia potentially using them to induce oversupply.
*	Key equipment segments benefiting from complexity are metrology, etching, and deposition, due to increased process precision and inspection requirements.
*	The expert identifies a progression of bottlenecks for AI infrastructure build-out: compute (resolved), memory (resolved for now), then storage, followed by interconnect/photonics, and ultimately power supply.
*	The laser-based photonics industry faces significant scaling challenges due to exotic materials, low yields, and structurally niche manufacturing, making it a critical choke point for AI.
*	The tone is nuanced and cynical regarding industry hype and customer behavior, but bullish on core AI demand and the long-term structural tailwinds for leading-edge semi.

________________________________


2. Key Takeaways by Theme


Semiconductor Market Cycles & AI Surge BULLNUANCED


The speaker provided a historical context of the semiconductor market, detailing the boom in 2021-H1 2022 due to COVID-driven electronics demand, followed by a sharp slowdown in late 2022 for foundry and late Q2 2023 for memory. The memory market experienced the "sharpest and most dramatic decline ever," with pricing halving and revenue literally cut by half in 2023. This led to a significant cut in capex, especially in NAND (down to zero for most players, except Samsung). The market then saw an inflection point around March-June 2025, driven almost entirely by AI data center infrastructure build-up, causing an "immense surge" in demand across compute and memory. Hyperscalers are placing orders of $20-30 billion capex per quarter for AI infrastructure. Initially, the surge (late 2024) was compute-driven (GPUs, AI accelerators), leading to advanced node shortages. Subsequently, memory became the bottleneck, particularly HBM, driving an undersupply of 10-15% and skyrocketing prices and profitability. The expert notes that the industry tends to make "infantile mistakes" by projecting trends indefinitely, emphasizing the cyclical nature on an upward trend.

*	Investment read-through: The AI infrastructure build-out is a powerful and sudden demand driver, compensating for and rapidly reversing the prior cyclical downturn. While the long-term trend is upward, investors should be wary of over-exuberance and factor in cyclical cooling periods.


Capex Allocation & Supply Discipline NUANCED


Historically, Samsung's average annual capex was around $40 billion (approx. $25-30 billion memory, $10-15 billion foundry). With the AI surge, this has increased to $60+ billion per year, roughly split as $40 billion in memory and $20 billion in foundry. Despite the demand, memory players are "very careful how much capex investment" they deploy, fearing overcapacity and a collapse in pricing. Samsung was the only memory player investing significantly in 2023, with capex more than double all other memory players combined, albeit still lower than prior years. This reflects a newfound discipline, or at least caution, in the industry to sustain profitability.

*	Investment read-through: The industry is showing signs of greater discipline, potentially leading to more stable, higher margins over cycles. However, the expert's skepticism about LTAs and customer behavior suggests this discipline could be tested by hyperscaler demand-side pressure. The shift in capex allocation towards memory (HBM) and advanced foundry is a clear trend.


Foundry Competitive Landscape BEARBULL


TSMC remains "head and shoulders ahead" of competitors, holding an 85-90% market share (even 95% in some advanced nodes). Samsung is seen as the only player capable of taking 10-15% market share from TSMC, primarily benefiting from TSMC's current capacity overload. Samsung's foundry revenue is projected to reach around $20 billion this year "with good profitability," with all overflow demand going to them. Intel has "literally no chance" to catch up in the next 2-3 years, with even internal Intel products increasingly moving to TSMC. Geopolitical events (e.g., China taking Taiwan) are cited as the only scenario that could significantly shift the market balance. The expert notes foundry investments are more demand-driven ("a function of your the order that you've already received").

*	Investment read-through: TSMC's dominant competitive moat is reinforced. Samsung's foundry business benefits from the overflow, but its long-term market share remains capped without a geopolitical

GEN-DIYA: PART IX.
 
As a recent[ish] Gen-Z college graduate who is now covering the Consumer sector with Michael Dick at BofA, I thought I’d put my high screen time and shopping addiction to use. With that in mind, here is the next edition of Gen-Diya, a series filled with Gen-Z observations, trends, channel checks, and more. 
 
Subscribe HERE <mailto:nicholas.villani@bofa.com;%20michael.m.dick@bofa.com;%20diya.panjabi@bofa.com?subject=Hi!%20Please%20Subscribe%20Me%20to%20Gen-Diya> , and request past editions of Gen-Diya HERE <mailto:nicholas.villani@bofa.com;%20michael.m.dick@bofa.com;%20diya.panjabi@bofa.com?subject=Hi!%20Pls%20Send%20Me%20Past%20Editions%20of%20Gen-Diya> . I’m also planning on conducting a survey of BofA summer interns and sending it out soon, so please keep an eye out, and let me know if there are any questions you’d like answered!
 
With that, let’s get into some of the top Gen-Z trends I’ve been seeing lately:
 
KNICKS FEVER X KALSHI X … LOVE ISLAND?
 
What’s better than a Knicks win?? A Knicks win AND free food and drinks! Sounds too good to be true, right? Not for those who watched the game at The Jeffrey, a bar on Manhattan’s Upper East Side. 
 
During the Eastern Conference Finals, the bar offered customers 1% off of tabs for every point the Knicks won by… and took a $4,000 hit as a result. Together, Owner Andy Freedman and Kalshi came up with a brilliant plan to offset the financial hit from promotional strategies like this one: Hedge the risk on Kalshi.
 
For the next big game, The Jeffrey used Kalshi to place a $5,000 wager on the Knicks. Knicks win? The bet pays out, and covers everyone’s tab… AKA, free food & drinks on the house! Knicks lose? The wager loses $5k, BUT the massive crowd they drew in more than makes up for it in revenue (source <https://fortune.com/2026/06/03/nyc-bar-knicks-kalshi-win-prediction-market/> ).
 
They’re not the only ones. Bars across NYC followed suit, and so did my local bagel shop. Utopia Bagels hopped on the Kalshi train to hedge the market, offering to use the payout to cover everybody’s breakfast the following morning. And let’s just say… I’m sure that Sunday morning bagel was desperately needed by many.
 
Plus, the energy of the crowd is 10x higher with rewards at stake. Sounds like a win-win to me! I expect (and hope) we’ll see more of this in the future, especially with the World Cup in progress and Football season around the corner (go Seahawks!)
 
What else has Kalshi been up to? They’ve created markets where people can bet on Love Island eliminations / top couples / more! I’ll admit, while I haven’t been a user in the past, this is both (1) extremely tempting, and (2) something I unfortunately have extensive knowledge on. In other words… if that “Purchases of the Month” section gets a whole lot longer, you know what’s funding it!
 
For more on Kalshi, check out this awesome private profile <https://rsch.baml.com/r?q=X0MMVc8u9rUc1nf-ZC3WOA&e=brian.fenske%40bofa.com&h=jYZ4Xw>  from analysts Shaun Kelley and Julie Hoover. 
 
THE “FIFA 15”
 
The latest trend that’s taken over TikTok? Food reviews from visiting World Cup fans. They’re immersing themselves in all of the quintessential American food experiences, with the most common stops I’ve seen being Chili’s (specifically for the triple-dipper), Taco Bell, In-N-Out, a 1am Waffle House run (classic), Starbucks, Crumbl, Olive Garden, IHOP, Raising Canes, Texas Roadhouse, Chipotle, automated soda machines, Reese’s Oreos, and Cheesecake Factory (where most have gotten too full to make it to the actual cheesecake). Their reactions are hilarious, a mix of delight and true awe.
 
Similarly, many are in absolute shock at the bottomless chips and dip at restaurants, experiencing the ultimate “cannon event” (Gen-Z slang for an unavoidable and highly common learning experience): eating too many chips, and consequently being too full to enjoy the actual meal. 
 
My favorite comment? With all of the new foods being tried, people are saying it will result in visitors heading back home with the “FIFA 15” (not to be confused with the Freshman 15).
 
Posts saying things like “To those heading to America for the World Cup, if there’s a Texas Roadhouse near your hotel, head there immediately!!” and “Is this size normal in America?”, as well as videos of visiting fans wearing cowboy hats from Buc-ees (another favorite, though my Texas self may be biased here) and calling Costco a “museum-like lifechanging ex

DATE: 2026-06-30 15:24:13 | SENDER: Applied AI <hello@theinformation.com> | SUBJECT: Exclusive: Anthropic Preps Claude Agent in Microsoft Teams
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Salesforce and Microsoft may be worried about threats posed by AI upstarts like Anthropic to their core enterprise apps, but they’re taking a conciliatory approach. Even though the two incumbents sell proprietary AI agents that can be used inside their Slack and Teams messaging apps, for instance, they’ve decided the apps ought to be a “platform” or app store for any AI agents their customers might want, including Anthropic’s Claude. A partnership Anthropic and Salesforce announced last week lets Slack customers summon Claude in their group chats to review their communications and handle workplace tasks, as long as they connect it to the other apps or databases their business uses.  And Anthropic recently told Microsoft it is planning to develop such a feature for Teams, according to someone briefed on the discussions.

DATE: 2026-06-30 15:30:33 | SENDER: Andrew Tyler - Americas Market Intelligence <andrew.m.tyler@jpmorgan.com> | SUBJECT: JPM Global Market Intelligence | Global Thematic Views: June 2026
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUMMARY OF THEMATIC VIEWS

Below is a summary of the views which we investigate in this note with the ‘Deep Dive’ section including (i) a detailed rationale for the theme; (ii) key charts; and, (iii) color on positioning.

 

*         SECURITY & RESILIENCE INVESTING (“SRI”) – A FOCUS ON INDUSTRIAL POLICY: Government priorities will remain drivers of equity returns. We anticipate Physical AI becoming more salient in US vs China competition. EU is moving on 2 axes, specifically Tech Sovereignty and Protectionism, but unlikely to do anything bold. China will continue to emphasize self-sufficiency in core technologies, supply-chain resilience, and strategic buffers in food and energy. The next China tech giants will be in upstream equipment/materials, the wafer-fabrication “foundation,” domestically memory, advanced packaging & testing, and compute/chips. Other Asian Economies will fight for their edge (Korea & Japan)  

*         GLOBAL CONSUMER – PART 2:  Our key argument is that the global macro regime should shift back to recovery/expansion (from slowdown/stagflation) and should drive an inflection in Consumer Sentiment and related Equity market themes. The Consumer also benefits from attractive price relatives and low positioning. Give the lack of earnings momentum we would still say selective and favor names with at least one of the following characteristics:  a) target more resilient upper-end  consumer (given wealth effects); b) capture the shift to spending  on experiences; c) are exposed to regions with solid wealth and cyclical backdrops (US,  Korea, Taiwan); and d) stand to benefit from a substantial decrease in oil prices in 2H26. 

*         TRACKING FLOWS IN THEMATICS: We track flows into 16x Secular Equity Themes. The AUMs are relatively small ($500bn) but are rising fast (25% organic inflows in June, 2-2.5x the rate for broader US Equities). Over the past month, the Themes with the strongest inflows have been AI, Infrastructure and Quantum while those with weakest inflow have been Blockchain, Space and EV & Battery.

 



 

THEMATIC DEEP DIVE

SECURITY & RESILIENCE INVESTING (“SRI”) – A FOCUS ON INDUSTRIAL POLICY. 



*         The world is becoming multi-polar and structural reorganization is underway in public and private investment from efficiency/globalization-first towards building greater national and economic security, resiliency and reliability. Hence, government priorities have become dominant drivers of equity returns globally. Priorities cluster around 5 key themes/areas <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514284&ad=4536925850&h=TiWj4Q9&sig=BMbL7gMj809k8ksJkl2ZeL7SPID&v=2&isig=VlvBj91InWXReAC7EvN3gKvYV4S&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/a3irdl74/GPS-5274031-0.pdf/2be655df-041a-4849-b44b-6d4930f16857> : 1) Advanced Manufacturing and Supply Chains; 2) Aerospace and Defense; 3) Energy Independence and Resiliency; 4) Frontier and Strategic Technologies; and 5) Pharma and Healthcare. Previous editions of this Thematic Pulse <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514284&ad=4536925850&h=roeqiCB&sig=S4uNfNMT8eoCvKtP5goVsi8FazB&v=2&isig=2ZwZunkrlqiPbHQZW7XMAzCAu3R&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/87jukur1/GPS-5284019-0.pdf/2be655df-041a-4849-b44b-6d4930f16857>  have covered 2) & 3) in details while below we run an update of what’s in focus right now.  

*         US –AI is seen as a two-country race between China and the US with both countries moving to vertical integration to limit external influences and to establish a dominant position on future industries. While the race on LLMs is more socialized, we think ‘Physical AI <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514284&ad=4536925850&h=_ZJSciJ&sig=4kyKo1TUUyVwpXzCBvjYaYFhqcJ&v=2&isig=aFeGOzW4MUE7dhNzYgWxMz7We98&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/a9qhgorl/GPS-5346537-0.pdf/2be655df-041a-4849-b44b-6d4930f16857> ’ is going to become the evolution of US-China competition. US officials could soon take action <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514284&ad=4536925850&h=_rXs6Lf&sig=OXS5aCdcr5gOkVmmkp9DBEYKVkT&v=2&url=https://www.politico.com/news/2026/06/23/lutnick-china-robots-commerce-00972576?nid%3D0000018f-3124-de07-a98f-3be4d1400000%26nname%3Dpolitico-toplines%26nrid%3D6689c2df-5a4c-473b-9b52-93479349fd17>  on Chinese Robotics as they increasingly see China’s state-backed robotics industry as a national security threat, fearing subsidized robots could dominate global markets before U.S. manufacturers have the scale to compete. China accounted for ~80% of all humanoid robot shipments in 2025, while it also dominates supply chains for drones. 

*         EU – the bloc is moving forward on two axes. 1) On AI/Tech, there is growing recognition <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514284&ad=4536925850&h=Isy0zoV&sig=3WAz84f3MHC8HjyEsO6OCAitaUN&v=2&url=https://europe2031.ai>  that dependence on others for AI technology has to be reduced. The response has been the EC Technological Sovereignty Package, which includes the Chips Act 2.0 and the Cloud & AI Development Act. The Chips Act 2.0 aims to build capacity in advanced semiconductor technologies, speed up permitting and support strategic projects. The Cloud and AI Development Act target a tripling of European data center capacity over the next 5-7 years and introduces a single EU-wide framework to assess cloud and AI sovereignty.  The initiatives so far are encouraging but consensus is that targets are unlikely to be met <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514284&ad=4536925850&h=J5E-srC&sig=Tnp9qlXyTx0nrex65BxL8YPyCwZ&v=2&isig=FkVVoEZajcFjTYPZtLLH5Y6DOFT&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/5vn7ua27/GPS-5342249-0/2be655df-041a-4849-b44b-6d4930f16857>  and actionable ideas spans only a handful of names in Cloud and Satellite space. 2) On trade, focus is on the ‘second C

͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­͏     ­

Background


New York has moved to the forefront of the national debate with the Responsible Data Center Development Act, omnibus legislation sponsored by Sen. Kristen Gonzalez (see here <https://javatar.bluematrix.com/docs/html/8a9f616f-c0d7-42bc-9a06-35ce65de2f96.html>  & here <https://javatar.bluematrix.com/docs/html/80ad0728-aa82-4316-bfb0-29dcec358f88.html> ). The bill would place a one-year pause on permits for new large data centers while the state evaluates their community impacts, and is now awaiting a decision from the governor.

On this call, we will discuss the bill’s key provisions and what New York’s proposal signals for the broader national conversation on AI infrastructure. Join us with Sen. Kristen Gonzalez, Chair of the New York State Senate Internet and Technology Committee.


Date & Registration


Monday, July 20, at 11:00 AM ET

DATE: 2026-06-30 16:12:39 | SENDER: Morgan Stanley Research <resweb@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: PULSE: Circle Internet Group Inc. (CRCL.N): Thoughts on Open Standard Announcement, Coinbase Partnership, and Composition of Stablecoin Activity
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Circle Internet Group Inc. (CRCL.N) 	
Thoughts on Open Standard Announcement, Coinbase Partnership, and Composition of Stablecoin Activity	 
Read Full Report <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/4b5a59a0-748a-11f1-9560-223b52d1e427?t=1782846664:1708:17494:acba1c0882e9&m=1&ch=CDF Research ISG#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> 	 
(PDF: 10 Pages) 	
North America 	
Stock Rating   Equal-weight
Price Target   $106.00

James E Faucette, Michael N Infante, Meryl R Thomas, CFA, Shefali Tamaskar	 
June 30, 2026

	

What happened? Earlier this morning, Open Standard announced Open USD, a new US dollar-backed stablecoin for global money movement, backed by a broad consortium of more than 100 fintechs, payment networks, banks, crypto firms, and technology platforms, including Visa, Stripe, BNY, BlackRock, Klarna, Chime, Alphabet, Coinbase, Mastercard, Shopify, DoorDash, Corpay, and others. The stablecoin is expected to go live later this year, with partners planning to integrate it into their systems. The stated goal is to build a stablecoin that is open, low-cost, high-volume, broadly accessible, and better aligned with business users by enabling free minting and redemption, shared reserve economics, and collaborative governance through an independent Open Standard entity.

Open Standard looks like a competitive risk for Circle from both a governance perspective...Open USD appears predicated on collaborative governance, with Open Standard operated by an independent company whose board is made up of Open USD partners. That contrasts with USDC’s more Circle-centric model, where Circle controls USDC governance. We find DoorDash’s (covered by Brian Nowak) comments—"in building payout products for Dashers and merchants in the U.S., we’ve seen firsthand how meaningful faster, more affordable access to earnings can be. Stablecoins give us a real path to bring that level of financial flexibility to other geographies we operate in. What sets Open USD apart is that it’s genuinely open: no single company controls it, and the partners building on it have a seat at the table. That’s the right foundation for moving money for everyone"—particularly interesting, as it implies collaborate governance is a key reason Open USD will be attractive to large distribution platforms. As a reminder, DASH recently announced a partnership with CRCL where it would leverage USDC for international driver payouts.

...as well as the underlying revenue model. Open Standard says partners receive the earnings generated on Open USD reserves, less a small management fee for operating costs, creating a broader default revenue-sharing model for consortium participants. Based on disclosed arrangements, Circle’s model appears more negotiated and distribution-led, with economics shared with partners such as Coinbase and Binance based on platform balances and treasury holdings. As a result, we think the key distinction is less that Circle cannot share yield and more that Open Standard is attempting to embed shared economics and shared governance into the core design of the stablecoin from inception.

Coinbase’s inclusion in the Open Standard consortium may not complicate the August renewal, but could be increasing the temperature. We still think it is very unlikely Coinbase voluntarily steps away from the Circle partnership because the deal remains quite favorable. Coinbase can continue building Coinbase Payments, push more commerce and settlement activity onto Base, and participate in Open Standard in pursuit of strategic optionality, all while preserving its USDC economics. As a reminder, Coinbase keeps 100% of the yield generated by USDC held on its own platform and receives 50% of the residual economics from off-platform USDC activity after contractual deductions. From a contractual perspective, the agreement was last was renewed on came on August 18, 2023, with the initial three-year term expiring in August 2026. From our read of the threshold criteria, we believe it's highly unlikely either party doesn't satisfy its obligations and thus, while Open Standard and Circle’s Arc both raise the strategic tension, Coinbase remains in a strong position with respect to its ability to monetize USDC, build Base, expand payments, and preserve strategic optionality at the same time.

USDC activity is still predominantly crypto trading in nature with BTC weakness resulting in stablecoin market cap compression. Per Exhibit 1,stablecoin activity remains overwhelmingly skewed to crypto trading and transfer activity vs. payments. McKinsey estimates roughly $80T of annualized stablecoin volume, of which $45T reflects technical transfers and roughly $35T reflects trading and other nonpayment financial activity, leaving only $0.39T of payments, or roughly 0.5% of unadjusted activity and about 1% of adjusted activity. That aligns with what we've observed as well, in that use cases beyond consumer remittances and in-country spending on USD-backed stablecoin-linked cards, remains limited. Additionally, while YTD changes in USDC market cap (down ~2% YTD) have fared meaningfully better vs. BTC (down ~32%), we continue to believe that meaningful expansion of USDC in market cap (where the company believes USDC market cap will continue to CAGR at ~40%) is predicated on real-world use cases that appear nascent and unlikely to meaningful inflect over the near-term (Exhibit 2, Exhibit 3).

The majority of stablecoin activity is still for non-payments use cases (e.g., crypto trading

Capstone, 

The next tech IPO wave is already taking shape, and the biggest signals are showing up before the filings. 

Our recent reporting revealed that Kalshi has passed $2 billion in annualized revenue and held informal IPO talks, while OpenAI’s $3.7 billion first-quarter cash burn raises new questions about how investors will judge AI companies heading toward the public markets. Space companies including Sierra Space, Vast Space and Axiom Space are also plotting listings as SpaceX fuels IPO momentum. 

Behind the headlines is a broader question investors, founders and operators are watching closely: Which major tech company will go public next? More importantly, when and how?

*       JPM ECON ON TODAY’S MACRO DATA (here <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514903&ad=4537353171&h=_g8iGGk&sig=BTp9DWad8NYrrIlhXwksNyNpDHi&v=2&isig=HSEu2KObQvoSZ2xlLENck2jCOes&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/-vu7jted/GPS-5353105-0/37539fe9-4bdf-465e-952c-42e15277b2a2> ) – “The labor market message from the June consumer confidence survey and May JOLTS sent conflicting messages, with consumer confidence suggesting that unemployment may yet rise further while the JOLTS managed to hold onto the spike in job openings from the prior month. The consumer confidence report in particular is a reminder that amidst a notable improvement in a range of labor indicators, including payroll growth and jobless claims, there continues to be ongoing deterioration in some measures that have historically been correlated with the unemployment rate.”

*       PREVIEW FOR ISM-MFG (Feroli; here <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13514903&ad=4537353171&h=GfdmPbf&sig=IV91hG3BmbsJ8Ld0IGN7HJIodqX&v=2&isig=12y5ZDXLDrQ2OUjQlHyBKNoqSf4&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/nahe0bhi/GPS-5321939-0/37539fe9-4bdf-465e-952c-42e15277b2a2> ) – “We expect the June ISM manufacturing index to tick up to 55.0 from 54.0 in the prior month, along with a broadly unchanged print of 56.0 on the final PMI manufacturing report. The ISM has been marking cycle-high levels since the large jump in January, with some of the recent improvement driven by front-loading behavior to get ahead of rising inflationary pressures and supply chain issues from the Middle East conflict, as noted in recent ISM and PMI press releases. Early signals from the flash PMI report and the regional manufacturing surveys point to continued strength in manufacturing. Since the spike in January, both the new orders and production metrics have been declining in the ISM report, before the improvement in May. The index for new orders moved to 56.8 in May from 57.1 in January, while the production index marked 54.3 in the latest report from 55.9 at the start of the year. This wedge between the two metrics has moved to the upper end of its recent range, which could point to a further rise in manufacturing activity in the upcoming print. The flash PMI manufacturing report saw moderating price pressures, likely reflecting receding global energy prices. However, the price index remains elevated.”

DATE: 2026-06-30 18:12:17 | SENDER: Daniel Grozdea </O=EXCHANGELABS/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE GROUP (FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=7712A7E28EA34D5F95E956A82CF5CA0F-47207B35-27> | SUBJECT: TSEM Susq_30 jun 26 (30/06)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Tower Semiconductor: Optical Interconnect Technology & Market Update


Insights from a call with Marco and Amol from Tower Semiconductor, discussing the evolving landscape of optical transceivers, silicon photonics, and AI infrastructure interconnects.


1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY


*	The optical interconnect market is experiencing significant, multi-year growth, driven by accelerating data rates (currently **1.6T**, with **3.2T** next) and expanding AI/datacenter build-outs. This includes both exploding unit volumes and technology migration.
*	A critical transition is underway from traditional pluggable transceivers to **Near Package Optics (NPO)**, with NPO expected to see significant production volume in 2025 (some in 2024), particularly for **1.6T** deployments. NPO, by bringing optics closer to the ASIC, offers enhanced performance and content opportunities.
*	Tower Semiconductor (TSEM) is a direct beneficiary, seeing higher content per module in NPO due to potential for more integrated lanes and combined transmit/receive (Tx/Rx) functions on its silicon photonics (SiPho) dies.
*	TSEM's **heterogeneous integration platform**, which embeds Indium Phosphide (InP) lasers directly onto SiPho wafers, is a key immediate opportunity. This technology, already in early production, simplifies module assembly, improves reliability, and expands TSEM's serviceable available market (SAM) to include high-value laser components.
*	The widespread adoption of **Co-Packaged Optics (CPO)** is seen as a longer-term event, potentially diminished and delayed by the success and sufficiency of NPO in addressing many current challenges like signal loss. CPO presents significant integration, thermal, and testing hurdles.
*	TSEM’s **200mm SiPho platforms** remain highly competitive and often more cost-effective than 300mm for current optical applications, though TSEM is strategically expanding its **300mm capacity** (pending a METI grant) for future larger form factor or specialized applications.
*	New players and startups (e.g., **Cintil**, **Salience**, **Oriel**, some backed by **Nvidia**) are leveraging TSEM's advanced foundry capabilities to drive innovation in integrated lasers and optical switching. Overall tone is bullish on TSEM's positioning and the broader optical interconnect market.

________________________________


3. KEY TAKEAWAYS BY THEME


Optical Interconnect Market Growth & Data Rate Migration BULL


The speaker highlighted an explosive increase in the number of units and a rapid progression in data rates. The market has moved from **400 Gigabit per second (Gbps)** a few years ago, through **800 Gbps** last year, and is now transitioning to **1.6 Terabit per second (Tbps)** as the dominant data rate, with **3.2T** expected next. This migration necessitates technology refreshes in both silicon photonics (SiPho) and silicon germanium (SiGe) components, as they must double their operating speed. This leads to more value for the customer and for Tower Semiconductor.

*	Why it matters: Sustained demand for higher-speed optical interconnects directly correlates with the growth in AI infrastructure and hyperscale data centers. This trend drives unit growth and increases the complexity and value of individual components, benefiting specialized foundries like Tower Semiconductor.
*	Investment read-through: This dynamic ensures a multi-year growth runway for the optical interconnect sector and its enablers.


Transition from Pluggable to Near Package Optics (NPO) and Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) NEUTRAL


The discussion provided a clear differentiation between pluggable, NPO, and CPO architectures:

*	Pluggable: 
*	Near Package Optics (NPO):higher content per die due to more integrated lanes and a trend towards combining transmit and receive functions.
*	Co-Packaged Optics (CPO): 

NPO is described as a "good solution" that solves most of the problems addressed by CPO without incurring all the complexities. It's closer to being "real" and already available. The speaker suggests that NPO, as it gains traction, has the potential to minimize the perceived benefit of CPO and push out its widespread adoption to some degree. NPO is expected to see significant production volumes next year (2025), with some activity in **2024**, aligning with **1.6T** deployments. It could also be sufficient to enable "scale up" within the rack.

*	Why it matters: 
*	Investment read-through:Positive for NPO adoption in the near to medium term, benefiting TSEM with higher content. BULL

Both SiPho and SiGe technologies are crucial for optical transceivers. SiPho primarily handles the transmit modulator side, while SiGe is used for drivers and Transimpedance Amplifiers (TIAs) on the receive and transmit electronic pieces. Both technologies are seeing significant growth, with SiPho experiencing **3-4x year-over-year growth** and SiGe **20-30% year-over-year growth** in recent years.

The migration to NPO further enhances opportunities for both: 

	*	SiPho: 
	*	SiGe: 
	*	Why it matters: 
	*	Investment read-through:Strong positive for Tower Semiconductor, indicating sustained and growing demand for its core offerings in the optical space.


Heterogeneous Integration of Indium Phosphide Lasers on SiPho BULL


Tower Semiconductor has announced and is in early production of a platform that integrates Indium Phosphide (InP) lasers directly onto silicon photonic wafers. This is a significant development:

	*	Technology: 
	*	Benefits for Customers: 
	*	Benefits for Tower:Bundles two components into one, significantly expanding Tower's serviceable available market (SAM) to include the high-value laser component. It also offers enhanced reliability (hermetically sealed within the wafer, no 3-5 material exposed to moisture) and can help with thermal management by enabling external laser sources for CPO or NPO applications.
	*	Market Application:pluggable and NPO markets and does not r

DATE: 2026-06-30 19:10:25 | SENDER: Amerian, Amir <amir.amerian@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: GLASS/PANELS - the AI story - TSM vs INTC,  GLW,  Innolux vs BOE,  ABF Substrates
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SALES COMMENTARY ONLY (NOT A PRODUCT OF RESEARCH)

For institutional use onLY

 

I used to say silicon wafers were the final frontier of AI penetrating the deepest parts of the supply chain. But I stand corrected – Panel stocks would be one of the last and most surprising areas of tech to finally see AI benefit the numbers. It’s still early to see any financial impact, but with Innolux +300% YTD and GLW’s recent rally, I’m getting more questions what’s going on in glass/panels. I’ll do my best to summarize what’s going on, but for the in-the-weeds technology discussion, our Greater China Hardware analyst Derrick Yang is a great resource <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/295f25ba-6472-11f1-918b-4841bb500f53?t=1782857414:7515:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> , along with of course Head of Greater China Semis Charlie Chan and US Networking Equipment analyst Meta Marshall (her take on GLW here <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/ef10c80c-73d8-11f1-9560-223b52d1e427?t=1782857414:7515:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> )

 

 

The source of this excitement on glass/panels:  TSMC vs INTC.  Specifically in Advanced Packaging.  It’s well telegraphed at this point that the upcoming version of INTC’s advanced packaging technology (EMIB-T) has performance and cost advantages over that of TSMC (CoWoS). These advantages theoretically are evident when we get to very large chips (i.e. above 9.7 reticle-size). To be fair, excitement on EMIB-T is still early. The original EMIB failed for multiple reasons, but this time market is more excited for EMIB-T due to 1) much higher sample yields (although Howard Kao notes Substrate makers worry production yields will still be low); and 2) the warpage and cost advantages vs CoWoS in these large chips. Therefore, if we assume EMIB-T can be a viable technology, the market believes TSMC will more aggressively adopt glass/panel across parts of its advanced packaging technology to compete.

 

 

Before I go further, I’ll emphasize again that CoWoS vs EMIB-T is the key driver of painting any blue sky. If market sours on EMIB-T, the 2nd derivative impact may be thinking TSMC needs to less aggressively adopt parts of below technologies. And I’ll emphasize that from a stock perspective, it’s ok to NOT be too early on these potentially long-dated technology shifts. Derrick and team wrote a really great deep-drive in 2024 <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/a7bf4330-91f7-11ef-9743-347dd77fb5d0?t=1782857414:7515:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> , but their message then was it’s too early. Just comparing Nittobo vs Innolux (the former being a perceived loser from “Glass Core Substrate”), sure Innolux has outperformed YTD, but Nittobo is up 1055% since Jan 2023 vs Innolux 408%.

 

 

With this context, I will get into the 2 technologies that TSMC is potentially using to close the gap vs EMIB-T:

 

1) Glass Core Substrate

 

The goal is to solve for warpage in CoWoS as we get to larger chips.

 

In “CoWoS”, this changes the “oS” aka Substrate. Right now, the Substrate is made using an organic CCL (think Resonac/Mitsubishi Gas, who require T-glass from Nittobo). The ABF layers goes on top of the CCL. But in Glass Core, it replaces the organic CCL with a Glass Core. It’s essentially a piece of glass that uses “TGV” for vertical connectivity (TGV = Though Glass Vias, aka holes, think like TSV when we talk about HBM). After the Glass layer, then there is copper layer, then ABF, then copper, then ABF, etc.

 

So if we just take this on face value, market assumes it’s a negative for CCL and T-glass, but still a positive for ABF Substrate (Ibiden, etc) along with Glass supplier (e.g. GLW) and Panel makers (e.g. Innolux). The panel maker is primarily responsible for drilling the TGV holes, and the glass maker would need to come up with the right chemistry for the glass, both working to make cracks in the glass much less likely.

 

Timing wise, Derrick says adoption is more likely 2H28, vs market assumes CoPoS comes in 2029. That means theoretically speaking, Glass Core Substrate wouldn’t contribute to full year earnings until 2029 (the mass production year for Feiynman).

 

What got market excited was that on June 11th, TSMC at an event in Japan talked about Glass Core Substrate and specifically listed Ibiden and Innolux on a slide as development partners. Derrick checks suggest what this TSMC slide means is just that proof of concept is completed. I.e. TSMC has validated the benefits over organic. But now is when design starts for the product and spec. Then gets tested again. And after this, TSMC might release the spec to the industry and look for more partners.

 

Derrick says theoretically speaking, if Innolux and Ibiden are development partners with TSMC, they would like have high share in the first generation at mass production. But he would assume TSMC would want more supply chain partners from resiliency perspective. 

 

On the Panel side, Derrick says AUO is not focused on this, so the competitive threat is BOE (he is OW). But BOE’s strategy is different. BOE wants to do the entire Glass Core Substrate stack, so both Glass Core and the Substrate (vs splitting Innolux / Ibiden). I’m personally a little surprised and wonder where BOE would have built the ABF Substrate know-how from (remember that Unimicron still struggles to gain meaningful share vs Ibiden within NVDA). But BOE does have global aspiration ex NVDA, so not just supporting China’s ecosystem. Derrick says BOE’s strategy is to work with other GPU and ASIC makers who may need to transition to Glass Core / TGV, and if they build partnerships with the fabless customers, that may cause the fabless customers to push TSMC to use BOE as a supplier.

DATE: 2026-07-01 00:54:03 | SENDER: Hacking, Alexander (Citi) <alex.hacking@investmentresearch.citi.com> | SUBJECT: Alcoa Corp (AA.N): Sizing Up With S32 Assets; Accretive On Citi's Bullish Price Deck.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Alcoa has announced the acquisition of S32's bauxite, alumina and aluminum assets (ex-Mozal).  Payment is mostly cash, i.e. long-term success/failure will largely be a function on aluminum/a prices.  The deal adds more alumina (+54%) than aluminum (+34%).  The transaction is not a surprise - Alcoa mgmt. had flagged its appetite for this kind of M&A with asset overlap in Australia and Brazil.  Deal size is $4.7-5.4bn EV (with contingent payments) or 31-36% of AA.  S32 is flagging $1.2bn of ARO's that are less at ~$400m under US GAAP.  Valuation isn't straightforward given huge recent volatility in aluminum/a prices but is EBITDA per share accretive on 2025, 2026E, 2027E and Spot prices - see Fig 1.    AA's stock may see pressure & the stock component is a future overhang - but the numbers work on Citi's bullish price deck & we like the clear path to de-leveraging (FCF, asset sales, Ma'aden stock sales).   
 	
Flash | Citi Research 	
Alcoa Corp (AA.N) | Buy 
Sizing Up With S32 Assets; Accretive On Citi's Bullish Price Deck. 
CITI'S TAKE 

Alcoa has announced the acquisition of S32's bauxite, alumina and aluminum assets (ex-Mozal).  Payment is mostly cash, i.e. long-term success/failure will largely be a function on aluminum/a prices.  The deal adds more alumina (+54%) than aluminum (+34%).  The transaction is not a surprise - Alcoa mgmt. had flagged its appetite for this kind of M&A with asset overlap in Australia and Brazil.  Deal size is $4.7-5.4bn EV (with contingent payments) or 31-36% of AA.  S32 is flagging $1.2bn of ARO's that are less at ~$400m under US GAAP.  Valuation isn't straightforward given huge recent volatility in aluminum/a prices but is EBITDA per share accretive on 2025, 2026E, 2027E and Spot prices - see Fig 1.    AA's stock may see pressure & the stock component is a future overhang - but the numbers work on Citi's bullish price deck & we like the clear path to de-leveraging (FCF, asset sales, Ma'aden stock sales).  

	

Highlights from the AA call:

*	Management rationale: Clear strategic fit - highly complementary assets.   Synergies - $900m NPV,  including $50m in 1 year run-rate cost savings.  Note: the vast majority synergies are in Western Australia mining/refinery operations.  Financials - EPS and FCF accretive.   AA is acquiring well below replacement costs: $1,850/ton smelting; $600/ton refining.
*	Asset highlights: Western Australia - Boddington bauxite & Worsley alumina refinery:  big opportunity to optimize long-term mine planning.   Brazil - Additional interest in Alumar refinery & smelter (which AA already part-owns & operates).  South Africa - Hillside smelter:  immediate cash flow accretive; same AP30 smelting technology that already operate; power contract through 2031.
*	Deal size is $4.7-5.4bn=$3.1 bn cash + $1 bn AA stock (17 mln shares) + $600m of lease-related debt + $750m of contingent payments linked to metals prices (see Fig 3).  S32 is flagging $1.2bn of rehabilitation liabilities in its presentation but AA noted that these are ~$400m under US GAAP on their call.
*	Approvals could take up to 12 months and close in 1H27.  S32 will have a shareholder vote in Oct/Nov - early signs are positive with the stock trading up in Australia.
*	No intention to raise additional equity given expected strong FCF generation in 2H, plus asset sales, plus Ma'aden shares.

DATE: 2026-07-01 01:03:49 | SENDER: John Aiken, CFA <jaiken@jefferies.com> | SUBJECT: USMCA Negotiations vol. 2 - Where Things Stand Now On July 1
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://www.jefferies.com>   	Equity Research
July 1, 2026	 
	Canada | Cross-Sector Views	 
 <https://javatar.bluematrix.com/links2/html/40f635e3-d597-4108-9b84-1719b7b8f9e5> 	 	 
USMCA Negotiations vol. 2 - Where Things Stand Now On July 1 <https://javatar.bluematrix.com/links2/html/40f635e3-d597-4108-9b84-1719b7b8f9e5> 	 
The mandatory July 1 USMCA joint review shifted from a routine assessment into a high-stakes renegotiation under Trump 2.0. Given contentious U.S.–Canada talks, the two economies now face ambiguity without the formal renewal, moving to annual reviews with the U.S. pursuing bilateral carve-outs. Trade keeps flowing, but policy uncertainty is extended indefinitely. While negative for the economic outlook, it is preferable to the devastation of a full withdrawal.

	
Source: Jefferies, Governments of Canada, Mexico and the U.S.	

As we have now passed the July 1 deadline to renew the USMCA, the agreement has now devolved into 10 years of annual reviews until the agreement renegotiated or expires (unlikely). While President Trump recently disparaged the agreement that he negotiated six years ago, it is unlikely that the U.S. will terminate the agreement. However, even with progress between Mexico and the U.S., we see no immediate resolution between Canada and the U.S., with pundits going as far as saying that discussions could proceed past the November mid-terms. We do not believe the market is adequately pricing in the risk of extended negotiations heading into the winter or even 2027.

While trade continues to flow between Canada and the U.S., the lack of certainty has some specific impacts on the economy that will remain as headwinds until there is greater clarity:

*	Prolonged Investment Limbo: A rolling annual review cycle effectively institutionalizes a state of permanent trade negotiation and policy uncertainty, keeping businesses and multinational corporations in a state of long-term planning limbo.
*	Chilled Capital Expenditure: While trade continues under existing tariff-free frameworks, the lack of long-term regulatory visibility is expected to chill capital investment, delay major corporate relocations (nearshoring), and compress operating margins for cross-border logistics.

From our perspective, the negotiating stances between the two nations remain far apart with little movement in recent discussions. The U.S. remains frustrated with Canada's supply management in its dairy industry, provincial bans on American alcohol sales and has pressured the Canadian government on its digital streaming tax.

Removing steel & aluminum tariffs is a priority for Canada. For the Canadian metals and mining sector, a key goal for Canada in its negotiations is removing the 50% tariffs on steel and aluminum exports to the US. The next best outcome would be reducing the tariff rate on steel and aluminum - potentially to 25% on steel and 10% on aluminum, as was the case briefly in 2018. We think this is more likely than 0% tariffs. It appears bilateral agreements, instead of a renewal of USMCA, is the most likely outcome, in which case applying different tariff rates to different metals is certainly on the table. A bilateral agreement would represent a more formal framework - one that is adjacent to USMCA - vs. the current piecemeal Section 232 tariffs. We think it's unlikely tariffs will be applied to other metals such as copper and gold in a bilateral agreement. Finally, we expect Canada will use critical minerals supply as leverage to negotiate lower tariffs on steel and aluminum.

Other Publications in and related to the series:

*	USMCA Negotiations - Implications for the Canadian Economy and Major Sectors <https://content.jefferies.com/links2/pdf/6aab565b-4fb0-436f-8007-eb813b570270?firmId=32195> , April 16
*	USMCA Negotiations: Implications for Canadian Economy & Major Sectors | REPLAY <https://content.jefferies.com/links2/pdf/295f9e39-143b-4cde-8be0-a23d0c872cdb?firmId=32195> , April 27
*	Unpacking USMCA Review with The US Chamber of Commerce | RECAP <https://content.jefferies.com/links2/pdf/57011018-2df5-443b-88be-638e7399ce68?firmId=32195> , May 15
*	USMCA Outlook with Fm. Undersecretary of Finance of Mexico | REPLAY <https://content.jefferies.com/links2/pdf/80b08194-ef1c-4406-aac2-a12409f6628d?firmId=32195> , June 1

DATE: 2026-07-01 01:11:05 | SENDER: Morgan Stanley Research <resweb@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: IDEA: Grindr Inc. (GRND.N): On the EDGE of Glory; Upgrade to Overweight
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Grindr Inc. (GRND.N) 	
On the EDGE of Glory; Upgrade to Overweight	 
Read Full Report <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/09d5dbfc-7184-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae?t=1782878682:3075:45476:5e2e4f67363b&m=1&ch=CDF Research ISG#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> 	 
(PDF: 45 Pages) 	
North America 	
Stock Rating   Overweight
Price Target   $18.00

Nathan Feather, Brian Nowak, CFA	 
July 1, 2026

	
WHAT'S CHANGED?	 
Grindr Inc. (GRND.N)	 
Rating	 
From:   Equal-weight	 To: Overweight	 
Price Target	 
From:   $15.00	 To: $18.00	 
GRND is a one-of-one asset that’s heavily undermonetized versus peers, but it's launching two products which could change that: an ultra-premium subscription ($100-500/mo.) and a DTC telehealth brand. Trading at a ~35% discount to peers with a compelling catalyst path, we upgrade to OW; $18 PT. 
Key takeaways	 

*	GRND has strong fundamentals with a now compelling catalyst path trading at a discounted valuation; Upgrade to Overweight 
*	A high quality asset with strong network effects (15M MAUs), industry-leading engagement (>65 mins/DAU), and significant profitability (>40% EBITDA margin) 
*	GRND monetizes ~30% below peers, but it's launching 2 products which could help: EDGE (ultra-premium tier coming 4Q/1Q) and Woodwork (DTC telehealth brand) 
*	With GRND's revenue growth of ~$90M/year (on a ~$500M base), we believe EDGE and Woodwork each have the potential to deliver 'one-year' or more of growth 
*	Its multiple has ~halved over the past year to ~11x EBITDA, or a ~35% growth-adjusted discount to peers, creating a compelling entry point 

High quality asset, a compelling catalyst path, and discounted valuation; upgrade to OW: Grindr is an underappreciated company with strong network effects, industry-leading engagement, and significant profitability. However, the stock is down 36% over the past year on concerns that paywall-led monetization was impacting user growth. We initially shared those concerns <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/fb1decd2-8fe1-11f0-a3f6-3da67634994d?ch=rp&sch=cr> , but have grown meaningfully more constructive as GRND has pivoted towards healthier product-led monetization with the upcoming launch of its ultra-premium tier EDGE (~$100-$500/mo.) and telehealth brand Woodwork (a HIMS competitor). Either could be individually transformative for GRND, but with both in development we now have conviction the brand can grow revenue at a 18% '25-'28 CAGR… with far more upside than downside. With the stock trading at just 11x '27 EBITDA, a ~35% discount to peers on a growth-adjusted basis, we see a compelling entry point ahead of a rich catalyst path and upgrade to OW with a $18 price target (25% upside). If EDGE or Woodwork can become a meaningful win for the brand, we believe our $29 bull case valuation could be in play (~100% upside). 

GRND is a one-of-one asset that’s heavily undermonetized versus peers: Grindr has strong network effects among its 15M users, reaching 60% global brand awareness despite marketing spend at <4% of revenue. Users are highly engaged with DAUs spending >65 minutes on the app daily. That has translated to consistent >40% EBITDA margins. For a sense of its ubiquity, about half of gay relationships in the US start on GRND. It also plays in a higher income and more retentive segment than online dating brands like Tinder or Bumble. Despite its advantages, the app monetizes ~30% below other dating apps - a gap which we believe can close as GRND expands its product suite. 

GRND is shifting from value extraction to value creation with two products that could enable step-function upside: Grindr had been underinvested in and undermonetized before going public in 2022. Since then, the company materially increased and optimized the paywall which delivered a remarkable ~31% '22-'25 topline CAGR, but also increased user frustration and led to MAU growth concerns. The company has been working to pivot towards healthier product-led monetization (creating new value for users and then capturing it). That process has taken time, but we now have line of sight to meaningful contribution from two new products that we believe can drive revenue without impacting user growth: EDGE (an ultra-premium tier) and Woodwork (a DTC telehealth brand). The upside from these new products is material: GRND has grown revenue at ~$90M per year and we believe EDGE and Woodwork could each deliver 'one-year' or more of revenue growth (>$90M).

1) EDGE: Grindr is set to launch an ultra-premium, AI-led tier which could drive the next leg of growth: GRND is planning to launch EDGE in 4Q26/1Q27, targeting its high-income power users with AI-based tools for better profile discovery and ways to re-spark past connections. The company tested pricing at $80/month in Australia and saw significantly higher than anticipated demand. As a result, it's now testing pricing at $100-$500/month. That's well above anything major peers are charging and could represent a step-change in revenue with even modest adoption. For every 10bps of payer penetration at $100/month, EDGE would be a 4% contribution to revenue. So GRND getting 0.25% of its MAUs to subscribe to EDGE at $200/mo. would be equivalent to an entire year of revenue growth (~$95M)… and GRND is targeting higher payer penetration and pricing(~50-100bps with pricing up to $500/mo.). In our base case, we model EDGE generates $78M of revenue by '28 (11% of total) while in our bull case we model $113M (15% of bull revenue).

2) Woodwork: Its new telehealth business offers a novel physical + digital bundle: GRND is also planning to launch a variety of DTC product lines to sell to its users. The first is Woodwork, a HIMS-like telehealth business offering ED medication, GLP-1s, and peptides (HIMS is covered by Craig Hettenbach). As 30% of its user base uses ED medication and 60% have considered it, there is a sizeable addressable market. The value prop is clear as Woodw

DATE: 2026-07-01 01:18:24 | SENDER: Joseph Moore <Joseph.Moore@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: Semiconductors: Semiconductor Inventory Tracker: Not Restocking Yet
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Semiconductors 	
Semiconductor Inventory Tracker: Not Restocking Yet	 
Read Full Report <https://ms.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13515781&ad=4538214017&h=DPgazJ6&sig=TR48zAL7WkrV73hRAzWEj3ifPGy&v=2&url=https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/27302d02-6f5d-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae?t%3D1782879381:1922:17494:acba1c0882e9%26m%3D1%26ch%3DCDF%20Research%20ISG%20Autoblast%23e%3DdHJhY2tlZC1tb29yZWpvcy1jZGZhLTMwMzQ4NzktcGNkZmlyZXMtcG1ocGxvY3ZibGJ6K3d2bTB5YW92QG1zLnN0cmVldGNvbnR4dC5uZXQ%3D> 	 
(PDF: 16 Pages) 	
North America 	
Industry View   Attractive

Joseph Moore, Nicole Kozhukhov, Ella Tulchinsky, Shane Brett, Mason Wayne	 
July 1, 2026

	
Supply chain inventory rose q/q but outperformed seasonality, with below-seasonal producer builds and distributor declines. Supply is tightening, but meaningful restocking has yet to emerge. 
Key takeaways	 

*	Overall supply chain outperformed seasonality, increasing by less than the typical 1Q increase. 
*	Producer and disti DOIs outperformed seasonality; customers were ~in-line. 
*	Auto OEM DOI moved above historical median, while Auto Supplier DOI declined to in-line with historical levels. 

Overall supply chain inventory increased q/q in 1Q, but the build was below typical 1Q seasonality. We remain above historical median levels, as distributors declined and producers built less than seasonal levels, while customers were ~in-line. While this is a step in the right direction, we still remain 33 days above historical median for the supply chain, and have not yet seen a broader restocking cycle.

The quarter reflected a mix of normal 1Q inventory build and continued discipline across the supply chain rather than broad restocking. Distributors continue to lean out, producer builds remain relatively steady, and customer trends were mixed. For stocks, we prefer areas where supply/demand is tightening or inventory risk is more defensible, including premium-end analog exposure in ADI and NXP, compute/networking names NVDA, AVGO, and CBRS, memory names MU and SNDK, and semicap names MKSI, KLAC, LRCX and ONTO.

Stacked DOI increased 9 days vs. a seasonal 19-day increase and is 33 days above the historical median. Trailing decreased ~2 days. 
 
Source: FactSet, Morgan Stanley Research

DATE: 2026-07-01 02:53:32 | SENDER: sunny.lin@ubs.com <sunny.lin@ubs.com> | SUBJECT: UBS: UBS Global I/O Semiconductors "Cloud AI: TSMC and ASE driving faster CoWoS..."
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Adv packaging for next-gen AI chips diversifying, but TSMC remains the leader with a 50% sales CAGR for the segment the next 5 years. 
 <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed83> 	 	 Global Research 
01 July 2026 	
Global I/O	●	UBS Global I/O Semiconductors	
Cloud AI: TSMC and ASE driving faster CoWoS expansion, unlocking larger TAM <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed84&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjM0Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=fBX7HTilmP8e3PuTRpl0DUVq1zH98KoYbaFOvMDWu5A>  	
Adv packaging for next-gen AI chips diversifying, but TSMC remains the leader with a 50% sales CAGR for the segment the next 5 years. 


Read Report   > <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed85&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjM1Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=hC4t2pTa1-P1uMT9SKqtGMJlI2qIs2crA-O3WHKk9UA> 		
CoWoS capacity upside in 2026-27 across TSMC and ASE 

We view TSMC and broader industry CoWoS expansion as a leading indicator of cloud AI demand over the next 2-3 years. Capacity expansion over the next 12-18 months is progressing faster than we expected a month ago <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed86&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjM2Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=xu2nr_955ZiTJ_IxOTRJR2-egtz0l100I4z2-4mzUjw> , suggesting stronger underlying cloud AI demand. TSMC's CoWoS capacity expansion is re-accelerating and we now expect capacity to reach 130k/180k wpm by end-2026/27 vs our prior estimates of 120k / 150k wpm. We believe this reflects a much larger advanced packaging TAM over the next several years, with a meaningful portion likely to remain on CoWoS even as Intel EMIB-T and TSMC CoPoS enter mass production in 2028. ASE has also been accelerating its full-process capacity expansion for 2027. We now forecast its full-process CoWoS capacity to more than double from 20kwpm at end-2026E to ~50kwpm end-2027E vs prior estimate of 40kwpm. (See our ASE note <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed87&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjM3Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=3auZgngxB5NczXvN40g8hUJaAHT3_0OrLxHSAv7E68M> ). Overall, we estimate industry CoWoS capacity may rise from 160kwpm at end-2026 to 250kwpm by end-2027. 

Robust server CPU demand; Nvidia Rubin ramp to accelerate in H226 

On the demand side, we believe server CPU continues to show upside into 2027. ASE's faster CoWoS expansion should be underpinned by higher AMD Venice volumes, which we estimate at 4mn units in 2027, up from 1.3mn in 2026. AMD's CoWoS demand could grow 232% in 2027E with a strong ramp of Venice server CPU and MI450/455. We also lift Nvidia's Vera CPU units to 5.5mn units in 2027 from 1.6mn in 2026, implying 57% growth in Nvidia's CoWoS demand in 2027. Rubin GPU ramp was slower in Q226 due to redesigns, but we anticipate a steep pick up in H226 to reach 2.1mn for 2026. We forecast Google TPU chipset units to rise from 4.1mn in 2026 to 9.0mn in 2027, with MediaTek expected to support 4mn units of TPU v8t capacity. Amazon Trainium 3 demand is growing and we lift 2026/27E unit estimates to 1.8mn/2.8mn (from 1.7m/2.3m). See our CoWoS supply vs demand analysis in Figure 2-Figure 12. 

More diversified supply ahead, but TSMC should remain the largest player 

As previously noted <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed88&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjM4Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=1S6_XqvhUvFE9KtZ1dMqJFnakX1llY-Bx2u8kWoytc0> , we anticipate advanced packaging supply to become more diversified from 2027-28 onward. We see increasing opportunities for ASE and Amkor in H226/2027, mainly driven by server CPUs. Intel's EMIB-T is gaining traction, but we believe Intel may face resource and capacity constraints in 2028, and will likely prioritise internal products and Google/MediaTek's TPU v9 initially. Overall, we think TSMC's advanced packaging sales should sustain solid ~50% growth over the next five years on its leading market share, rising content through 3D stacking, and tech upgrades such as CoPoS and co-packaged optics. 

Stock recommendations; ASE/GPTC price target raised to NT$835/$5,000 

Along the semiconductor supply chain for cloud AI, our top picks are TSMC (the industry's leading cloud AI foundry), MediaTek (design services for Google TPU), and ASE (advanced packaging & testing). We estimate backend, including advanced packaging, to reach ~12%/15% of TSMC sales in 2026/27E, and our recent Q226 earnings preview <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed89&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjM5Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=-3kF-SqnABCq9z6VwHTgtDOMOZh1TmMmSIJD-WSh9kE> raised our sales and EPS estimates on stronger cloud AI demand. MediaTek is a Buy and a Key Call. We lift our ASE price target to NT$835 from NT$660 <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h798f8806,3b0d316,4be1ed8a&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYxOTIwMDIyJm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTgyMjQwJm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=lxVV3Cgc1oL1-HUBuWg60XA89-agFPIQK3A6DL65zUY> . Critical equipment suppliers for advanced packaging & testing could also benefit from the cloud AI ramp-up, and we like GPTC, Chroma, Hon Precision, and ASMPT. We raise our GPTC price target to NT$5,000 (from NT$4,000) based on 33x 2027-28E PE (vs 33x 2027E PE previously). See page 6. KYEC remains well positioned in the final test space. We like Aspeed for its strong BMC outlook, GUC for its robust Google CPU upside potential, and Alchip for its Amazon Trainium3 and Trainium4 opportunities.

Memory vs Memory Capex Beneficiaries



 

We have published our June Thematics <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13515993&ad=4538467075&h=HNIRvd9&sig=RuNsHfgl4FdPQYFzMHDkiuhPXOz&v=2&isig=HvvvoZIWDw9pPFcKcubIg5kFANX&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/-lko56u5/GPS-5353255-0.pdf/6f1d827c-76da-4bc3-b566-83c3877ea559>  note. Three key themes: 1) flows into global thematics; 2) SRI – focus on industrial policy; 3) Global Consumer (part 2). 

 

TRACKING FLOWS IN THEMATICS: We track flows into 16x Secular Equity Themes. The AUMs are relatively small ($500bn) but are rising fast (25% organic inflows in June, 2-2.5x the rate for broader US Equities). Over the past month, the Themes with the strongest inflows have been AI, Infrastructure and Quantum while those with weakest inflow have been Blockchain, Space and EV & Battery.

 



 

SECURITY & RESILIENCE INVESTING (“SRI”) – A FOCUS ON INDUSTRIAL POLICY: Government priorities will remain drivers of equity returns. We anticipate Physical AI becoming more salient in US vs China competition. EU is moving on 2 axes, specifically Tech Sovereignty and Protectionism, but unlikely to do anything bold. China will continue to emphasize self-sufficiency in core technologies, supply-chain resilience, and strategic buffers in food and energy. The next China tech giants will be in upstream equipment/materials, the wafer-fabrication “foundation,” domestically memory, advanced packaging & testing, and compute/chips. Other Asian Economies will fight for their edge (Korea & Japan) 

 

 

 

GLOBAL CONSUMER – PART 2:  Our key argument is that the global macro regime should shift back to recovery/expansion (from slowdown/stagflation) and should drive an inflection in Consumer Sentiment and related Equity market themes. The Consumer also benefits from attractive price relatives and low positioning. Give the lack of earnings momentum we would still say selective and favor names with at least one of the following characteristics:  a) target more resilient upper-end  consumer (given wealth effects); b) capture the shift to spending  on experiences; c) are exposed to regions with solid wealth and cyclical backdrops (US,  Korea, Taiwan); and d) stand to benefit from a substantial decrease in oil prices in 2H26. 

 



 

Fun Facts on AI Spillovers: Courts across the U.S. are now seeing a steady rise in filings that include made-up or inaccurate references produced by AI tools. These issues are showing up more often in certain states, especially where AI adoption is moving faster than review practices.  Looks similar to the growing use of American idioms by UK MPs.
