Relevant Alten, CAP – KPIT profit warning yesterday on weaker autos end market
Indian engineering services company KPIT yesterday downgraded its outlook for Q1 FY27 (June end) and the rest of the year citing a sudden drop in revenue in the last few weeks. The company stated that there is an expected decline of ~ 1% in USD reported revenues for Q1FY27 as compared to Q1FY26 (YoY) primarily due to sudden actions by some European OEMs triggered by their recent profit warnings/ adverse business outlook. This impact was not seen coming earlier and has been realized only in the recent weeks. (KPIT <https://www.bseindia.com/xml-data/corpfiling/AttachLive/bee7f0cf-3011-46be-b131-6409fc46b980.pdf> )
>>> BofA comment: While the customer is not named in the release, we note that BMW, which profit warned recently, is a KPIT customer. Both Alten and Capgemini are exposed to automotive clients in the engineering R&D space. 
 
SAP gives AI product oversight to CEO and COO in reshuffle
According to Bloomberg, SAP is divvying up responsibilities for its product and engineering functions in its second top-level reorganization this year, as Europe’s largest software company grapples with staying ahead of rising AI competition. SAP has decided to split the responsibilities of Chief Product Officer Muhammad Alam among existing executives as Alam prepares to leave the company in March, rather than name a new CPO with those duties. CEO Christian Klein will take over most of Alam’s teams, while COO Sebastian Steinhäuser will handle industrial AI. (Bloomberg) <https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-06-30/sap-distributes-ai-product-oversight-to-ceo-coo-in-reshuffle?srnd=phx-technology> 
>>> BofA comment: Head of Product and Engineering Muhammad Alam’s decision not to renew his contract post 2027 was announced back in March.

MORNING PICCOLO | Good start to the new half. Japan is the story today, everything in the AI supply chain is up at the same time - wafers, substrates, MLCCs, ABF. Sumco +11%, Ibiden +9%, Taiyo Yuden +15%. The US handed them a great boost overnight and then a wave of price target hikes on WFE names this morning kept it going. NKY is 30% above the 200DMA at this point, worth keeping in mind. Taiwan is very similar. TSMC +3% as people position for what could be a 70% gross margin print next quarter. The interesting move is probe cards - MPI, Winway, Gallant all up 10% - which fits with Fubon's July call on advanced packaging. Korea though is a different story. KOSPI -1.8%, SEC -4.3%, SK Hynix -2%, which is pretty strange given what Nasdaq and SOX did overnight. The reasons going around are a bit thin to be honest - NPS rebalancing starting today, a small dip in June DRAM export data, some unconfirmed post on X about a memory efficiency breakthrough. Foreigners have now sold for nine straight sessions. Power equip and defence are catching the rotation again - LS Elec +10%, HW Aero +10%. KOSDAQ at +1.4% , Jusung Eng +24% on the Samsung/SK Hynix capex story. China basically flat, HK closed for a holiday. India bounced back above 24,000 off the 50DMA, IT services a bit soft after KPIT flagged a weak outlook, autos doing well, MCX +5% on the Jefferies BUY initiation. Australia was all about banks - ANZ -3.6%, NAB -2.8% - and house prices just had their biggest monthly drop since 2022 which isn't helping sentiment there.

DATE: 2026-07-01 06:14:28 | SENDER: Pasquariello, Tony <tony.pasquariello@mail.marquee.gs.com> | SUBJECT: markets / macro :: observations on H1'26.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1. at the halfway mark, S&P has generated a total return of +10%. while that’s somewhat anticlimactic relative to the convexity of recent years -- and

1. at the halfway mark, S&P has generated a total return of +10%.  while that’s somewhat anticlimactic relative to the convexity of recent years -- and it lags equal-weight S&P (+12%) and small cap (+23%) -- the fact is +10% is very solid relative to the long arc of market history (and is stronger than the first half of last year). 

  

2. here’s another framing: if S&P closes the year over the 7530 level, that will mark FOUR consecutive years of double digit returns.  in the 68-year history of the index, that has only happened ONCE before (technically, it was five straight years -- from 1995 through 1999, of course).  

  

3. yes, some high profile stocks have sold off meaningfully from their respective highs.  with that said, consider this: beneath the surface of S&P, 44 stocks are up > 50% YTD (in contrast, only 6 are down > 50%).  in addition, 29 are up > 75% (none are down that much).  finally, 22 are up > 100% (as you would probably guess, none are down that much).  so, there have been some enormous moves within the index, which have clearly and heavily favored the right tail.   

  

4. the AI buildout is rapidly accelerating, which has clearly accrued to the immense benefit of the AI infrastructure providers, and is a theme that’s shot through this entire note.  consider these YTD returns of GS custom baskets: memory +250% ... data centers +115% ... AI semis +101%.  with that said, the market narrative hasn’t necessarily followed a straight line (the most recent development being tension between US frontier models and Chinese open-weight).  

  

5. a rich opportunity set doesn’t mean the ride has been easy.  again, trading is about navigating the path, and the downside gaps in March -- or the upside gaps in April -- bear witness to the degree of difficulty.  away from stocks, the macro landscape hasn’t been all that straightforward, given the swing in front end rates (from around 50 bps of expected cuts in 2026 to 37 bps of expected hikes), the dollar (from rampant bearishness in March to general bullishness today) and commodities (the SoH was closed for nearly four months, yet oil has given back most all of its rally).  

  

6. point-to-point, North Asian equity markets have stolen the show this year.  measured in total returns and local currency, here’s the very top of the H1’26 leaderboard: Korea (KOSPI) +102% ... Taiwan (TWSE) +62% ... Japan (NKY) +40%.  while each of these markets has a specific story to tell, the throughline is they all sit at the coalface of the AI infrastructure story.  for what it’s worth, note that Asia also commands the very bottom of the global leaderboard: India (NIFTY) -7% ... Hong Kong (HSI) -10% ... Indonesia (JCI) -33%.  

  

7. one additional point on Japan to underline: NKY rallied 37% in Q2, which is the single biggest rally in any given quarter in market history (data back to 1970).  

  

8. one additional point on Korea that I find interesting: for as good as the headline returns have been, this year has also seen five intraday trading halts, which is nearly half of the total halts from this entire century (thanks Matt Mason).  spot up / vol up, by any other name. 

  

9. a final point on Asia.  for a discussion of what happened in the first half and what we expect in the second half, this week’s podcast is with Tim Moe, who brings to bear 40 years of experience in the region: link <https://marquee.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fmarquee.gs.com%2Fresearch%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQL5byDr-pJNZaIkf7V6mo_UcS2cGRDdgm6_bAJs_31FQZGEyThIAAEAu0TRSie9qFD1JQi-x94EoiPAa6b-W-s5K0qjHG_WjDkBvg9ydQKGZat19JUS9eQxHvDCI3l4VwOzephdctUu_CyxAEWqGRr46VdgL49N-mTwC_djx8KD9fszSTHiY7jOrAB-CvL9BbfE6HMjag7WQlTz1pgZbu_ck5GxY10wPSV5RmZWnEZU2i55n1Bk5yqqsyY3dXbDCbm1KzlodJKzv5BHwIqUMwJ-vyqU-xCKMRctWcn0n5upIXkInlaGAAcb8IV_4SX2FlF0ApOON6HrHiqsOkR6XD6MRzeTV3ikEyPJNZNksv9_Ih6SyzYxqWakNAq7Z3yq2p88vcUeyWOgjA**%26id=%2Fs%2Fcontent%2Fmarkets%2F56286519-6dc4-4a31-b911-f3f1d3ee82de%3Fmq_utm_source=article%26mq_utm_medium=email%26mq_utm_content=emailBody%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1cf45357-0ea19c89-9359-4649-9bdb-13bafc4bf5b2-000000/A9qeAqTEoTZRZOkV6DHfZmdEZH-AdEvNMUv02BeAw1A=452> .  to summarize his views in one line: stronger-for-longer markets, but with an increase in volatility. 

  

10. what else stuck out in the first half?  I certainly didn’t see it coming, but small cap has performed masterfully, and is tracking for its largest annual outperformance over S&P since 2003.  ex-post, I chalk this up to a few factors: the cyclical growth environment (this is evident in several parts of the market, simply pull up a chart of CAT) ... some gearing towards biotech and select AI infrastructure beneficiaries (mostly the form of power and data center plays) ... as well as positioning (recall a record short base in RTY futures just one month ago).  

  

11. in an environment of high dispersion (and, thus, low correlation), the momentum factor continued to shine.  after a 48% rally in 2024 and a 30% rally in 2025, our flagship pair trade is up 57 YTD%.  without question, the perceived set of leaders and laggards from AI has been stimulative for this factor.  with all that said, I’d be remiss if I didn’t note that the realized volatility of this factor increased noticeably in the past few months, and that the fundamental community has plenty of leverage to it (link <https://marquee.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fmarquee.gs.com%2Fresearch%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQLEVMfWrw1h5HwNTt0oxvePV0-PTBANMmnxc0bAjHSvqj6EjhfNAAEAQ8rMLvKKokx1hs2OoBpqnwZt9uojiUWYPko5wO7uBqxX1hXK-qccklc1GDNBDpRPNUzCyMttqsPxuqlME9zbodu0BKeB36LvdtWUJ6MOSD6xJeS-TIHC6a0AQc65JYhEFs-xb8WeEEvvCiGrKJ1cS99zZgNBvPsVtvv7NaPa1U_13HGEyEuTOZVsJI_oK2fzFcbAxqnHi5_hx4-yF9K8pFmEmKoPzoIWL3w7C-5ix_Kx4z_12ScQ8cj3kkvtCWN080VCojaVze5KUYJ0FW8TdTWI6PWSgSr

DATE: 2026-07-01 06:15:04 | SENDER: EG Geo-technology <geo-technology@eurasiagroup.net> | SUBJECT: EG Geo-technology, EU: AI dependency draws Europe toward Washington despite tech sovereignty push
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Geo-technology, EU


01 Jul 2026 05:13 EDT

	  	 
 	
 	 
AI dependency draws Europe toward Washington despite tech sovereignty push

 	
 	 
 	 ________________________________

 	 
 	 
*	The Fable/Mythos shut-off highlighted Europe’s dependency on Washington for access to US frontier models, leaving it exposed to unpredictable White House decisions. 
*	The EU will remain far behind the US in total compute, and a megaproject to build an Anthropic-level lab is almost certainly politically and economically unfeasible. 
*	European leaders will seek to anchor model access guarantees in the transatlantic alliance— even as the bloc pursues tech sovereignty in parallel.

 	 
 	 ________________________________

 	 
 	 
European countries are now dependent on a volatile White House for access to frontier models (see note: Anthropic cut-off will boost tech sovereignty efforts abroad <https://library.eurasiagroup.net/go/wfpub_eurasia_26606_bfa35aab/wfpub_eurasia_26606_bfa35aab.html?token=dd305963-00b2-4e59-b92e-1bd3f80cc27c&extension=.html&click=15fc251c-f8a6-4c28-8606-31aab923c628> , 19 June 2026). The recent Fable/Mythos shut-off appeared to confirm a key prediction in Europe 2031 <https://europe2031.ai/summary/> , a viral essay laying out a scenario in which Europe is reduced to a vassal of the US due to AI. The paper was widely circulated in European tech circles and amongst officials. Shortly afterwards, reports emerged that the White House had struck a deal with OpenAI to vet access to its most advanced model, GPT-5.6.

This will further motivate Europe and other middle powers to find ways to ensure access to cutting-edge AI. At the G7, European leaders and AI CEOs pitched a US-led coalition for AI governance and a “trusted partner” scheme. But there was reportedly little enthusiasm from the US government. The European Commission is preparing an action plan to ensure that advanced AI cyber models are available in the EU, and help European industry defend against them. 

Some European policymakers nonetheless fear the cyber capabilities of the most advanced models such as Mythos could amount to a decisive strategic edge, analogous to nuclear weapons. If so, neither access agreements with Washington nor domestic “near-frontier” models may be good enough, leaving the EU with no alternative but to invest hundreds of billions of euros in AI chips and datacenters and its own frontier model. However, the EU is highly unlikely to pursue this “moonshot”.

Europe will not catch up in the compute race absent unprecedented new private sector investment. The centerpiece of Brussels’s AI strategy, the AI gigafactories, will not begin construction until next year, while their financing will depend on tense and already well-advanced negotiations over the next seven-year budget. But these will pale in comparison to the largest data centers under construction in the US and the Gulf. Building world-class AI clusters will therefore depend on attracting many more big-ticket private sector investments like Softbank’s €75 billion data center project in northern France, and upgrading the bloc’s energy grid (see note: Energy constraints will limit but not collapse Europe’s AI infrastructure growth <https://library.eurasiagroup.net/go/wfpub_eurasia_26704_107d2907/wfpub_eurasia_26704_107d2907.html?token=af720f04-ec50-48a9-be97-5055154101f5&extension=.html&click=15fc251c-f8a6-4c28-8606-31aab923c628> , 30 June 2026). 



A megaproject to build a European Anthropic or OpenAI is almost certainly out of reach. Besides the compute requirements, such an initiative would also require poaching elite researchers from around the world with sizeable compensation packages. No funds have been set aside for this, while the bloc must also finance other pressing priorities. The winner of the commission’s Frontier AI Grand Challenge, a consortium led by the Italian company Domyn, will build a model with more than 400 billion parameters, compared to 10 trillion for Mythos.

Brussels will instead focus on AI adoption, deregulation and industrial applications. President Ursula von der Leyen has met on multiple occasions with a group of leading European tech CEOs, who have emphasized deregulation, consolidation and completing the single market, with sovereignty a secondary concern. While these would improve competitiveness, it would not deliver frontier-level capabilities. Her new industrial AI advisor, Siemens Chairman Jim Hagemann Snabe, will issue recommendations in September. 

Mistral will remain Europe’s best asset for sovereign AI. Having focused on enterprise deployment over top-tier model development, it has fallen in global LLM rankings—but will release a powerful new model this summer, and is backed by major European tech players such as ASML. As the only top LLM-builder in Europe left standing following the acquisition of Aleph Alpha by Canada’s Cohere, the company will benefit from the uncertainty surrounding access to leading US offerings. 

While Chinese open-weight models such as Zhipu’s GLM 5.2 are a high-performing alternative for businesses concerned about access to US models, there is similarly no guarantee that future releases will also be freely available (see note: Zhipu's gains point to escalating competition and supply-chain decoupling <https://library.eurasiagroup.net/go/wfpub_eurasia_26674_2bc43336/wfpub_eurasia_26674_2bc43336.html?token=729830f2-91f9-4eac-92c0-63953c8e8cd1&extension=.html&click=15fc251c-f8a6-4c28-8606-31aab923c628> , 26 June 2026). Chinese foundation models are also likely not compliant with the EU AI Act, according to some EU officials, and significant questions remain open around their safety and security.

But if true sovereignty means having capabilities on par with the very best LLMs, Europe will fall short. Even Elon Musk and Mark Zuckerberg have failed to match Anthropic and OpenAI, despite their immense resources. A middle power coalition along t

Apple Inc.	●	(AAPL.O) Neutral	 	
UBS Evidence Lab Inside: iPhone purchase intent mixed as the US and Europe rise but China falls <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h79912267,3b41e15,4be20008&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYyMTM1ODI5Jm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTg2OTc0Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=u3WmalAp45CmDWbhm2Tn2kCXD9-slErlGCjyCKjCjpc>  	
Our latest survey results suggest that Apple Intelligence is not driving upgrade activity, consistent with our expectations. 


Read Report   > <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h79912267,3b41e15,4be20009&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYyMTM1ODI5Jm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTg2OTc1Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=TAiWgxTc3xhfTVIEjw52eEBZSDxQQ1ufilJefj-CT6g> 		
'12-month purchase intent' indicates solid interest in the US and Europe 

UBS Evidence Lab (> Access Dataset <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h79912267,3b41e15,4be2000a&e=ZGlkPUFDNy1FLTYyMTM1ODI5Jm9mZl9pZD1BQzctRS0xNTg5NTg2OTc2Jm1hPVk0Njc4NTM0OTQ5Nzg1QTQ1JmNhbXBfaWQ9RU06VU5LVzoyMDI2LTA3OjAxOkM&s=VfnPcBJGK3bHmFjY7hpzayATVS3oG-UUgcBUNxdLioQ> ) recently surveyed over 7,500 smartphone users in the U.S., U.K., China, Germany, and Japan to gauge smartphone demand. The key takeaways from the survey pertaining to Apple:

1.	12-month global iPhone purchase intent in the US rose ~300 bps YoY to ~20%, as China fell ~100 bps YoY to ~15%. The UK (+600 bps YoY) and Germany (+400 bps YoY) saw material increases as the change in Japan (+100 bps YoY) was more modest in our view.
2.	The average age of an iPhone in the user base downticked to ~22.9 months from last survey (-0.8 months HoH) but still near survey highs.
3.	Apple Intelligence is not driving upgrade activity as total respondents indicating that they would upgrade sooner for Apple Intelligence features declined to ~24% (-500 bps HoH) while those noting no impact on their purchasing decision rose to ~31% (+300 bps HoH). 
4.	Total 'net interest' (the delta between 'interested' and 'not interested') in an Apple foldable declined ~100 bps from the prior survey to ~39%, but the favorability spread over a foldable smartphone rose ~600 bps HoH. 

Apple foldable interest ticks lower but spread widens vs foldable smartphone 

As Apple is expected to launch a foldable iPhone at its annual September event, we highlight interest in both a foldable smartphone and a foldable specifically by Apple. 'Net interest' in a foldable smartphone notably declined ~600 bps HoH to (8)% in aggregate. While 'net interest' in an Apple foldable also declined (-100 bps HoH), we note that the favorability spread of a foldable specifically by Apple over a foldable smartphone widened by ~600 bps HoH to ~48%. We believe that the sentiment towards an Apple foldable is directionally positive for iPhone demand, particularly as AI features recently announced at WWDC26 are unlikely to be a material driver in our view. 

Our Sept-26 quarter and FY26 iPhone forecasts are unchanged 

We estimate Sept-26 quarter and FY26 iPhone rev / units of $56.0B / 55.1M (Consensus $55.3B / 57.9M) and $251.6B / 261.6M (Consensus $250.8B / 257.7M), respectively. 

Valuation: Our PT of $296 is 30x our CY27 EPS est of $9.86 

Our $296 price target is ~30x our CY27 EPS est of $9.86. At 30x, Apple shares would be trading roughly in line with the trailing 3-year average and a 1 turn discount to the trailing 12-month average, reflecting solid demand balanced by uncertainty around the company's AI strategy.

Market Colour

Software & Internet


Amazon (Neutral) / IT Services - AWS investing $1bn on FDEs
AWS is investing $1bn to launch a Forward Deployed Engineering (FDE) unit, embedding AI experts into enterprise client teams. This Palantir-style approach bypasses traditional consulting to co-develop agentic AI solutions in days, leaving clients with self-sufficient systems running natively in their AWS environments. This is a strategic land-grab to solve the "last-mile" AI deployment bottleneck. By directly engineering workflows on its own infrastructure, AMZN is locking in customer stickiness. This is an incrementally negative read for IT services, where their consulting businesses are increasingly competing in a more fragmented market, with many of those emerging competitors better positioned to help the end customer

Meta (Buy) - Judge denies bid to dismiss state AG child addiction lawsuit
A federal judge rejected Meta’s final attempt to toss a multi-state lawsuit alleging Facebook and Instagram intentionally addict teens and violate privacy laws, clearing the path for an August 18 trial. Despite the alarming headline, this regulatory overhang is largely background noise. We believe Meta’s overarching legal strategy remains completely unchanged: systematically settling bellwether cases - like the recent Kentucky school district settlement - to kick the can down the road and delay sweeping precedents. An out-of-court settlement in this impending California trial is highly probable; failing to settle would be the actual surprise. 

Meituan (n/r) - launches 1.6T parameter model trained entirely on Chinese silicon
Meituan’s launch of LongCat-2.0, a 1.6-trillion-parameter LLM trained and run entirely on domestic Chinese chips, marks a potentially critical milestone. This is the first model of this scale to achieve full training and inference without Nvidia hardware. Lots of things to consider here, but it seems clear to me the regulatory protectionism around chip/manufacturing IP is having the opposite effect vs what the politicians intended!

SAP (Buy): management responsibilities formally adjusted ahead of CPO departure
Bloomberg reports (here <https://specialistsales.cmail20.com/t/d-l-woedt-hjyuihouk-r/> ) that Chief Product Officer Muhammad Alam’s product and engineering responsibilities will be split between CEO Christian Klein and COO Sebastian Steinhauser and that an external search for a new product lead is ongoing. The company announced in March that Alam would not renew his three year contract when it expires in March 2027, for personal reasons, and that Klein would assume his responsibilities in the short term. This article effectively formalises the temporary reporting structure during an external search. The CPO role is important for the equity story because it includes oversight of AI product development, where SAP has lagged peers in direct AI monetisation – the calibre and background of an external hire will therefore be closely watched as a potential indicator of a shift in strategy. 

Datadog (Buy) - Acquires Adaptive ML 
The platform has acquired Adaptive ML, a Paris-based AI startup developed the world's first reinforcement learnings operations (RLOps), enabling enterprises to build and deploy their own agents based on open-source LLMs. The platform centres around long-term adaptability and continious learning; the founders had previously contributed to projects such as Falcon and BLOOM, holding R&D roles at Hugging Face. The team will join Datadog AI research, focusing on technical problems and collaborating with product & engineering teams to develop new capabilities. Deal terms remain undisclosed, with a reported $100m valuation in the seed round raised in 2024.


Tech Hardware


Semi-cycle Tracker
Smartphone users face higher handset prices as chip supply remains constrained into 2027.  ASICs and GPUs are ramping adoption of 2nm processes for their newest chips. Qualcomm (n/r) and MediaTek (n/r) reportedly shifted their smartphone chips to 2nm in 2026, after 3nm capacity became crowded with AI chips. This could lead to another leg of smartphone price increases going forward. RDBN View: We view that AI-driven demand has already increased prices across servers and PCs. However, the impact on end-market dollar revenue growth has been relatively modest. A separate data point worth flagging is that Taiwanese component maker Yageo (n/r) expects strong earnings this year, driven by its 50% revenue share from capacitor products. Wesfarmers Ltd. (WES.AX): Downgrade from Neutral to Sell on valuation 
	
1 July 2026 | 7:35PM AEST | Research | Equity 	
	
	
We downgrade WES from Neutral to Sell on valuation and a deteriorating risk reward. WES has significantly outperformed since 18th May +27% vs. the ASX200 +3%. We think this is partly on the back of the US market lead with HD +18%; BBY +31%; TGT +6%. We think the US retailer stock prices are reflecting a better consumer environment (lower gas prices, better retail spending, world cup driven enthusiasm) which is not the case in Australia (spending is slowing modestly, house prices are declining and petrol prices are set to increase). We are within 1-2% of consensus EPS across 2H26-FY28E but note recent tailwinds are moderating. FX has become less of a tailwind since mid-May (AUD/USD now 69c vs. 72c) and Lithium prices are moderating (also peeking in mid-May). WES now trades on ~34x GSE FY27E EPS vs the 10 year average 24x (or ~26x since COL demerger) and at close to a record premium to the ASX200. Our PT increases from $76 to $78 on higher market multiples; hence, with 14% downside we downgrade to Sell from Neutral.

DATE: 2026-07-01 07:02:29 | SENDER: Joseph Cardoso <joseph.cardoso@jpmresearchmail.com> | SUBJECT: JPM | Hardware & Networking | Data Center Watch: AI Demand Supported as LLM Usage and GPU Pricing Climb; Meanwhile, Memory Spot Prices Diverge
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
North America Equity Research 	

Hardware & Networking


Data Center Watch: AI Demand Supported as LLM Usage and GPU Pricing Climb; Meanwhile, Memory Spot Prices Diverge

 	 
By Joseph Cardoso AC <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13517126&ad=4539466625&h=ClBHs3Z&sig=ALluGD3dEg8zXcvtsYmJ9l7MhV6&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/N694339> , Manmohanpreet Singh <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13517126&ad=4539466625&h=K0nu8sZ&sig=5Is0P1cAjCzy8VQ9xfD7z9OTGDK&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/O756946> , Marc Vitenzon <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13517126&ad=4539466625&h=dr-lNzd&sig=L2gbuCmJTxYLNwFm7cjAAD7jIah&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/E964623> , Akanksh Chauhan <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13517126&ad=4539466625&h=w0yNEuf&sig=Kxb6sKTHzB9QAAifLfMSzVe2spP&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/F753427>  

Click here for the full document and disclaimers <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13517126&ad=4539466625&h=yMWeWn7&sig=OJctcP7YX0s7nBcbtD5DPxsh5xN&v=2&isig=H9HRL9drTkvSPiWueU6Nac1yOtG&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/-dakcbun/GPS-5353532-0/fd33fd8f-aef8-4584-a005-3175d0552b95> 

In the Data Center Watch report, we outline key data points relevant to AI infrastructure demand, including LLM token volumes and prices, GPU rental prices, and memory costs. Taken together, the latest data suggest positive trends for the AI infrastructure demand environment, including the expansion of LLM usage, which is more than offsetting year-on-year LLM token price declines, while GPU rental prices continue to grind higher month-on-month. Importantly, based on our sample and simplified assumptions, we estimate that token economics are directionally tracking favorably for model providers, even assuming conservative token prices. Meanwhile, DRAM prices continue to rise, albeit at a slower rate, while NAND spot prices have contracted modestly for three months in a row. Key highlights from Data Center Watch report: 

*	LLM trends re-accelerate on OpenRouter for the month of June. LLM trends on OpenRouter in June broadly re-accelerated, with token volume (+70% m/m, 20x y/y), pricing (up modestly m/m but still -5% y/y, with U.S. models bucking the trend by rising y/y), and spending (+70% m/m, 16x y/y) all increasing. Interestingly, while U.S.-based models lost volume share (35%), they dominated spend (85%+), with Anthropic’s Claude Opus 4.7 standing out as the only model ranking top five in both volume usage and spending. 
*	GPU rental prices rise across all tiers in the month of June. GPU rental price sequential growth continued across the board in June for non-hyperscaler capacity, with prices for all three tiers of Nvidia GPUs (A100, H100, B200) tracking higher m/m. A100s led the m/m gains, posting the steepest sequential increase among the three, while H100s and B200s expanded at a more measured pace. Pricing for B200s was ~2x that of H100s, and H100 pricing was ~1.7x that of A100s, with both ratios ticking marginally lower for the second month in a row. 
*	Memory prices remained elevated in the month of June but diverged, with DRAM and NAND moving in opposite directions. DRAM spot prices climbed sequentially again in June, a third straight monthly gain that puts it up more than 8x y/y, while NAND spot prices slipped modestly, a third consecutive small monthly decline after a strong 1Q26 run-up, yet still sitting over 5x higher y/y. 

  

LLM Token Tracker 


Our LLM Token Tracker captures a single week of usage and pricing data each month, providing a monthly snapshot or sampling of trends across ~300 LLMs listed on OpenRouter, an aggregation platform that routes API requests to models through a single endpoint. Keep in mind, OpenRouter skews towards developer, startup, and agentic-coding traffic and excludes first-party API volume (direct OpenAI/Anthropic, hyperscaler-hosted endpoints). 

Key takeaways: 

*	Token volume growth accelerated in the month of June, following a moderation in growth through the start of 2026. Token volume growth accelerated in June, expanding +70% m/m (vs. +33% in May and +5% in April) and 20x y/y (vs. 12x in May and 15x in April). By comparison, volumes for U.S.-based models (OpenAI, Anthropic, Google, xAI, etc.), which represent 35% of the total (vs. 46% in May and 56% in April), also saw growth accelerate in June, expanding +30% m/m (vs. +9% in May and +23% in April) and 8x y/y (vs. 6x in May and 10x in April). 
*	Token pricing continued to trend lower year-over-year into June, albeit more modestly than in recent months. While average token pricing rose +7% m/m in June (vs. +5% in May and +19% in April), year-over-year declines continued, albeit at a more moderate rate, tracking down -5% y/y (vs. -21% in May and -24% in April). We believe this moderation in the rate of decline was led by strong pricing trends for U.S.-based models, as evident in volume-weighted average pricing, which rose +27% m/m for U.S. models (vs. +19% in May and +10% in April) and +77% y/y (vs. +36% in May and +4% in April) vs. flat m/m for total models (vs. -8% in May and +15% in April) and -20% y/y (vs. -25% in May and -23% in April). 
*	Token spending also accelerated in June, following a moderation in growth over the past two months. Token spending growth accelerated in June, expanding +70% m/m (vs. +23% in May and +21% in April) and 16x y/y (vs. 9x in May and 12x in April). By comparison, spending for U.S.-based models, which represent 85%+ of the total (vs. 90% in May and 85% in April), also saw growth accelerate in June, expanding +65% m/m (vs. +30% in May and +35% in April) and 14x y/y (vs. 8x in May and 10x in April). 
*	Opus 4.7 ranks as a top five model across both usage and spending. The top five models in June based on token usage were: 1) DeepSeek V4 Flas

AI Engineer at Robotics Company Sees Experimental Phase in Data Strategies for Physical AI <https://research.alpha-sense.com?alertEventId=e3030d56-95ed-41a9-b092-a165f545f22d51444222350&documentId=EC-1000000-202836&source=email_alert&category=main_doc> 	
NVDA  •  Consultant  •  Expert Insight  •  2 pages  •  1 Jul 2026 	
Call Summary 

1.	The conversation covers the current landscape of data collection and training strategies for physical AI and robotics, focusing on the role and value of egocentric data, the structure of data pipelines, and the economics of data versus compute. The discussion also addresses the challenges and uncertainties facing data vendors and the evolving demand for diverse, high-quality datasets in the robotics industry.
2.	The expert is an AI Engineer with experience in learning-based approaches for autonomous robotic systems, including self-driving and humanoid robots, and has recently focused on vision-language-action (VLA) and world model-based approaches, as well as the data and infrastructure required to train and deploy these models at scale.
3.	The expert believes the field of data collection and training strategies for physical AI and robotics is still highly experimental and research-driven, with no clear, established best practices.
4.	They express skepticism about the long-term defensibility and value proposition of egocentric data vendors, citing the likelihood that major robotics companies will eventually collect their own data and the current oversupply relative to demand.
5.	The expert is uncertain about whether robotics will follow the same trajectory as LLMs in terms of generalization and the eventual need (or lack thereof) for post-training/fine-tuning, noting that the field has not yet reached the data scale required for such generalization.
6.	The data collection strategy for robotics is often conceptualized as a pyramid: large-scale, low-cost internet video (including egocentric data) at the bottom, mid-tier data with some hardware interaction (e.g., sensor gloves), and expensive, high-value teleoperation or RLHF data at the top.
7.	Egocentric video data has seen a surge in interest due to its scalability and its perceived role as the closest analog to internet-scale data for robotics, but the business of selling such data is challenged by low defensibility and oversupply.
8.	Data diversity, quality, and relevance to the target use case are critical factors for robotics model training; large, undiversified datasets (e.g., from a single geography or environment) are less valuable.
9.	Most robotics companies build their own custom data pipelines and annotation tools due to the bespoke nature of hardware and use cases, limiting the scalability of third-party data vendors.
10.	The majority of costs in building physical AI models are attributed to compute and engineering, with data acquisition costs being significantly lower in comparison.

United States: AI on Track to Define 2028 Election


Observatory View


*	Data centers have become the poster child of voter negativity directed at AI in the 2026 midterm campaigns, but our view is they are just the leading indicator for a growing anti-AI sentiment that will fuel the next wave of populism driving US politics, as it comes to symbolize concentrated wealth and economic strain for voters already feeling both.




*	Trump captured economic, trade, and immigration populism to win the White House twice. He found surface-level outlets for those grievances (tax cuts, tariffs, deportation) on the campaign trail that fired up voters with hope, but voter frustration with the status quo has persisted. AI is poised to magnify it. 




*	Proposals are surfacing to channel voter anger toward AI beyond data centers, but Washington has no clean mechanism to absorb it. The current administration views winning the race against China as existential, the US has not passed comprehensive technology legislation in three decades, and intraparty conflicts are emerging over how to respond.




*	We expect political resistance to US AI development to intensify beyond the data center fight, increasing friction along the way, but without slowing its development. AI is on the path to become the defining issue in the 2028 election — and right now, Democrats are better positioned to capture that backlash than Republicans.

­	 

AI politics expanding beyond data centers


*	Data centers are where the AI backlash is showing up first because they directly tie to voters' current grievance — affordability. It’s what makes data centers the first policy front, but the pushback is expanding.




*	The policy response is already moving past infrastructure. Senators Josh Hawley (R-MO) and Mark Warner (D-VA) have introduced legislation requiring quarterly employer disclosure of AI-driven layoffs to the Department of Labor — a direct response to job-loss fears that ignores data centers completely. 




*	Senator Bernie Sanders (I-VT) has moved on AI's economic concentration, none of it about data centers: a 5% wealth tax on billionaires and another bill to take a one-time 50% equity stake in major AI companies to fund direct payments to Americans.




*	On the right, Steve Bannon led 60+ Trump allies to petition the White House in May 2026 to require government vetting of AI before release, arguing the administration's hands-off approach leaves working Americans financing a technology that could devastate their jobs with no accountability and no stake in the upside. With Bannon running an organized campaign, it shows the fault line on AI is inside the Republican base, not just around its edges. 




*	Safety is the third front. Ninety percent of women over the age of 50 – a key voting demographic for either party – want national standards on AI and children. More than 20 states now have active chatbot-safety bills on top of multiple safety proposals in Congress.




*	Each of these developments stands apart from data centers entirely — signaling the political resistance toward AI is outgrowing where it began.


No easy fix to channel AI backlash – just like affordability


*	Just as no easy fix exists for affordability, none exists for AI either. Trump's economic, trade, and immigration platform gave voters hope it would solve their populist anger. AI policies offer more of the same: a political cudgel, not a solution.




*	The growing list of AI proposals is aimed at that same populist instinct — jobs, wages, wealth concentration — but none are on a path to tamp down the rising backlash for reasons both structural and political.




*	The US has not passed comprehensive technology legislation since the 1996 Telecommunications Act. Since then, there have been three decades of bipartisan agreement that social media, algorithmic power, and data privacy all need federal rules but have yielded no major legislation, just things around the edges to give policymakers political cover. Our view is nothing meaningful will materialize in the near term. AI inherits the 30-year track record of agreement on the tech problem without resolution.




*	Industry money has yet to manufacture resolution either, despite spending heavily to try. Pro-AI super PACs are projected to spend more than $300mn to the 2026 election cycle, but their policy priorities are misaligned. PACs, led by OpenAI, are pushing to preempt state-level AI regulation entirely; others, led by Anthropic, are fighting to preserve that approach. This is AI money against AI money, not resources closing the gap.




*	The administration's determination to win the race with China over responding to backlash at home, an industry too divided to push any outcome through, and policy proposals that serve more as rhetoric than action leave voter anger with nowhere to land other than the ballot box. That’s exactly the condition that keeps populist pressure compounding toward 2028.


AI to dominate 2028


*	Trump and Sanders both broke through in 2016 by capturing populist energy neither party's establishment could answer, fanning grievances about elites and “globalists” profiting while ordinary voters absorbed the cost. AI is the newest entry in that same pattern, not a standalone tech-backlash story. 




*	The narrative is shaping up to be the same: concentrated gains for a handful, diffuse costs for everyone else in the form of job losses, economic hardship, and unregulated risk to society at large.

Safra on Tenda: Takeaways from Alea’s site visit 

	
Rating: OUTPERFORM 		Target Price: BRL 46.00 	View Full Report <https://8n6lg8tm.r.sa-east-1.awstrack.me/L0/https:%2F%2Fapiext-bi.safra.com.br%2Fapl-api-download-documentos-rdv%2Fdocumento%2FPROSPECT-35746.PDF%3Fidu=124454/1/0103019f1d75d572-0c9ad12b-3bd0-4169-b5dc-503c75742542-000000/7NSG13HcCuIIkO8mBXgFinVkjME=258>  


On June 30, we attended a site visit to Alea's operations in Ribeirão Preto and Jardinópolis, with the company's top management, represented by Rodrigo Osmo (Tenda’s Co-CEO), Luiz Maurício Garcia (Tenda’s CFO), and André Massote (Alea's Operations Executive Director). Overall, we continue to see compelling long-term fundamentals on Alea. The subsidiary's significantly lower on-site labor intensity—21% of total unit cost versus 44% in traditional masonry—should prove a competitive advantage in an environment of labor scarcity, especially as labor wages has consistently outpaced inflation in materials for the past few years. While we acknowledge that cash breakeven is only expected in 2027 and the path to profitability may be gradual and with some hurdles, Alea's share of the company’s consolidated results should diminish over time as Tenda's core operation continues to grow, supporting our constructive view on the stock. Despite the 55% YTD rally, we continue to see its shares at an attractive 5.4x YE27 P/E.

Movers + Macro.

 

Equity futures lower this AM after a relatively quiet night / morning of market moving news, with the biggest headline being Anthropic’s Fable 5 being redeployed.

 

Asia memory names all lower overnight, European telcos trying to rebound after the recent weakness, while SAP and ASML are both up small.

 

With the 1H of ’26 in the books and the Nasdaq up ~20% and the S&P 500 up ~10%, below were the key contributors to the performance YTD, see further below for more stats / charts.

 

Most glaring to us in the below is that virtually 100% of the returns in the Nasdaq during the 1H of ‘26 have been driven by 10 stocks.

Pre-Market News.

 

Anthropic: Last night Anthropic noted <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518219&ad=4540295793&h=D5Lgp6C&sig=Rb2z1TgSB8mKzDd7SJwZzS0l8qb&v=2&url=https://x.com/AnthropicAI/status/2072163884430229756>  that their redeploying Fable 5 “with a new set of classifiers to target and block more cybersecurity tasks. In the near term, some routine tasks like coding and debugging will fall back to Opus 4.8.”

 

Autos: The FT noted <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518219&ad=4540295793&h=wO3GRZO&sig=QZ34kjPLF1xaI1OrCh1zB9y97Ly&v=2&url=https://www.ft.com/content/dc7b4dfb-b279-4740-ae71-862a9e267aa9?syn-25a6b1a6%3D1>  last night that Chinese carmakers are rushing to cut their dependence on foreign chips in an echo of how their dominance of battery technology gave them an upper hand in making electric vehicles.

 

DT Board Seats: Announced this AM that they are giving 2 seats to Starboard, this follows their letter <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518219&ad=4540295793&h=ru0nh8x&sig=UkTF8gTfg2dQqfaKTq6t1nHEv8d&v=2&url=https://www.starboardvalue.com/wp-content/uploads/Starboard_Value_LP_Letter_to_DT_Management_and_Board_04.28.2026.pdf>  to the company back in April of this year. DT also announced it’s holding an Investor Day following FQ2 earnings to outline its path to the “Rule of 50” in FY’29 and reiterated its intention to continue returning significant capital to shareholders under its $1B share repurchase authorization.

 

Memory Pricing: Trendforce notes <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518219&ad=4540295793&h=SM0Z5LD&sig=YwYJ6a4tmYfZrigUBzvCUBa3df0&v=2&url=https://www.trendforce.com/news/2026/07/01/insights-memory-spot-price-update-dram-spot-prices-see-gains-in-low-density-ddr4-and-ddr3-amid-sideways-market/>  that DRAM spot prices this week have seen upward momentum in LDDDR4 and DDR3 segments, while the broader market continues to trend sideways. In NAND Flash, suppliers are adjusting quotations to optimize inventory levels, but buyers remain reluctant to accept current pricing, with 512Gb TLC wafer spot prices continuing to decline.

 

   

 

MSFT Job Cuts: Last night Business Insider noted <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518219&ad=4540295793&h=GIYOWOU&sig=LdTe5mUCl6m6gJOF2oSOdcuKLZo&v=2&url=https://www.businessinsider.com/microsoft-job-cuts-layoffs-sales-consulting-2026-6>  that MSFT is planning to announce job cuts soon as they continue efforts to control costs. BI notes that “The cuts are expected to impact thousands of roles, including sales and consulting, in addition to jobs at the Xbox gaming division.”

 

TeraFab: Wccftech noted <https://jefferies.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518219&ad=4540295793&h=K7n_Y0V&sig=6eTRbCCSqSpC6VZsyCASQguXWcw&v=2&url=https://wccftech.com/musks-terafab-scores-18-year-intel-veteran-as-foundry-manager-for-55-billion-chip-manufacturing-project/>  last night that Terafab’s 1st major hire is Gary Jiang, an 18-year INTC veteran, where in his latest role he was a factory manager at INTC’s Arizona facility.

From Ranjan’s SE/GRAB/GOTO Q226 Earnings Previews <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13518269&ad=4540325718&h=5g2QUZy&sig=Q6f6eYUImAvPoOXIVGlMLFJj5zX&v=2&isig=9vPVrgFn0jLJi6potAh4xYkbA4G&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/-sit9hb3/GPS-5352365-0/ab72eece-5a18-41ee-b960-48089391f667> : “ASEAN internet stocks have been weak this year (SE: -27%, GRAB: -25%, GOTO:-22%, NASDAQ: +11%) due to worries about competition, macro impact, and the broader de-rating of internet stocks. In our view, GRAB’s 2Q26 could dispel many of the concerns with continued strong growth in on-demand GMV, market-share gains and stable margins. Any addition to the existing buyback program is likely to be positively received, given the stock is at a 2028E EV/EBITDA multiple of 8x. While we anticipate continued strong growth at Shopee, we believe margins are unlikely to inflect in 2Q26E. Given the Street’s focus on Shopee’s margins, we believe GRAB could perform better than SE with 2Q26 results. Taking a long-term view, we remain OW on both SE and GRAB as we believe the Street is underestimating the earnings potential of both platforms.” 

*	“GRAB – Market share gains likely to have continued into 2Q26. We anticipate mobility and delivery GMV growth of 18% and 20%, respectively. In our view, GRAB is outpacing industry growth and gaining market share, driven by its product-led initiatives and platform advantage. We believe that on-demand industry shows strong network effects which are benefitting GRAB. We forecast 2Q26E adj EBITDA of $160m (+47% yoy, +4% qoq). In our view, GRAB should comfortably meet its 2026 adj EBITDA guidance of $700-720m (JPMe: $715m) with upside risk arising from the potential easing of macro headwinds in the region. Our model does not yet incorporate the acquisition of Foodpanda Taiwan and consolidation of Superbank.” 
*	“SE – Shopee likely to deliver strong growth but margins yet to inflect. We forecast 26% yoy GMV growth for Shopee in 2Q26. However, with continued investments (e.g. VIP Program), we believe any margin improvement (2Q26E JPMe: 0.61% of GMV) is likely to be marginal despite the increases in take-rates. We anticipate continued growth in the fintech business with adj. EBITDA growing to $287m (+12% yoy, +4% qoq). Our growth expectations are driven by the growing credit portfolio, product suite and customers across SE’s geographies. We anticipate gaming to see a sharp decline in gross bookings by 21% qoq as 1Q26 benefited from content collaboration.” 
*	“GOTO – Top-line growth is likely to be modest. We forecast ODS GTV growth to remain modest at 3% qoq/yoy. Adj EBITDA for ODS could also see a sequential decline in 2Q/3Q26E vs 1Q26 due to changes in Indonesia's ride-hailing policies, including a reduct

Market Summary

• Maintain a constructive equity outlook for 2H26, supported by resilient economic growth, healthy consumer spending, easing inflation expectations, and a strong earnings backdrop, with any near-term volatility viewed as a buying opportunity.

• AI remains the dominant investment theme, with continued upside expected across hyperscalers, semiconductors, memory, data centers, power infrastructure, and industrial AI as enterprise adoption accelerates and capital spending remains robust.

• Broaden exposure beyond mega-cap AI leaders by adding healthcare, defense, power/grid infrastructure, industrial automation, and national security themes, while maintaining selective cyclical exposure.

• Consumer fundamentals remain strong, with record household cash balances and resilient spending supporting above-trend GDP growth and corporate earnings despite higher interest rates.

• Key risks to monitor include inflation and bond market volatility, geopolitical developments, AI positioning/crowding, and upcoming macro catalysts including labor market data, earnings season, and central bank decisions.

 

Macro & Market Outlook

• Constructive outlook for 2H26: Markets remain supported by resilient economic growth, easing inflation expectations, robust corporate earnings, and continued AI-driven capital investment despite elevated geopolitical and policy uncertainty.

• Near-term catalysts: Labor market data, July earnings season, inflation releases, Fed meetings, USMCA review, and geopolitical developments remain the key market drivers.

• Market backdrop remains favorable: Strong corporate fundamentals and healthy consumer balance sheets continue to offset higher rates and geopolitical risks.

 

AI & Technology

• AI investment cycle remains the dominant structural theme, with hyperscalers, semiconductors, memory, optical networking, power infrastructure, and data center equipment expected to remain primary beneficiaries.

• US export restrictions on advanced AI models were eased, improving global commercialization opportunities while reinforcing AI as a strategic national priority.

• Industrial AI consolidation is accelerating, highlighted by strategic acquisitions of AI/data platforms as companies seek to own industrial data layers required for enterprise AI deployment.

• Enterprise AI adoption continues to broaden across information services, professional services, finance and education sectors.

 

Consumer & Economy

• US consumer remains resilient, supported by record household cash balances, healthy corporate balance sheets, and continued consumption strength.

European equities are trading lower today, in a tight range following, yesterday's record close for the regional STOXX 600. The focus remains on cooling inflation prints.

Yields on 10-year US Treasuries are holding steady following their ~10bps move up yesterday to 4.47%. Front month Brent oil is back down to $72/bbl after its short-lived flare up yesterday. 

Broadening out across EM equities in 2H. EM equities have rallied strongly in 1H26, but the gains have been narrow and earnings-led, and concentrated in AI/tech, while the broader market has lagged. Looking ahead to 2H26, Sunil Koul remains constructive because forward EPS has risen faster than prices, leaving valuations lower despite the rally, as discussed in an overnight note, "EM Equities: 2H Outlook: Broadening Gains <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQIqCr0KtGc4NHedZKn8XOW5U7cEMhDJr53gHFWZjL7ZppDXeMf8AACw0jQkVUYVLVFRWoOeOPojaY3Etrggs6OPipGV8SI_X4fFP1BiqBMsIjPb6Ii4IlOf6QYAaTP9gdyFNwv3v3B5SOJHFMUOm8DpXbzk_MVM0KZxdgeKpNX_nJNxQlfM88lLLrSNqNCrP4Yel4X8qt__H6U_8JRKMn30-lXpiI4VyDawkmu_q_XpgNC4Gp3jokjrCu4Qy9YJUi56uY6jCQQSvxxqVkrtUREw_-Z8TV_qr2c*%26id=95526063-b5a2-4843-b526-1ccfa1598591%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1dab81de-74b16402-2f25-4dfb-94d2-fb648c8724ec-000000/-zAcSMXymaIPVMOFLpkATQCRqxq5Na2AAMGPLrhgCCg=452> ." With the US-Iran agreement reducing oil tail risks, look for a broader cyclical recovery, favoring oil importers such as India, Turkey, and Egypt, plus rate-sensitive markets like Brazil and South Africa. North Asia should continue to lead on memory-driven earnings, while our sector preference shifts toward Banks and Capital Goods and away from Energy and Internet.

PHARMA: VITAL SIGNS – JUNE EDITION <https://sales.cmail20.com/t/d-l-wozkk-dyiuuktjju-j/>  - We present the 26th edition of Rothschild & Co Redburn’s monthly publication, which provides a snapshot of where global biopharma is and where it is headed. Using a diverse range of data sources, we offer insights into what biopharma companies are doing today and tomorrow across multiple activities (be it R&D or M&A) and how those efforts are recognised, or not, by investors, with analysis in absolute terms and relative to their peers, other healthcare sectors and the rest of the market. This month, we look at probabilities of pipeline success, showing that the most popular areas may not be the easiest.

 

ALBEMARLE: EARNINGS HIGHER IN FY26, LOWER IN FY27 - Our view on FY26-27 earnings trajectory of ALB stands, but we see a more pronounced bullwhip effect. We see lithium prices falling from c$25/kg in Apr 2026 to c$15/kg by YE2026. The price impacts ALB’s top line w/ only a 1-quarter lag, while COGS impact of high spodumene prices comes w/ a 2-3-quarter lag. We thus see FY26 earnings disproportionately elevated (adj. EBITDA c$3bn, 5% above cons.) and FY27 earnings disproportionately depressed (adj. EBITDA c$1.4bn, 53% below cons.). We lower our PT from $188/sh to $170/sh, with a lower multiple attached to FY26 earnings. Our Q2 2026e adj. EBITDA est. is c$1bn, 34% above cons (high pricing, no spodumene COGS drag). At the current stock price ($135/sh), Q2 earnings could serve as a catalyst for a short-term outperformance.

 

BLOOM ENERGY: BROOKFIELD PARTNERSHIP EXPANDED TO $25B - After US close yesterday, Bloom announced the expansion of the strategic partnership with Brookfield to $25bn, as Brookfield increases its framework to finance power projects for AI infrastructure. This represents a fivefold expansion since the original $5bn partnership was announced ~9 months ago in Oct-25. We still have very little detail over the partnership details, but making an assumption that ~50% of the $25bn is upfront costs, this would imply 3.0-3.5GW of fuel cell capacity orders. No timings or project specifics were provided in the release. The stock was up 8% in aftermarket trading, having already been up 10% on the day with the whole space strong. These large partnerships with Brookfield and Oracle help build backlog and justify manufacturing expansion plans. It' is likely that Ceres Power (Buy) trades up today in response to another large order in the SOFC space, with the news highlighting the longer term potential as Ceres' partners grow and compete with Bloom in the growing SOFC market.

 

CROWDSTRIKE: STOCK SPLIT 4:1 – CRWD will execute a 4-for-1 stock split after market close today. With the stock trading circa $760 per share, can expect to be around $190-200 per share. CrowdStrike trades at 33x EV/sales 12months fwd (3x that of the cyber peer average) and 1% fcf yield.

 

DYNATRACE: ANNOUNCES BOARD APPOINTMENTS - The platform has announced the appointments of George Riedel and Dan Streetman to its board of directors, effectively immediately – this follow engagement with Starboard Value. Both carry security and IT operations pedigree, aligning closely with Dynatrace's narrative. Riedel possesses a strategy background, with deep public and private board chairmanship experience – with prior seats at Cerner and Xperi (n/r). Streetman has experience scaling go-to-market motions under private equity ownership. Notably, Dynatrace has also announced plans to hold an investor day following 2Q27 results, to outline its path to the "rule of 50" in FY29 – Dynatrace and Starboard intend to engage substantively in the coming months. Mr Connell has confirmed a commitment to refining their equity investor communications. An incremental positive for shareholders considering historic struggles regarding the stock's narrative - shares are +3% pre market.

DATE: 2026-07-01 09:48:49 | SENDER: Vital Knowledge <updates@vitalknowledge.net> | SUBJECT: Vital Knowledge: Meta follows SpaceX in shifting toward a hyperscaler/neocloud model
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://vitalknowledge.net/assets/images/resources//section1.png> 	
 <https://vitalknowledge.net/assets/images/resources//vertical_divider.png> INTRADAY COMMENTARY 	
Jul 01, 2026 8:47:32 AM EST 	
Meta follows SpaceX in shifting toward a hyperscaler/neocloud model 	

*	META (Meta) – according to a Bloomberg report <https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-07-01/meta-is-building-a-cloud-business-to-sell-excess-ai-compute>  this morning (at ~8:35amET), Meta is forming a new cloud business to sell computing capacity to external customers, entering a market currently dominated by Amazon (AWS), Microsoft (Azure), and Google (GCP). 
*	What bulls will say: Meta has been one of the heaviest spenders (in terms of capex/revenue) and many feared it was building way more capacity than it could ever use internally, so this external cloud business will help monetize all that infrastructure, bolstering revenue, margins, and cash flow. Since the industry in aggregate still seems to be capacity constrained, this Meta compute infrastructure will likely be quickly utilized by others.
*	What bears will say: the formation of an external cloud platform is a tacit admission from mgmt. that it overbuilt capacity and/or is falling short on its own internal AI model initiatives. Meta isn’t the first company to make this transition – SpaceX’s xAI also appears to be dialing back expectations for its internal AI tools (Grok and Cursor) and has started selling capacity to external customers (including Google and Anthropic). If Meta and SpaceX slow the pace of capacity additions over the coming months and quarters, it would deal blow to the pick-and-shovel providers capitalizing on the data center boom.
*	What we think: the Meta news is great for that company specifically, but negative for sentiment toward pick-and-shovel providers (and it could weigh on other hyperscalers/neocloud companies too).

Oil

 

Brent and WTI are trading lower and there are no major changes to the narrative.  Time spreads and physical markets have weakened as the Strait has partially opened with Russia crude oil exports at the highs and China’s purchases remaining well below pre-war levels.  Yesterday, the EIA monthly had U.S. production up by 216k/d sequentially to record levels, above where the weeklies were.   Refined product futures are higher this morning in the front which roles to the August delivery contract today – this is the bull case for oil at the moment, along with the risk that the U.S. and Iran can’t get a final deal done and spec positioning which is extremely light on the long side.   The WSJ had an article out last night that said, according to unnamed U.S. officials, that President Trump had decided against a broader military campaign and didn’t mind if negotiations drag beyond August 18 (60 days after the MOU).  President Trump said publicly that he could give Iran more time, “if they behaved.”  Vice President said yesterday that Tehran has not yet made the concessions to fully honor the MOU (not yet “behaved” in other words.)  He said that the administration has two options if Iran fails to honor the MOU, and “.both those options are the table.”

https://www.moneycontrol.com/world/deal-or-more-military-action-jd-vance-says-us-has-two-options-if-iran-backs-out-of-post-war-mou-article-13963574.html
Iran’s Deputy Foreign Minister is meeting with Qatari ministers today to discuss implementation of the MOU.  Jared Kushner and Steve Witfkoff met with mediators yesterday. 

Weekly API Crude Oil and Refined Products Inventories (according to Bloomberg) vs. Consensus for the DOEs

*	Gasoline -2.106 mm vs. -560k
*	Distillate +2.9 mm vs. +10K

*	The Kremlin confirmed yesterday that it’s in talks to import gasoline

President Z said today that Ukranine hit Russia’s Ufa refinery for the second time this week.

 

PJM News

 

There was a lot of noise out there yesterday regarding the IPPs with clients asking why the group suddenly sold off in the afternoon.  Yesterday, PJM held a closed at 2:30.   Bloomberg and reporters reported that they voted in favor of a proposal by the Data Center coalition and regulated utilities to procure power through the “backstop” auction. Bloomberg reported, “Proposal includes a “subscription based” procurement target that recognizes the benefit of data centers securing bilateral contracts for power generation.”  None of the other proposals passed, including a curtailment proposal.  Yesterday, several clients sent me a letter from most of the governors of PJM states to PJM asking that PJM adopt curtailment requirement for large loads that weren’t buying from new build generation.  Curtailment may be a part of the solution, but nothing has been decided yet.
https://blinks.bloomberg.com/news/stories/THGMKET96OSH

https://www.reuters.com/legal/litigation/biggest-us-power-grid-pjm-vote-managing-data-center-demand-2026-06-30/

 

I had the opportunity to sit in at a dinner last night with a former FERC Commissioner hosted by Nick Campanella and Betty Jiang with a small group of clients.  There were some interesting elements of the discussion, but to me the primary takeaway is that although she thought the recent FERC orders were a positive step, the regulatory process is incredibly complex and variable in the RTO regions, and until there is regulatory clarity, large loads may continue to migrate to BYOG and regions were stuff can get done fastest like TX, GA etc.  Nothing earthshaking here.  I’m happy to discuss.  

 

META News

META announced that it’s looking at building a cloud business to sell excess AI computing power and models. The fact that they have excess computing power or think that they will have excess capacity may raise a few eyebrows.   META is the only one of the big companies that doesn’t have a cloud business and id could be a diversification strategy into a very good business.  These companies need to generate a return on investment for the spend they’re making (I think?) and this helps in that regard.  They are not deffering projects, but investors could start thinking more about long term investment growth plans.  Feedback here is most welcome.

 

Company News

 

VST is selling 3 “conventional” power plants with a combined capacity of 752 MW to Winslow Power.  The assets are the 541 Casco Bay combined cycle facility in Veazie, ME, the 108 dual fuel combustion turbine facility in Croghan, NY and the 103 MW dual fuel combustion turbine plant in Sovay, NY.   The press release came from the buyers and had no mention of asset prices.  VST also announced an expansion of its revolver from $3.44 B to $5.50 B.

DATE: 2026-07-01 10:40:04 | SENDER: Hu, Kenny (Citi) <kenny.x.hu@investmentresearch.citi.com> | SUBJECT: Coal inventory at Indian IPPs down 28% y/y, biggest 3 month drop, 16 days of use end-June’26 close to average
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
While the market has well noted the unusual volatility between Chinese domestic and seaborne coal prices due to the power crisis in China in summer of ‘21 and geopolitics in Europe last year, the big (and unseasonal) drawdowns in coal inventories in India went relatively underappreciated and was a contributory factor to the strength in seaborne coal prices in ’22–‘23. At end-Jun’26, Indian inventories were 41.8mn, lower than the peak above 58.1mn tonnes in Jun’25. Inventories have come down by 13.5mn tonnes in the last three months, the biggest three-month drop and exceeding the 11.2mn tonnes drop over Jun–Aug’20 during the pandemic lockdowns. They were down 28% y/y and 11% m/m in June (compared with average seasonality of 4% m/m decrease during the month). Inventories are now at 14 days of use (vs long-term average of 13 days), down from a peak of 19 days in March. 
 	
Viewpoint | Citi Research 	
Global Metals & Mining 
Coal inventory at Indian IPPs down 28% y/y, biggest 3-month drop; 16 days of use end-June’26 close to average 
CITI'S TAKE 

While the market has well noted the unusual volatility between Chinese domestic and seaborne coal prices due to the power crisis in China in summer of ‘21 and geopolitics in Europe last year, the big (and unseasonal) drawdowns in coal inventories in India went relatively underappreciated and was a contributory factor to the strength in seaborne coal prices in ’22–‘23. At end-Jun’26, Indian inventories were 41.8mn, lower than the peak above 58.1mn tonnes in Jun’25. Inventories have come down by 13.5mn tonnes in the last three months, the biggest three-month drop and exceeding the 11.2mn tonnes drop over Jun–Aug’20 during the pandemic lockdowns. They were down 28% y/y and 11% m/m in June (compared with average seasonality of 4% m/m decrease during the month). Inventories are now at 14 days of use (vs long-term average of 13 days), down from a peak of 19 days in March.

Read Full Report <https://www.citivelocity.com/rendition/eppublic/documentService/dXNlcl9pZD1vOFkxVHA2RHVCTDU3dVNPeXJieFJfdkc3dW1VSWFOdiZlbWFpbF9zZW5kX2lkPTQxMzg1NTkzODAmdj0x/Y2xpZW50U3lzdGVtSWQ9UkRFX0ZBVkUmYmxhc3RLZXk9MTI2NjQ4ODMmRU5BQkxFX1JFTkRJVElPTl9JRlJBTUVfUEVSU09OQUxJWkFUSU9OPU4mZG9jX2lkPTMwNDQwNTM1JnBsYXRmb3JtPTg0JmNsaWVudEJsYXN0SWQ9MzA0NDA1MzU> 	
India is often an underappreciated factor in global seaborne coal markets — While the focus of the coal market usually is on China, India is close behind as one of the top 3 importers of both coking coal and thermal coal (c.15–17% share of global seaborne demand for both)

Coal inventories at Indian power plants down 18% y/y as of end-Jun’26 — Inventories at Indian IPPs typically rise during Nov–Apr and draw down in the subsequent six months. Inventories declined by 33% during Apr’24–Oct’24 but has since increased by 62% to its peak in and are now down 28% y/y.

June-end inventories down 11% m/m vs average seasonality of down 4% m/m — Inventories normally come down in June (by an average of 4% m/m over the last decade), and hence the down 11% m/m in June’26 is greater than normal seasonality. 

Absolute level of inventories coming down — The demand weakness due to lockdowns took inventories to 50.7mn tonnes at end-Apr’20, then an all-time high. More recently, inventories peaked at 58.2mn tonnes in June’25 and have since come down to 41.8mn tonnes by end-June’26.

Inventories only marginally above average levels in terms of days of use — 41.8 mn tonnes of inventories at power plants translate to 14 days of burn at the power plants, higher than the 13 days of burn over the last decade, having come down from the peak of 31 days of burn in Apr’20. The 21 days of use at end-Jun’25 is also the highest since Dec’20. The lowest level in the last decade was 5 days of burn during the “coal crisis” of Sep–Oct'14.

	
Coal inventory at Indian IPPs (mn tonnes)
 <https://www.citivelocity.com/rendition/eppublic/documentService/dXNlcl9pZD1vOFkxVHA2RHVCTDU3dVNPeXJieFJfdkc3dW1VSWFOdiZlbWFpbF9zZW5kX2lkPTQxMzg1NTkzODAmdj0x/Y2xpZW50U3lzdGVtSWQ9UkRFX0ZBVkUmYmxhc3RLZXk9MTI2NjQ4ODMmRU5BQkxFX1JFTkRJVElPTl9JRlJBTUVfUEVSU09OQUxJWkFUSU9OPU4mYW5jaG9yPW1zd29yZC01NDA2NmZmZC05OGM2LTRkMjAtOGJkOC01NjBlZDZmZTcwNTQtZGI1OTg5NzAtNjc0ZC00OThlLTkyNzEtZjEwYjlhMDNlMDIwJmRvY19pZD0zMDQ0MDUzNSZwbGF0Zm9ybT04NCZjbGllbnRCbGFzdElkPTMwNDQwNTM1>

MediaTek (2454.TW): Stronger AI ASIC momentum to reshape earnings growth trajectory; reiterate Buy with TP up to NT$6,800 
	
1 July 2026 | 9:47PM CST | Research | Equity 	
	
	
We now see much stronger AI ASIC momentum at MediaTek beginning in 2027, and we are raising our AI ASIC revenue to US$20.3bn (vs. US$12.3bn previously), accounting for 49% of its total revenue in 2027E. Our forecast is significantly higher than the company's high end guidance of US$12bn as we see a stronger demand upward revision from customer over the past 2 months. For 2028, we also tweak up our AI ASIC revenue to US$52.5bn (from US$48bn previously), accounting for 69% of total revenue, as we expect to see incremental shipment units from the current project, on top of the next-gen project.

We are also factoring in a 5% price hike for MediaTek starting 3Q26. The increase mainly reflects the rising cost along the supply chain. However, as the adjustment is intended to cover cost inflation, we expect MediaTek's GM to remain largely steady at the current level. 

Net net, we are now modeling MediaTek’s 2027-28E revenue to grow by 95%/83% YoY (vs. 61%/111% previously) with OpM expanding to 25%/33% (vs. 15% in 2026E), and EPS of NT$181.92/NT$422.17 in 2027/28E. We raise our 12m TP to NT$6,800 from NT$5,000 (still based on 25x 2H27-1H28E EPS). With 57% implied upside, we reiterate our Buy rating on MediaTek.

Discussion Topics

	*	Retail Media?

*	MELI’s Ad Tech Initiatives: Data? How strong is MELI’s data advantage today? Where is it differentiated, and where does it still need to improve?
*	MELI’s Ad Tech Initiatives: AI & Automation? How is MELI applying AI across bidding, targeting, and campaign management? Are these tools improving outcomes yet?
*	MELI’s Ad Tech Initiatives: Self-Serve & Platform Scalability? What progress has MELI made on self-serve tools? Are you seeing improvements in adoption, and what friction still exists?
*	MELI’s Ad Tech Initiatives: Geographical Reach? Where is MELI seeing the most traction for ads today? Is growth still concentrated in core markets?
*	MELI’s Ad Tech Initiatives: Next Steps? If he were running MELI’s ad business, what would you focus on next? What are the key unlocks from here?

RESEARCH:

CRCL <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519530&ad=4541082814&h=yKGX8Pc&sig=Z3SFqd3Qt1b283BM8sVZMPxsT0g&v=2&url=https://www.bernsteinresearch.com/brweb/ViewResearchStreamer.aspx?cid%3DDKAYWQ0WKvdwFVRHPFP8ZdUd160F8xqXHDD7VGzceSzkytHL51wQRh951F22ifgP>  - Gautam Chhugani sees Open USD as further validation for stablecoin going mainstream... OUSD is credible, but no change to his l-term thesis on CRCL (already has scale, liquidity and distribution). The 17.5% selloff following the Open USD announcement is well understood, but Gautam sees it as additional validation that stablecoins are entering the financial mainstream. While Open USD's consortium of 140+ partners across payments, financial services, tech, and crypto represents the first credible challenger to the Circle/Tether duopoly, stablecoins remain a network-effects and liquidity business where incumbency matters. Circle and Tether have spent years building liquidity, trust, distribution, and partner integrations, advantages that are difficult to replicate even with a powerful founding consortium. Open USD likely increases both the long-term TAM and competitive intensity, but the announcement is ultimately a sign of the category's growing strategic importance rather than evidence that Circle's position is suddenly impaired.

 

Payments (OUSD) <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519530&ad=4541082814&h=7FpW5CW&sig=KxlwA3x1pe9qVZNUms52Y9IaRei&v=2&url=https://www.bernsteinresearch.com/brweb/ViewResearchStreamer.aspx?cid%3DdsAJSQ%25252bFzwu78tNf5BTVBkUFcYWpOmYOfGFIbRSpFysTEGBsmZvkNP9NCfsSCKNC>  - Harshita Rawat says Open USD announcement highlights a growing battle over stablecoin economics and governance. The effort is backed by Visa, Mastercard, Amex, Stripe, Coinbase, BlackRock and 100+ partners, though notably absent are JPM, BofA, Citi, PayPal and incumbent stablecoin issuers. She views stablecoins primarily as settlement rails rather than payment products, with the biggest opportunities in treasury management, cross-border payments/transfers and financial infrastructure modernization. Harshita pointed to Google as a potential AI/agentic commerce angle and Stripe as a potential infrastructure winner. The key question is whether 100+ partners can align on governance, economics, and distribution. Despite those uncertainties, Harshita remains bullish on Visa, arguing stablecoins are more likely to enhance than disrupt the card networks' position. Across her conversations with investors it seems there is strong interest to own Visa.

 

Datacenters & Neoclouds <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519530&ad=4541082814&h=-_CJRmb&sig=AVOwWTOhV33qBn5wFEYpj5wWlTK&v=2&url=https://www.bernsteinresearch.com/brweb/ViewResearchStreamer.aspx?cid%3DKyhe%25252bXDn4M2JeyIijDGs36IfykbC4NH2sTME3R64VYlN2%25252fI%25252fYK0QOXk3X3IPKzre>  – Madison & Gautam build on their $/MW analysis note <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519530&ad=4541082814&h=-_CJRmb&sig=AVOwWTOhV33qBn5wFEYpj5wWlTK&v=2&url=https://www.bernsteinresearch.com/brweb/ViewResearchStreamer.aspx?cid%3DKyhe%25252bXDn4M2JeyIijDGs36IfykbC4NH2sTME3R64VYlN2%25252fI%25252fYK0QOXk3X3IPKzre>  to unpack margins and unit economics. The traditional data center REITs (EQIX, DLR, CoreSite), neoclouds (CRWV, NBIS, IREN), and Emerging AI Infra providers (CIFR, WULF, CORZ, RIOT) are situated at different locations in the ecosystem, but trying to solve a similar problem: enabling compute for AI (and non-AI) workloads. In this note, we walk through five major comparisons across this company set: operating margin, revenue yield, financing, capex, and risk profiles. Within emerging AI Infra, CIFR and WULF stand out with strong leasing margins, declining cost of funds and hyperscaler counterparties. Within Cloud names, IREN demonstrates strong margins due to vertically integrated landlord economics, but is behind on scale and building an enterprise business (relative to CRWV and other clouds). We are also constructive on the colocation REITs, which offer a compelling combination of strong credit-quality counterparties, contractual revenue visibility, and moderate capex intensity.

 

NKE <https://bernstein.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519530&ad=4541082814&h=Gz_5NNC&sig=V92EfPDWaipKmJXIhdUH30br7AU&v=2&url=https://www.be
