DATE: 2026-07-01 11:11:43 | SENDER: Gokul Hariharan <gokul.hariharan@jpmresearchmail.com> | SUBJECT: MediaTek Inc.: Addressing Key Investor Questions
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Asia Pacific Equity Research 	

Hi Felipe,


MediaTek Inc.


Addressing Key Investor Questions

 	 
By Gokul Hariharan AC <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=_RmhlU0&sig=C932lidatqzMfHCIadOoXJKQSLG&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/U315071> , Jennifer Hsieh <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=4TSKviV&sig=SveX5jPDzlo2EaodQLL4lRuuB4S&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/V768229> , David Chou <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=YYIqW1y&sig=Xg6Me5xrX1qgYdWf8MfREDd680z&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/E950102> , Jason Chen <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=aQ1khGi&sig=SgzNoKIx0kfe1s1g7SJUXueH8w6&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/N801118> , Subham Singhania <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=sazfa5u&sig=M3FboU9YbsZ93kORP5uhFdFekmI&v=2&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/analyst/E878020>  

Click here for the full document and disclaimers <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=025g769&sig=VkWoReeIjOMK4sq4z1qSo7VhqZN&v=2&isig=T1rWNggzEqAdgJlmCQpianbIdaW&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/7ugrbmiv/GPS-5354216-0/8988d5fe-e16b-420b-bedf-229b801d3347> 

Overweight	 
2454.TW, 2454 TT	 
Price (01 Jul 26):NT$4,335.00	 
Price Target (Jun-27):NT$5,300.00	 
	

1.	TPU v8t (Zebrafish) ramping up on track, with potential for upside to 2027 revenue guidance: We believe TPU v8t is on track for a volume ramp-up in 4Q26, supporting the company's target of US$2bn in ASIC revenue (or 400-500k unit shipments) this year. For 2027, management has guided to US$7-12bn in ASIC revenue (implying 10–15% share of a US$70–80bn ASIC market), underpinned by strong customer demand and confidence in material availability. We have seen Google TPU demand skewing toward our previous bull-case scenario and have revised up our TPU estimates in May (now forecasting 8mn market TPU shipments in 2027 vs. 5mn units expected six months ago (latest CoWoS report <https://jpmorgan.email.streetcontxt.net/platform/al?a=13519653&ad=4541188886&h=nvtAA2A&sig=ZmZqGKSpzhJE0jgCuxjqjDovLu5&v=2&isig=SZat2Y9SJDgbWjnbyCykdpQP5QB&url=https://markets.jpmorgan.com/research/email/scx/sa7ft16j/GPS-5305898-0/8988d5fe-e16b-420b-bedf-229b801d3347> )). However, we still see upside to our current MediaTek enterprise ASIC revenue estimate of US$10.8bn in 2027 (~2.5mn TPU v8t units, ~30% share of 8mn total TPU shipments), with further upside beyond US$12bn achievable if MediaTek can secure additional substrate and 3nm wafer capacity. 
2.	TPU v9 Humufish design status on track to tape out in the next 2-3 quarters, market share likely to skew to the upside, given challenges with competitor program: We believe TPU v9 (Humufish) is on track to tape out in late 2026-early 2027, with revenue contribution starting in late 2027 or early 2028. We believe that v9 Humufish ASP should be 2-3x that of v8t (US$12k+ vs. ~US$4.3k), reflecting significantly greater design complexity (4 N2 compute dies, 4 I/O dies, and 4 memory I/O dies vs. 1 N3 compute die and 1 I/O die in v8t). Meanwhile, our supply chain checks continue to indicate that the key competing project (Pumafish) from US Fabless competitor has been either canceled or postponed, creating an opportunity for MediaTek to gain share in 2028-29. While we do not expect the competitor to be entirely absent - likely launching Sunfish v8i variant with 4 N3 based compute dies - we still expect MediaTek to benefit from an earlier mass‑production timeline (tape‑out at least 1-2 quarters ahead of peers’ v9). We are currently expecting ~2M units for Humufish v9 units in 2028, but do expect further upside, depending on Intel EMIB-T packaging yield progress. Our recent research indicates an extension of v9 Humufish (called Triggerfish), with specific design changes (including more SRAM and potentially a controller die within the package) to extend Humufish to accommodate inference needs as well. This could also result in upside to Mediatek’s TPU v9 family shipment expectations in 2028-29. 
3.	TPUv10 RFQ in progress, engagement model similar to v9, confident of securing a key project: MediaTek is currently engaged in the TPU v10 RFQ process, based on our checks, with results expected in the coming months. We see a high probability of MediaTek securing at least one TPU v10 (Icefish) project, with Broadcom supporting another v10 project. While there is some discussion around additional v10 variants—potentially including a full CoT model—our checks indicate that GOOG is still embracing a semi-COT model for the v10 family. Key IP that Mediatek is providing in the v10 generation would be 448 G High Speed electrical SERDES, die-to-die interconnect and experience in 3D packaging – we still do not see Google embracing CPO for its TPU projects in the v10 generation. We do see the possibility of further accelerator variants in the v9 family, including a fast-inference chip likely awarded to Marvell (SRAM based inference, codenamed Merope), as Google’s Compute program expands in scope and attempts to match workloads with specific ASICs. 
4.	More progress on new customer RFQs; increased rack-level design from smaller customers; Tesla most likely in the next 1-2 quarters: We believe MediaTek is in RFQ discussions with several hyperscalers (we believe Tesla, Meta, and Microsoft, etc.). While all are still in RFQ stage, we see the best chance of a win at Tesla, given its need for more front‑end design support, which aligns with MediaTek's strengths. While any win would not contribute revenue before late 2028-2029, confirmation would be positive for sentiment as it demonstrates diversification away from a single large customer. DATE: 2026-07-01 11:19:24 | SENDER: Iuri Honda </O=EXCHANGELABS/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE GROUP (FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=018BE688C91B4C4BA27E48FCBF07183F-82A2C364-40> | SUBJECT: ECB Forum on Central Banking 2026 - Resumo e transcrição (01/07)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ECB Forum on Central Banking 2026 (01/07)

 

Warsh (Fed)

Stance e price stability

*	Rejeita conforto com inflação acima da meta: quem esperasse tolerância acima de 2% "would be disappointed. We're going to deliver price stability in the US."
*	Reporta melhora nas expectativas no início do mandato: "Inflation risks have come down" e "expectations of inflation... they've come down."
*	Descreve o quadro do último comunicado sem atualizá-lo: "labor markets are steady" e "the demand side of the economy was solid."
*	Situa a independência como restrição vinculante: "No matter what the President wants... we've been an independent central bank for a very long time."

AI, capex e produtividade como eixo do outlook

*	Lê AI primeiro como choque de demanda via investimento: "the AI shock is leading to a boom in capital expenditures. We see that first and foremost in demand."
*	Expansão de oferta é esperada, não confirmada, e o juízo inflacionário fica reservado: "I'm confident we're going to see it in supply at some point" e "it's up to the Central Bank to decide whether it's inflationary."
*	Ancora o otimismo em produtividade já observada, majoritariamente anterior à AI: "structural productivity is in the high two % range", "potential growth looks like it's trended up" e "hours worked are relatively flat."
*	Separa diagnóstico de decisão: "does that optimism convey into policy in the next six or nine months? Still too soon to say."
*	Sobre emprego, invoca lump of labor fallacy e estágio inicial: "first or second inning of this revolution", com o "timing" como variável central sob dual mandate.

Balance sheet (6.7tn)

*	Subordina o balanço aos juros como instrumento primário: taxas "should be the dominant means through which we make monetary policy."
*	Descreve o canal de transmissão do balanço: "the balance sheet works mostly through asset prices... through signaling effects."
*	Qualifica o balanço grande como quase fiscal: "in my biased view, borders on fiscal policy."
*	Condiciona a redução à compreensão prévia dos mercados e a um horizonte longo: "will not be implemented until financial markets have come to understand" e "it'll take us more than 18 weeks."

Comunicação, reaction function e dados

*	Argumenta que os mercados já leem a função de reação, dispensando mais guidance: "volatility's not up, it's down... yields aren't up, they're down... inflation expectations are down."
*	Agenda de dados real-time como resposta a mismeasurement oficial: aspiração de captar a economia "in a contemporaneous real-time way", reduzindo dependência de dados "with mismeasurement problems."

 

Lagarde (ECB)

Reaction function e decisão sob choque de oferta

*	Decisão apresentada como resposta direta ao choque, não a um nível de inflação isolado: "in the context of a supply shock that led us to the decision that we made."
*	Função de reação com quatro insumos formais: "inflation outlook, balance of risk, underlying inflation, transmission of monetary policy."
*	Balanço de riscos reponderado, com risco agora incorporado à própria avaliação de inflação: riscos "to the upside on inflation and to the downside of growth are probably more broadly balanced than they were a few weeks ago."
*	Reequilíbrio atribuído à velocidade do movimento de energia: "$72 a barrel now when it was 120 back in March."
*	Cenários como método de robustez da decisão, não como mero exercício: "milder, severe, and adverse scenario to make sure that our decisions are solid and robust across scenarios."

Rejeição de stagflation via mercado de trabalho

*	Recusa do enquadramento com base estrutural, não conjuntural: "stagflation is a concept of the 70s in circumstances that are not replicated."
*	Ancora a recusa no estado do emprego: "almost lowest historical levels of unemployment" e "employment participation continues growing."
*	Compromisso apresentado como reativo e já em curso: "We will take the necessary steps and we have."

AI como choque de produtividade a mensurar

*	Trata AI como objeto de mensuração de política, não como narrativa: "we need to measure the disinflationary, inflationary impact it will have over the course of time."
*	Assume incerteza sobre a ordem do impacto: "it might be disinflationary first and inflationary second, or probably more so the other way around."
*	Enquadra a dependência UE-EUA como estrutural, limitando a leitura de simples atraso europeu: "When Europe represent 25% of the revenues... we depend on each other."

Estabilidade financeira e cautela regulatória

*	Alerta contra simplificação que desloque risco: preocupação com risco que "have moved and traveled afar through different structures, bodies and different names."
*	Reafirma o princípio de alocação de risco: quem toma o risco deve arcar com a responsabilidade correspondente.
*	Levers de crescimento situados fora da política monetária: "Capital market union. 28th regime and boost the venture capital."

 

Bailey (BoE)

Stance e transmissão

*	Justifica o hold pela atividade, não pela inflação corrente: "a softening economy... a softening labor market... a bit of an output gap opening up."
*	Data a fraqueza como anterior ao choque: "we had that before the hostility broke out in the Gulf."
*	Mantém convicção de convergência à meta apesar do desvio: "I was very much of the view that we were going to have inflation back at the 2.0 target... in the late spring."
*	Trata a retirada do easing precificado como aperto efetivo: "the mortgage rate went up 1%. So you can argue that we've actually tightened policy."
*	Distingue a dinâmica britânica pela defasagem regulada de energia: "a delayed reaction mechanism to energy prices because of... our household energy price cap system."
*	Foco de risco em second-round effects: risco de "pass through of the energy prices" e efeitos que "we don't want it to become embedded."

AI e emprego

*	Recusa generalização, elencando canais opostos:

DATE: 2026-07-01 11:29:13 | SENDER: Iuri Honda </O=EXCHANGELABS/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE GROUP (FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=018BE688C91B4C4BA27E48FCBF07183F-82A2C364-40> | SUBJECT: IGNORAR VERSÃO ANTERIOR: ECB Forum on Central Banking 2026 - Resumo e transcrição (01/07)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ECB Forum on Central Banking 2026 (01/07)

 

Warsh (Fed)

Postura de política e compromisso com a meta

*	Ele descarta qualquer conforto com inflação acima de 2% e diz, de forma direta, que quem apostava em tolerância vai se decepcionar: "would be disappointed. We're going to deliver price stability in the US."
*	Como sinal de progresso já no início do mandato, ele aponta melhora nas expectativas e nos riscos de inflação: "Inflation risks have come down" e "expectations of inflation... they've come down."
*	Ao descrever a economia, ele repete o retrato do último comunicado sem atualizá-lo, sinalizando estabilidade: "labor markets are steady" e "the demand side of the economy was solid."
*	E coloca a independência como limite inegociável, inclusive frente ao Executivo: "No matter what the President wants... we've been an independent central bank for a very long time."

AI, capex e produtividade como o centro da leitura macro

*	Ele lê a AI, num primeiro momento, como um choque de demanda: o boom de investimento aparece antes de qualquer efeito sobre a oferta. Nas palavras dele, "the AI shock is leading to a boom in capital expenditures. We see that first and foremost in demand."
*	A expansão da oferta é uma expectativa, não um fato observado, e ele reserva o julgamento sobre se isso é inflacionário: "I'm confident we're going to see it in supply at some point" e "it's up to the Central Bank to decide whether it's inflationary."
*	O otimismo dele se apoia em produtividade que já apareceu nos dados, e que em boa parte antecede a AI. Ele cita produtividade estrutural na casa dos 2 e poucos por cento, um potential growth em alta e horas trabalhadas estáveis: "structural productivity is in the high two % range", "potential growth looks like it's trended up" e "hours worked are relatively flat."
*	Ainda assim, ele separa o diagnóstico da decisão, recusando-se a antecipar a política com base nesse otimismo: "does that optimism convey into policy in the next six or nine months? Still too soon to say."
*	Sobre emprego, o raciocínio é que não existe um estoque fixo de vagas a ser destruído pela tecnologia: novas tecnologias criam funções que ninguém previa, e ele avalia que estamos no início desse ciclo. Ele resume como "first or second inning of this revolution", sendo o "timing" a variável que realmente importa, dado o dual mandate.

Balance sheet (6.7tn)

*	Ele subordina o balanço aos juros, que devem ser o instrumento principal de política: as taxas "should be the dominant means through which we make monetary policy."
*	Sobre como o balanço afeta a economia, ele diz que o canal é indireto, via preços de ativos e sinalização, não via crédito direto: "the balance sheet works mostly through asset prices... through signaling effects."
*	Ele chega a classificar um balanço grande como quase política fiscal, o que motiva o desejo de encolhê-lo: "in my biased view, borders on fiscal policy."
*	Mas condiciona qualquer redução a duas coisas, previsibilidade para o mercado e tempo, deixando claro que não será abrupta: "will not be implemented until financial markets have come to understand" e "it'll take us more than 18 weeks."

Comunicação, função de reação e a agenda de dados

*	Ele argumenta que os mercados já entendem como o Fed reage, e usa a própria reação dos preços como prova de que mais guidance seria desnecessário: "volatility's not up, it's down... yields aren't up, they're down... inflation expectations are down."
*	E propõe uma agenda de dados em tempo real como resposta aos problemas de mensuração das estatísticas oficiais, para enxergar a economia de forma contemporânea: leitura "in a contemporaneous real-time way", reduzindo a dependência de dados "with mismeasurement problems."

 

Lagarde (ECB)

Como o ECB está decidindo sob o choque de oferta

*	A alta de juros foi enquadrada como resposta ao choque em si, e não a uma leitura pontual da inflação. Ela situa a decisão no ambiente de choque de oferta: "in the context of a supply shock that led us to the decision that we made."
*	A função de reação foi verbalizada de forma explícita, com quatro insumos que o comitê pesa em conjunto: "inflation outlook, balance of risk, underlying inflation, transmission of monetary policy."
*	O balanço de riscos mudou nas últimas semanas: antes assimétrico, ela agora o vê mais equilibrado, com risco de inflação para cima e de crescimento para baixo se compensando. Nas palavras dela, os riscos estão "more broadly balanced than they were a few weeks ago."
*	O que destravou esse reequilíbrio foi a velocidade da queda da energia, que ela cita diretamente: "$72 a barrel now when it was 120 back in March."
*	Os cenários (mild, severe, adverse) são usados como teste de robustez da decisão, para que ela se sustente independentemente de qual mundo se materialize: "to make sure that our decisions are solid and robust across scenarios."

Por que ela descarta stagflation

*	Ela rejeita o paralelo com os anos 70 por razões estruturais, não porque a inflação esteja baixa. O argumento é que as condições da época não se repetem: "stagflation is a concept of the 70s in circumstances that are not replicated."
*	A âncora do argumento é o mercado de trabalho, que segue forte: desemprego perto do menor nível histórico e participação ainda subindo, "almost lowest historical levels of unemployment" e "employment participation continues growing."
*	E ela apresenta o compromisso com a meta como algo que já está em execução, não como promessa futura: "We will take the necessary steps and we have."

AI vista como um choque de produtividade que ainda precisa ser medido

*	Ela trata a AI como objeto de mensuração para a política monetária, não como narrativa de mercado. O ponto é entender o efeito líquido sobre preços ao longo do tempo: "we need to measure the disinflationary, inflationary impact it will have over the course of time."
*	E ela é honesta quanto à incerteza sobre a or

**UBS TMI: META Madness - What to make of it?

 UBS Sector Sales – Sales Commentary for Institutional Investors Only – This is not a product of UBS Research 

This communication has been generated by Global Markets and has not been vetted for Global Wealth Management end client distribution. You are responsible for making sure the communication complies with regulations and internal policies before sending to a Global Wealth Management client

  <https://neo.ubs.com/r/7/?id=h76cbc981,ffb51c52,1> 

Another wild morning in a week that SHOULD have been nothing but BBQs and some much-needed rest into another long earnings season…META +9% with headlines hitting that the company apparently building out a cloud business to sell excess cloud compute…hmm… Okay, so first thing that catches my eye here is the term “excess capacity”… yes, while that isn’t really the peachiest datapoint when we think through AI demand trends (IMO probably reads MOST negative CRWV/neoclouds), I think the kneejerk read (and the biggest reason why the stock is up +HSD%) is just that this moves shows at least SOME financial constraint from Zuck so capex is NO longer biased to the upside. So now the story can shift to FCF stabilization, a potential new revenue stream, and all of it at what many would argue are near-trough valuation multiples. It also raises an interesting question heading into earnings: if META can post in line 2Q/3Q guide while reiterating FY capex, is that enough to cut it?? It’s feeling like it… 

  

Now for context, this idea was at least flirted by mgmt. earlier this spring <https://analytics.ubs.com/b/ss/ubsextern-cca-prod/4/REDIR/?v5=Click&v6=SMEP&pe=lnk_o&pev2=link&events=event3&url=https%3A%2F%2Feur01.safelinks.protection.outlook.com%2F%3Furl%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Fwww.cnbc.com%252F2026%252F05%252F27%252Fmark-zuckerberg-says-meta-starting-cloud-business-on-the-table.html%26data%3D05%257C02%257Csh234045%2540UBSCloud.onmicrosoft.com%257C7a37565e6f644f1150a808ded77dc02b%257Cfb6ea4037cf14905810afe5547e98204%257C0%257C0%257C639185132328610190%257CUnknown%257CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJFbXB0eU1hcGkiOnRydWUsIlYiOiIwLjAuMDAwMCIsIlAiOiJXaW4zMiIsIkFOIjoiTWFpbCIsIldUIjoyfQ%253D%253D%257C0%257C%257C%257C%26sdata%3DctAZMlzGGj15MJGfNm2XmRP5MKN6KVtuHHTeROPr1Pw%253D%26reserved%3D0&v2=4698&v3=1f17559287716cf09ce0105163a4d1d5~4082~384074202606446&v4=false&c3=1f17559287716cf09ce0105163a4d1d5~4082~384074202606446>  so not really a HUGE shock to the system but still an uncomfortable datapoint heading into earnings preview season especially when we think about what it means for the compute/memory bottlenecks and thus pricing trends. So with that in mind, see below for early convos on read throughs. 

  

READ THROUGHS

*	SEMIS TRADE: A lot of debate as to what this move really means for the semis trade…just looking at how SOXX is trading out of the gates this morning, investors are pretty clearly connecting the dots as to what META’s move means for father capex increases and thus compute/memory bottlenecks (and thus pricing). Now I get the pushback that even if META theoretically eases, rest of hyperscalers will snap it up that capacity quickly. But at the same time the demand curve still shifts with the duration above trend demand shorter. In other words, so instead of compute shortages through CY29, what if its only CY28??? Nevertheless, I’m not a semis expert by any means so very open to thoughts here 
*	NEOCLOUDS: A negative read no matter how you cut it… no pushback there. 
*	HYPERSCALERS: Feedback more mixed... of course this means we’ll have another competitor on the table but to the extent compute bottlenecks ease, bulls are arguing these players can also benefit from a cost perspective. Cue the second question “what does this mean for everyone else's capex plans?” My initial read from conversations this morning is that the overbuild risk feels much more META-specific than industry-wide just considering how *arguably* behind investors believe they are in their AI efforts… I mean just days ago GOOGL cut off META too because they're so constrained <https://analytics.ubs.com/b/ss/ubsextern-cca-prod/4/REDIR/?v5=Click&v6=SMEP&pe=lnk_o&pev2=link&events=event3&url=https%3A%2F%2Feur01.safelinks.protection.outlook.com%2F%3Furl%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Fx.com%252Fnoxflux%252Fstatus%252F2071197823085765006%26data%3D05%257C02%257Csh234045%2540UBSCloud.onmicrosoft.com%257C7a37565e6f644f1150a808ded77dc02b%257Cfb6ea4037cf14905810afe5547e98204%257C0%257C0%257C639185132328637151%257CUnknown%257CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJFbXB0eU1hcGkiOnRydWUsIlYiOiIwLjAuMDAwMCIsIlAiOiJXaW4zMiIsIkFOIjoiTWFpbCIsIldUIjoyfQ%253D%253D%257C0%257C%257C%257C%26sdata%3DWgaVtqM7f4SQ%252Fn%252FTJHuiLMna5tMYJvzKOUWP0pJb2S4%253D%26reserved%3D0&v2=4698&v3=1f17559287716cf09ce0105163a4d1d5~4082~384074202716229&v4=false&c3=1f17559287716cf09ce0105163a4d1d5~4082~384074202716229> . Doesn’t read the same…

THE META NEWS & INVESTOR FEEDBACK ON META, SEMIS, NEOCLOUDS. META now up 11% on the THIS ARTICLE <https://insight.email.bofa.streetcontext.com/platform/al?a=1000000000036794&ad=1000000003924438&h=v-2WlKo&sig=3kb90w04p7UUBjafj4XhXnTF7UK&v=2&url=https://blinks.bloomberg.com/news/stories/THHY59KJH6V4> , and SEMIS down (-4%). Market reaction in general reads like 1) Good for META, cheap/beaten up, was not pricing in AI ‘success’ anymore, and direct ROI from its capex is bullish for them, plans to “sell access to AI computing power and models”. 2) Market reacting negative to notion that there is “excess” or “surplus” of compute given how virtually all other ecosystem participants have said the exact opposite.

If META is selling access to “it’s models” that’s not ecosystem negative at all. I would actually suspect their models crowd out this brewing “open source” mkt share,  not crowd out OpenAI and Anthropic and therefore we might have BETTER visiblity moving forward into they broader ecosystem. 


(Interestingly, just yesterday the FT reported that GOOGL had put caps on META’s use of Gemini AI from Google “after the social media giant sought more computing capacity than the rival tech group could provide, in the latest evidence of the infrastructure constraints….”)

 

MY 2 CENTS. One view I have is that while the mkt is fixating on whether META’s “plan” shows there was shadow supply of compute laying around and is triggered by the words “excess” & “surplus” (improbable based like, every data point/comment from other ecosystem partners, public companies, mgmt. teams, etc)..that the real SIGNAL HERE is that Zuck would likely only do this if he truly believed there was such massive, enduring demand for AI compute that being 18 years late to the game (relative to say, AWS), and facing a highly competitive, well-funded field…would STILL leave META with an attractive ROIC business. Anyway. Big topic. Lots of diff angles.

*        Short-term, above-market compute leases could help self-fund META’s AI infrastructure buildout while its internal AI products/models continue to mature.

*        Some investors argued this reduces the risk that META needs to cut capex, and instead supports continued AI investment.

*        Incremental revenue/EBIT from compute leasing is likely not in current models, so even modest contribution could be positive to FCF.

Midday Market Intelligence: rise up! 
	
1 July 2026 | 12:11PM EDT | Research | Equity 	
	
	
US stocks are kicking off the second half of the year on the same theme that we saw in 1H26 -- higher highs -- as investors digest today (Wednesday) a slightly weaker than expected ISM Manufacturing Index and a whole lot of Fed speak that is not having much of an impact on rates (10-year yields are little changed at 4.46%).

 	 

and not throwing away my shot 

Our strategists have written extensively about how the rally we have seen this year in stocks has been driven by earnings, not multiple expansion, as a combination of accelerating AI infrastructure investment, tax cuts, and improving business sentiment has helped earnings growth to step up. 1Q S&P500 EPS grew by 17% -- accelerating from the 12% pace we enjoyed in 2025.

And looking forward to 2Q26 results, Ben Snider points out that bottoms-up consensus EPS growth is now expected to come in at 22% -- an acceleration from the acceleration we saw in 1Q26 (see last Friday's Kickstart, "S&P 500 Q2 2026 earnings season preview <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQI-ZEhBxaSQmZcvscB49hyM8upDzRBAOPomsx96Wul6Fp_ON7BMAACwTMGrWBpWiuBlAgbKZFNsjVIrMNAPDGmiRC-Op-LDn2KcxdPpxYHaff5ALez96cxlooYSltJ_Ij42eq6imQK1IFcsQc1u4ELjN1LsYTsgHNnTyTaqAtbyVS_0biWwvQ44QGpX37iy1jQtVdMFnfQa09UwI0upp-hEGfOYTdOVyfHpzw6NfM6icrdB9JZ_Vt4Cs7nsxZPt3CGyhhL-jV6iXfkm3DvhLhZK_t-sE2MlrNY*%26id=a6df8040-3cf2-4b0b-a7d3-a2ea8042108d%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1e76f0d6-0c5fb71c-3350-47b4-96a0-ac96bd35dfe6-000000/zfIBr20KtIgAjjVbVBsM7C3LLrD82EyhYWqEgd_pBZc=452> ." For some investors, such a high bar may prove daunting. But another common theme of the past 3+ year stock market rally has been FOMO (fear of missing out). A lot has been written about how AI is falling short of delivering the enterprise efficiency gains that it has promised. But AI has not fallen short of delivering the AI infrastructure investment that it never promised -- but is nevertheless required to power the large language models being developed around the world. And as long as AI infrastructure investment remains intense, earnings growth may be buoyed alongside it.

A separate theme permeating markets in 2026 has been HALO investing - leaning into the stocks of companies with high asset intensity and low obsolescence (in other words, traditional industrials). And today, we got an update on business sentiment across the US manufacturing complex with a fresh ISM Manufacturing Index (see "USA: ISM Manufacturing Somewhat Below Expectations; S&P Global Manufacturing PMI Revised Down; Construction Spending Increases in May While Benchmark Revisions Raise Spending Level But Lower Recent Growth <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQKVe723ZTAfybZfJjRASMF8tMv-QxC0fE1pW_xv2V27J1Y8i5wMAACwzeIghRcSuPxrbaVel319xS6DjHrv_EliwYeZrQG1BI8xTPnzr_KLvpC0ngV90bgT9oVWPIc98xzr_U3WQ4sII9njsJWoaToYl1AWgnH51hplSYXpQ42I13HENyXK9GOcxY2HO5ec_I_RcjTkiRJDyvQ_MgwrGfph8xzOTmy111N7ynOwUxK3FvuPkmtEnJmb4MvvNB8TsHvjmt8mjTiEYuKhoH9c3A8Njwl3nzX32aA*%26id=1677fecc-a8dd-448d-83d2-3946fc5a51fb%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1e76f0d6-0c5fb71c-3350-47b4-96a0-ac96bd35dfe6-000000/pzaOkBGyyj-XIelo3fXzhWFZ4mE46eylsrqCCxktajw=452> "). The Index fell to 53.3 from 54.0 a month ago but remains elevated relative to what we have seen through most of the post-pandemic echo-boom when manufacturing business sentiment has signaled a contraction.

 	 

chart of the day 

Consumer confidence has also improved across the world, particularly in the US writes Megan Peters in "G10 Consumer Dashboard: June 2026: Resilience in Japan <https://publishing.gs.com/CL0/https:%2F%2Fpublishing.gs.com%2FtrustedLink%3Fopentoken=T1RLAQI66PDLfMJ8JCjEsTbgtUxMuOk4kxC8yX0ieBq47gm9F85mJ7TjAACw6sxKot3G-cIsp6W5MHxUfdjNzpRh6Zsp5g92Ex7MekFirj52j9z6POM2LzO6Sel_qYG-yCndYk27w9fYLAi3EPv_3ZbOUdX2w5lv0Yd0Jg0qUojobJ_xVa7d5LSLCGRBP1-y66t2g2h9ptvsOLrgGEmOmsvbDHsRQM1v7lqc8ZDElhLqtMx-5FjDIySqEz-golQD8b1XsrhP88BNE4wQiauWOW7l_REfSsX8qUHkHOk*%26id=496a304b-5a23-4fca-a7e8-f9c1972ac649%26utm_medium=pa/1/0100019f1e76f0d6-0c5fb71c-3350-47b4-96a0-ac96bd35dfe6-000000/NuJRVFazEb5mSlqr91Z12VBHaHTZ4aCZt1En2rnjO4o=452> ." Encouragingly, there is still a lot of upside to consumer sentiment which is at or below the 20th percentile of this measure almost everywhere in the world (see chart below).

DATE: 2026-07-01 14:12:46 | SENDER: Josey, Ronald (Citi) <ronald.josey@investmentresearch.citi.com> | SUBJECT: North America Internet: Meta Compute Unlocks Capacity (and FCF) for Meta's Superintelligence Ambitions

With the potential launch of Meta Compute, per Bloomberg, Meta appears to be planning to offer access to its AI compute and infrastructure, including the potential to offer multiple models, similar to AWS’ Bedrock. CEO Zuckerberg suggested this could be an option at Meta’s annual shareholder meeting in May and given recent capacity partnerships valued at ~$50B/GW, Meta Compute could significantly shore up its FCF while funding its capacity builds (Prometheus and Hyperion DCs) and newer products under MSL. And to this, we continue to expect Meta to launch multiple new AI products by year-end and has the infrastructure capacity to do so, as Meta Compute becomes a new business unit. We reiterate our Buy rating and $850 TP on META. 
 	
Viewpoint | Citi Research 	
North America Internet 
Meta Compute Unlocks Capacity (and FCF) for Meta's Superintelligence Ambitions 
CITI'S TAKE 

With the potential launch of Meta Compute, per Bloomberg <https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-07-01/meta-is-building-a-cloud-business-to-sell-excess-ai-compute> , Meta appears to be planning to offer access to its AI compute and infrastructure, including the potential to offer multiple models, similar to AWS’ Bedrock. CEO Zuckerberg suggested this could be an option at Meta’s annual shareholder meeting in May and given recent capacity partnerships valued at ~$50B/GW, Meta Compute could significantly shore up its FCF while funding its capacity builds (Prometheus and Hyperion DCs) and newer products under MSL. And to this, we continue to expect Meta to launch multiple new AI products by year-end and has the infrastructure capacity to do so, as Meta Compute becomes a new business unit. In this note, we include thoughts from Citi’s Software (Tyler Radke) and Telecom (Michael Rollins) Analysts, whereby they suggest AI demand continues to exceed supply despite overcapacity concerns. We reiterate our Buy rating and $850 TP on META.

Read Full Report <https://www.citivelocity.com/rendition/eppublic/documentService/dXNlcl9pZD1aZjhlUVZybW5feWhWNm9nZC0xSXZRVDluMnliVkNBdyZlbWFpbF9zZW5kX2lkPTQxMzg4NjA5OTgmdj0x/Y2xpZW50U3lzdGVtSWQ9UkRFX0ZBVkUmYmxhc3RLZXk9MTI2NjYwNTcmRU5BQkxFX1JFTkRJVElPTl9JRlJBTUVfUEVSU09OQUxJWkFUSU9OPU4mZG9jX2lkPTMwNDQwODEzJnBsYXRmb3JtPTg0JmNsaWVudEJsYXN0SWQ9MzA0NDA4MTM> 	

*	More Details on Meta Compute: Selling Model Access & Compute Capacity: Per Bloomberg, Meta is potentially establishing Meta Compute to monetize its AI infrastructure with plans to sell both model access (including Muse Spark and potentially 3P models) as well as excess GPU compute capacity. The article suggests Meta Compute would be run via Meta’s MSL and Infrastructure teams and reporting to Meta President, Dina Powell McCormick. CEO Zuckerberg has said that Meta would consider selling excess compute or launching API-based services if Meta builds out more capacity than it needs internally (per Meta’s shareholder meeting <https://www.cnbc.com/2026/05/27/mark-zuckerberg-says-meta-starting-cloud-business-on-the-table.html>  in May ’26 [CNBC, 5/27])—either for core advertising or its Personal Superintelligence product roadmap—and while we believe Meta’s internal demand for compute remain high and its project roadmap robust, we view Meta Compute as a newer business unit that can fund Meta’s broader AI ambitions (vs. Meta’s more traditional product launch approach of build, launch, grow awareness/adoption, and monetize…).

*	Meta’s Capacity is Likely Still Constrained Today, but Capacity is Expanding: With Meta Compute established in Jan. ’26 to develop 10s of GWs by 2030 and hundreds of GWs LT, Meta is building compute capacity in excess of current internal operational needs. As part of this roadmap, Meta is building out Prometheus (1GW+ cluster coming online in ’26) and Hyperion (5GW+ by ‘30, initial deployments in ’28) data centers, an MTIA (Meta Training & Inference Accelerator) family of chips (MTIA 300, 400, 450, and 500), as well as $100B+ in spend towards compute partnerships over the next 7+ years (Figure 1, including Google Cloud, CoreWeave, Nvidia, AMD, among others). Bigger picture, while Meta is likely still capacity constrained today, given reports of Meta encouraging employees to be more efficient with tokens, we believe Meta’s capacity is ramping significantly through Prometheus and newer partnerships.

*	Monetizing Meta’s Compute to Drive FCF Returns Long-term: Underpinning plans to monetize its AI infrastructure, we believe Meta is making a strategic decision to recognize NT revenue & FCF as it builds out MSL and its goal of reaching Personal Superintelligence. We currently project ’26E and ’27E Capex of $139B and $171B and FCF to be $14.6B and $8.5B, respectively. (Continued…)

DATE: 2026-07-01 14:13:15 | SENDER: MNI <mktbrief@marketnews.com> | SUBJECT: MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Will Be On Hold As Oil Shock Unwinds- Levy
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXakesI6aJhck8kHg~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CCJCjptJe2eJOIQ> 	 <https://emedia.marketnews.com/marketnewsintl/mni-pr-01-25.png?t=1> 	


MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Will Be On Hold As Oil Shock Unwinds- Levy 

By Evan Ryser
Jul 1, 2026


The Federal Reserve is likely to keep interest rates on hold as the oil shock from the Middle East conflict unwinds and a temporary drop in prices raises the real fed funds rate, Mickey Levy, an outside advisor to several Fed Banks, told MNI.

"I doubt if the Fed would vote to raise rates in an environment in which the general price level is declining," said Levy, a member of the Shadow Open Market Committee, a group of private academic economists that acts as the Fed’s outside watchdogs. 

"The Fed's not going to raise rates when the when the CPI or PCE price index are declining," Levy said. Financial markets are pricing in only about a 30% chance ​of a rate hike at the central bank's July 28-29 meeting. (See: MNI INTERVIEW: Fed’s Next Rate Move Most Likely Upward-Kohn <https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXakesI6aJhck8kHw~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CCJCjptJe2eJOIQ> ) 

Levy said this FOMC is on hold waiting for more data with the hope that core inflation recedes a bit, rather than having "its finger on the trigger to hike rates." 

UNWIND

The dramatic spike in oil prices generated three months of outsized increases in CPI and PCE inflation that pushed up their year-over-year measures. Oil prices have fallen sharply, and if current prices stick close to current levels, which is uncertain as inventories need rebuilding, continued rapid price declines in gasoline and other energy may result in months of decreases in the CPI and PCE price index.

"I think June's going to be the transition month in terms of the monthly inflation data, but in July and August you could have outright declines in the CPI and maybe the PCE," he said. "I can't remember when we've had such a period with oil where there's been a surge like we had on the way up and then a collapse on the downside. It's just striking."

This would ease some price pressures on consumers and let the Fed breathe more easily. The consumer in the last three months has been resilient, Levy said. "Consumption has been rising in real terms each month and you've got a nice bounce in employment." (See: MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Hike Plausible As Early As July - George <https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXakesI6aJhck8kHA~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CCJCjptJe2eJOIQ> ) 

Levy, a visiting fellow at the Hoover Institution, also noted that retail gasoline prices have fallen rapidly and the labor market is at maximum employment. 

In its updated June Summary of Economic Projections, the FOMC members estimated that a rate hike may be appropriate to be consistent with its dual mandate goals. "But the FOMC member dots are not binding, and subject to changing conditions," Levy said. 

DELIBERATE

Levy has known Fed Chairman Kevin Warsh, a former Hoover visiting fellow, for many years. He congratulated the move to establish five task forces, but Levy also suggested the task forces won't by themselves preclude any potential interest rate adjustments. 
 
"I like the idea. Having outside advisors is wise," he said. "In its deliberations and conduct of monetary policy, the Fed has to deliberate well before the task forces come together with some concrete recommendations," Levy added.

July 01, 2026

Quick summary, investors…

*	Are watching tomorrow’s Payrolls release with the same intensity as normal
*	Think the market reaction will be risk-on 

	*	52% risk-on
	*	17% mixed/negligible
	*	31% risk-off

*	Expect… 

	*	Payrolls at 133k (BBG consensus 115k, 113k at time of survey)
	*	AHE in-line at 0.3%
	*	Urate lower at 4.2%, BBG consensus 4.3% 

*	Are split on whether stronger data is risk-on or risk-off

PAYROLLS: 52% of investors believe that tomorrow’s data will be risk-on. 31% believe risk-off and 17% believe mixed/negligible. 40% of investors believe OTHER people think the data will be mixed/ negligible. Risk-on is the surprisingly popular answer since its prediction exceeds its popularity, and it therefore may carry more informational weight. 



Risk-on gained traction this month (52% versus 25% last month). 



The ranges for risk-on and risk-off payrolls estimates are much wider than last month, underscoring how uncertain investors are about the market’s reaction function. Investors are split on whether stronger or weaker prints should be treated as risk-on or risk-off.



The same trend holds true for the unemployment rate. 



Labor market data is being watched the same as normal for the sixth month in a row with a tail towards more than normal. 



Source: 22V Research

Investors’ focus remains on Payrolls, but AHE is increasing in importance. 



DATA ESTIMATES: Our survey consensus for Payrolls is 133k, above Bloomberg’s 115k (113k at time of survey). 60% expect above sell-side consensus. 



Survey consensus for AHE is in-line at 0.3%. 



Survey consensus for the urate is 4.2%, lower than Bloomberg’s 4.3%. However, there is a tail to a higher number. 



Investors think that a Urate of 4.0% implies inflationary pressure. This is higher than last month’s 3.9%. There is more of an even skew between higher and lower Urate versus previous months.

DATE: 2026-07-01 14:18:18 | SENDER: MNI <mktbrief@marketnews.com> | SUBJECT: MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Right To Hold Off On Hikes For Now - Keen
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXakb0I6aJhck8gHg~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CCJD1ptJe2eJOIQ> 	 <https://emedia.marketnews.com/marketnewsintl/mni-pr-01-25.png?t=1> 	


MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Right To Hold Off On Hikes For Now - Keen

By Pedro Nicolaci da Costa
Jul 1, 2026


WASHINGTON - The Federal Reserve should wait to see how much inflation comes down in the next few months following an easing of Middle East tensions that have brought oil prices sharply lower, Benjamin Keen, a former consultant and visiting scholar at several regional Fed banks, told MNI. 

“A lot of the inflation was being driven by oil prices, and we’re starting to see oil prices go down. I would expect in the coming months for that to show up in the data,” he said.  

“The Fed still wants to get the economy back to its long run 2% inflation target,” said Keen, adding that whether rate hikes will be needed to achieve that outcome has “yet to be determined.”

Fed officials are right to be worried about above-target inflation, and Chair Warsh’s focus on price stability is understandable given economic conditions and his priors as a Fed governor during the 2008 financial crisis, said Keen. (See MNI INTERVIEW: Fed Can't Ignore Mounting Prices Pressures-Liang <https://enews.marketnews.com/ct/x/pjJsdwXakb0I6aJhck8gHw~k1zZ8KXr-kA8x6_CCJD1ptJe2eJOIQ> ) 

NO RUSH 

Still, the direction of price pressures is not uncertain, and Warsh and the FOMC are probably right to take their time before rushing into any tightening move. 

“Based on what they’re seeing in the data, that seems to be a reasonable course of action,” said Keen, an associate professor at the University of Oklahoma. 

Like Warsh, Keen is optimistic about the prospect that the AI boom could unleash a new wave of productivity that also helps keep a lid on prices. 

“We could raise the natural rate from productivity build out, but as AI comes along and lowers per unit production cost, those will eventually be passed on to the consumer in terms of lower prices or lower growth in prices, which means what productivity shocks are disinflationary,” he said.

At the same time, the labor market is showing little hint of the kind of weakness that would require more accommodative policies from the Fed, said Keen.

“The macro data does not show the labor market needs support.  We do have a segment of the labor market, recent college graduates, that we have a problem with. But overall the macro environment looks good. That’s the Fed’s job, to worry about the overall macro. The Fed doesn’t need to be in the business of targeting unemployment rates for groups,” said Keen.

CONSENSUS

Warsh is trying to build consensus not just on the path of interest rates but also on his stated push for reform in areas like communications and the balance sheet, Keen said. 

The chair is right to shun forward guidance in a highly uncertain environment, he added. 

“It’s the assessment of the chair that forward guidance is tying our hands to some degree,” he said. “There’s a benefit to doing it when we are at the zero lower bound, but right now it comes with a greater cost because if the market is expecting one thing and they’re doing something different because new information has come in, then it’s going to catch the market by surprise.”

The Fed is still likely to want to avoid major market surprises, but the shift in communications approach could throw some curveballs.  

“We've gotten used to the current paradigm for a while, and now what he's suggesting is let's change that paradigm, and let's go back to, we walk into every meeting, we have a discussion on the facts on the ground, and the data that we're seeing,” Keen said.

DATE: 2026-07-01 15:11:10 | SENDER: Vital Knowledge <updates@vitalknowledge.net> | SUBJECT: Vital Knowledge: Is SpaceX going to sell a phone?
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://vitalknowledge.net/assets/images/resources//section1.png> 	
 <https://vitalknowledge.net/assets/images/resources//vertical_divider.png> INTRADAY COMMENTARY 	
Jul 01, 2026 2:09:46 PM EST 	
Is SpaceX going to sell a phone? 	

*	SPCX (SpaceX) has developed a handset-like device prototype and shown it off to some investors according to a WSJ article <https://www.wsj.com/tech/ai/spacex-showed-investors-prototype-of-elon-musks-new-ai-device-b445c57b?mod=newsviewer_click&adobe_mc=MCMID%3D26622675878327304541006841196593856970%7CMCORGID%3DCB68E4BA55144CAA0A4C98A5%2540AdobeOrg%7CTS%3D1782929193&_gl=1*ldlqm4*_gcl_au*NTQ3MzM3MDE0LjE3Nzk1MDUzMTg.*_ga*MTU4ODI3OTQ5Ni4xNzc5NTA1MzE4*_ga_K2H7B9JRSS*czE3ODI5Mjg1ODEkbzk3JGcxJHQxNzgyOTI5MTkxJGo2MCRsMSRoODIxMTc1OTQy>  published at 1:55pmET Wed afternoon. The device, which runs on a proprietary OS and Qualcomm chip, aims to “reshape how humans interact with AI”. 
*	What does this mean? Telecom stocks have been hit hard lately amid concerns that SpaceX plans to become a larger force in the consumer mobile market, and this WSJ report about a device prototype may only add to those fears. However, SpaceX has a long way to go before successfully manufacturing a consumer device at scale and competing against the leading platforms (incidentally, the same can be said about OpenAI, which is why investors should be very skeptical whenever they read about that company’s consumer hardware initiatives). Musk-led companies are given a massive benefit of the doubt when it comes to product promises (which translates into enormous valuation premiums at SPCX and TSLA based on products that are more ideas than reality), but it’s hard to imagine SpaceX becoming a force in consumer electronics (and on the telecom services front, Starlink is likely to remain more a complimentary service to AT&T, Verizon, and T-Mobile as opposed to a replacement for the foreseeable future).

DATE: 2026-07-01 15:20:24 | SENDER: Amerian, Amir <amir.amerian@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: SHORT CANON - May Industry Camera Sales -DD% YoY (1st DD decline since Dec 2023), more China-driven on tough comp but watching for downtrading trends, MSR US HW Consumer Tracker shows growing inflation concerns
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SALES COMMENTARY ONLY (NOT A PRODUCT OF RESEARCH)

For institutional use onLY

 

I personally continue to like Canon on the short side. I personally think there is still opportunity in the “Memory Losers” trade, focused on companies where end-demand is not extremely strong (unlike servers) and where companies total memory buying power is low. Cameras continue to screen in this risk category.

 

May Industry Data for Digital Cameras was released <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/3a69de54-7534-11f1-9560-223b52d1e427?t=1782929968:6055:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> , with units down -17.6% YoY. This is the first month of double digit YoY decline since Dec 2023. MS Japan Precision analyst Mie Yamazaki points out this was likely driven by China (-39% YoY), which may be a result of a tough comp from last year’s electronics subsidies. For the other regions: Japan +10% YoY, Europe -14% YoY, Americas -6.6% YoY, Asia -4.8%.

 

For Canon, worth noting it has less exposure to China than the industry. Canon’s CY25 Camera RoW Sales Ratio was 33%, vs Industry CY25 China Ratio 28%. Canon has relatively higher exposure to Americas (30% vs Industry 23%) and Europe (29% vs Industry 21%). So beyond the fact I’m admittedly cherry picking monthly industry data (April <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/8c429cec-5d93-11f1-bb82-5734c7383398?t=1782929968:6055:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==>  was fine), this data point alone may not be a direct reflection of Canon’s trends. However, China is the single largest camera market in 2025 (28%), and has been the key driver of industry growth in recent years.

 

 

The upside risk I’m watching out for is companies having price hike power if consumer’s expectations re-anchor to higher inflation (similar to 2022 inflation pick-up). AAPL’s <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/e2c2d0a6-7098-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae?t=1782929968:6055:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==>  price hike announcement last week raise that risk, although market initially feared memory-driven price hikes would lead to potential demand destruction. In the May Industry Data, Shipment ASP was +19.7% YoY. Yamazaki san thinks higher selling prices may have weighed on demand. There was also a divergence in Built-In Lens Camera unit growth -0.6% YoY vs Interchangeable Lens Camera units -23% YoY (Mirrorless -21%). That could imply some users in entry class mirrorless cameras are downtrading to built-in lens. If that’s a sustained trend, that me be a negative impact to Canon (interchangeable / mirrorless lens cameras are higher margin).

 

 

I’d also flag recent US Consumer spending tracker <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/5df66cae-70a5-11f1-b8bb-85ba1f0ac5ae?t=1782929968:6055:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==>  from MS US HW analyst Erik Woodring. Consumer Sentiment improved MoM, but next 6mo consumer electronics spending intentions worsened MoM. Usually these are correlated at a 1mo lag, so Erik is watching for the latter to likely improve MoM. However, he highlights that "coping with inflation" as a headwind has been steadily rising since Jan '26 as a top concern for consumers for this year, some of which reflects memory/component inflation in higher consumer electronics. 

 

 

Report: Precision Instruments: Digital Camera Stats (May 2026): Shipment Volume Down 2-digits YoY; Watching For a Continuation Ahead (1 Jul 2026) <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/3a69de54-7534-11f1-9560-223b52d1e427?t=1782929968:6055:42924:816774ccf5ea&m=1&ch=Email Safety Catch#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> 

 

Happy to discuss more and connect you with Yamazaki san. She is OW on Canon.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By Mark LaPedus 

Intel has broken ground on a new photomask manufacturing facility in Santa Clara, Calif.

The new facility will expand Intel’s existing photomask manufacturing operations at the Bowers Campus in Santa Clara. For several years, the company’s internal mask-making unit--Intel Mask Operations (IMO)--has been producing masks at the Bowers Cam

DATE: 2026-07-01 16:50:59 | SENDER: Rodolfo Ramos <rodolfo.c.ramos@bradescobbi.com.br> | SUBJECT: Mexico Equity Strategy: USMCA Will Not Be Rubber-Stamped; We Are Buyers of Trade-Induced Anxiety (Ramos)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Mexico Equity Strategy



USMCA Will Not Be Rubber-Stamped; We Are Buyers of Trade-Induced Anxiety 

Full Report <https://bradescobbi.bluematrix.com/links2/html/72ac91f6-d147-402c-83fc-82b684965c00> 	

In today's virtual USMCA Joint Review, the US declined to renew-or "rubber-stamp"-the agreement, defaulting instead to annual reviews. Given that the third and last round of bilateral talks is scheduled for July 20, it was implicit the review would not be concluded by July 1 as initially expected. We believe this fact, coupled with positive headlines regarding Mexico's cooperation on security, explains the muted response in the FX and equity markets, even in nearshoring proxies. Mexico's Economy Minister Marcelo Ebrard framed it as a procedural transition to negotiate structural adjustments, rather than a systemic crisis. It is worth noting that the USMCA remains in force for another 10 years unless a member country exits, which would need to notify the other two members six months in advance.

After the meeting, Ambassador Jamieson Greer (USTR) said that the review process will focus on addressing the US trade deficit with Mexico and tackling regional supply-chain imbalances. The US is pushing for stricter rules of origin, including requiring that 50% of automotive components specifically be made in the US, and raising the overall regional value content threshold for autos from 75% to over 80%. Furthermore, the US is demanding a unified front on export controls and investment limits to block China from using Mexico to dodge tariffs.

Our take: It seems as if the July 1 deadline had little significance in the overall context consisting of just a virtual meeting between the three countries to publicly, and formally, announce the US wouldn't be backing the agreement as it currently stands, which everyone had already anticipated. Instead, we believe the July 20 in-person meeting in Mexico City might provide us with clues of what exactly the US is looking to change and facilitate an agreement between Mexico and the US. A separate negotiation, which would bode well for nearshoring sentiment, is related to Section 232 tariffs. We would be buyers of any USMCA-induced market anxiety. A new deal tipping the scale in favor of the US would also give the Trump administration political ammunition ahead of the US midterm elections. Companies that are sensitive to US trade policies remain cautiously optimistic, including those in the steel and auto sectors. We maintain our positive and out-of-consensus view on the US-Mexico trade negotiations and favor nearshoring proxies Vesta, Fibra Prologis, OMA, and Banorte. We have also recently added Ternium to our LatAm equity strategy (A Second Opportunity in the Second Half <https://bradescobbi.bluematrix.com/links2/link/html/72ac91f6-d147-402c-83fc-82b684965c00/d0b38bb4-0480-48d5-9ab4-1409db2fb691> ).

Figure 1 - USMCA Review Timeline and Scenario Analysis	
	
Source: Bradesco BBI

*	Potential size of large load approvals, timing, and impacts on the ERCOT market
*	Implications of batching process for projects under development by power and crypto companies

 

 

Speaker Bio: Clayton Greer is at the forefront of integrating cryptocurrency mining operations and data center management with electrical power grids as the Vice President of the Energy Division at Cholla Petroleum. With a career spanning over three decades in the Electrical Power Industry, Clayton has been instrumental in the evolution of power distribution and market operations, particularly within ERCOT's zonal and nodal markets.

Beginning his journey at Public Service of Oklahoma, Clayton honed his skills in power system analysis, substation design, and emergency response in Tulsa, OK. His expertise grew through roles at Texas New Mexico Power and significant contributions to ERCOT's stakeholder process, where he played a key role in shaping Texas's electricity market. Clayton's career further expanded into power marketing and trading with notable firms before his strategic move to Cholla in 2022.

An honors graduate in Electrical Engineering from the University of Tulsa, Clayton's professional journey is underpinned by a deep commitment to innovation and efficiency in power distribution. His work not only ensures a reliable and efficient energy supply but also paves the way for sustainable energy practices in the rapidly evolving sectors of cryptocurrency and data centers.

DATE: 2026-07-01 17:31:44 | SENDER: EG Sustainability <sustainability@eurasiagroup.net> | SUBJECT: EG Sustainability: Responsible investing trends report: Now, next, later | Q2 2026 edition
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Sustainability


01 Jul 2026 16:29 EDT

	  	 
 	 
Responsible investing trends report: Now, next, later | Q2 2026 edition

 	
 	 
 	  Read full report <https://library.eurasiagroup.net/go/wfpub_eurasia_26734_bea49063/2026-q2_responsible_investing_trends_report_0.pdf?token=7c84f6ab-7e24-47a0-bfa1-00e4e9b6a5ce&extension=.pdf&click=ec98377e-d417-4e80-80c4-61d78468249b> 	
 	
 	 
________________________________

 	 
The second-quarter 2026 edition of the Responsible Investing Trends report highlights nine additional trends that are shaping how the investment community responds to global sustainability challenges, why they matter, and how they will likely evolve. It also provides an overview of how the September 2025, December 2025, and March 2026 trends have progressed. Highlighted trends in the June 2026 edition include:

*	Short-term trends (6–12 months): In the near term, pricing, regulation, and market fatigue are redrawing the boundaries of responsible investing. Water leads the shift, moving from a disclosure concept to a priced-in credit liability as drought-driven downgrades hit US municipal issuers. Standard-setters are also pivoting toward prescriptive, simplified rulebooks, with the EU streamlining its disclosure regime as a global sustainability reporting baseline consolidates. Meanwhile, greenwashing fatigue is pushing investors away from sustainability labels toward embedding those considerations into conventional risk management.
	 
*	Medium-term trends (2–5 years): Over the next few years, physical risk and policy will reshape capital allocation. Water stress is the clearest example, with solar emerging as a low-water hedge in grids that depend on stressed river basins for power and cooling. Adaptation and resilience are scaling through nature finance, carbon markets, and regulation as physical and transition risks move in tandem. Climate influence is also shifting from shareholder activism toward government policy and capital allocation, as engagement-led models reach their limits.
	 
*	Long-term trends (5+ years): In the long term, cyclical outflows and politicization will fail to halt the deeper integration of sustainable finance into mainstream valuation and prudential frameworks. Asia and the Global South will increasingly act as architects of sustainable capital, setting rules rather than just supplying assets. Responsible investment will deepen across new sectors, from AI and data centers to defense and space, expanding well beyond conventional environmental, social, and governance considerations.

 	 
 	  Read full report <https://library.eurasiagroup.net/go/wfpub_eurasia_26734_bea49063/2026-q2_responsible_investing_trends_report_0.pdf?token=7c84f6ab-7e24-47a0-bfa1-00e4e9b6a5ce&extension=.pdf&click=ec98377e-d417-4e80-80c4-61d78468249b>

Explanation of Political Trajectories (ie, “Trajectories”)

Eurasia Group's (EG) Political Trajectories are indicators of the net impact of political factors on the macro business environment in a country over specific timeframes. For each country, two Trajectories are provided, a short-term (6 months) and a long term assessment (24 months). Trajectories are assigned by Eurasia Group’s country analysts through a structured qualitative process. Each Trajectory represents a net assessment, indicating how political changes in a country impact the macro business environment, defined as the economic and investment climate in the country. Once initiated, Trajectories are updated both periodically and as events warrant. Trajectories may be suspended from time to time if there is no active analyst opinion or analyst coverage, but the opinion or coverage is expected to resume. Trajectories can be:

Positive: Political factors in the country are anticipated to have a positive impact on the macro business environment

Neutral: Political factors in the country are anticipated to have a neutral or negligible impact on the macro business environment

Negative: Political factors in the country are anticipated to have a negative impact on the macro business environment

Disclaimers: Trajectories are solely for informational purposes and should not be relied upon as investment advice. Trajectories do not indicate asset price movements, and have no value in forecasting market prices. Trajectories are based on data and analysis we deem to be reliable; they are not guaranteed as to accuracy or completeness. The Trajectories indicate the political outlook in a single country, over time. Trajectories do not address sector-specific or city/regional political risks that are often different than the country-level outlook. Trajectories represent an analyst’s net qualitative assessment of a country's political outlook. EG sales, analytic staff and products may provide analysis reflecting different opinions than those expressed by the Trajectories.

DATE: 2026-07-01 17:33:12 | SENDER: Iuri Honda </O=EXCHANGELABS/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE GROUP (FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=018BE688C91B4C4BA27E48FCBF07183F-82A2C364-40> | SUBJECT: ECB Forum on Central Banking 2026 (Sintra): resumo dos papers e principais debates
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ECB Forum on Central Banking 2026

Sintra 2026 · Resumo dos papers e principais debates

Produtividade europeia: reconectar investimento, inovação e difusão

Paper: Bart van Ark · Discussão: Monika Schnitzer

A Europa combina fraqueza na fronteira de inovação (baixa intensidade de P&D, firmas jovens que não escalam) com gargalos de difusão que impedem a tecnologia existente de se espalhar. O gap de produtividade frente aos EUA se ampliou em 2018-2025 e é sobretudo um problema de TFP dentro dos setores, não de composição setorial: a contribuição da TFP da UE caiu de cerca de 0,7pp (1996-2007) para cerca de 0,2pp (2011-2021), enquanto os EUA reaceleraram para cerca de 0,9pp. A IA já explicaria cerca de 40% da alta recente da TFP americana, com efeito negligenciável na Europa, onde a adoção efetiva segue baixa. A restrição binding são os intangíveis (P&D, software, capital organizacional, skills) e suas complementaridades. Para a política monetária, a transmissão enfraquece em economias intensivas em intangíveis (colateral fraco, depreciação rápida, menor sensibilidade a juros) e o aperto reduz a TFP via canal de investimento, reforçando o papel da política estrutural.

Paper: "Europe's productivity problem is not one of 'either-or' but of 'both-and'."

Discussão (Schnitzer): "Is Europe on the right track? Not yet, but it can still get there."

 



IA em mercados e estabilidade financeira (painel)

Apresentações: Itay Goldstein (AI trading) · Torsten Slok (AI e estabilidade financeira). Sem paper.

Goldstein mostra que agentes de IA (Q-learning) aprendem a negociar sem qualquer comunicação, negociando menos agressivamente e capturando lucros supra-competitivos, via price-triggers em baixo ruído ("artificial intelligence") ou viés de over-pruning em alto ruído ("artificial stupidity"), o que reduz liquidez e informatividade de preços; em modo mais avançado, os agentes chegam a coordenar trajetórias de preço, inflando bolhas e provocando crashes. O ponto regulatório é que frameworks feitos para humanos não transferem, pois a detecção de conluio depende de comunicação e intenção explícitas, que a IA dispensa. Slok trata a IA como risco de concentração sistêmico: as 10 maiores do S&P 500 já superam 40% do índice e a emissão ligada a IA domina o funding (87% do VC, 49% do IG, 38% do HY). O risco de cauda é bilateral, materializando-se tanto se a IA "over-deliver" quanto se "under-deliver", e a emissão de dívida dos hyperscalers pressiona a barriga da curva de Treasuries, conectando um tema de capex e equity diretamente às condições monetárias.

Goldstein: "AI algorithms acting as speculators in financial markets learn to trade less aggressively against each other making supra-competitive profits."

Slok: "If AI overdelivers it will impact financial stability. If AI underdelivers it will impact financial stability."



 

Impacto da imigração sobre produtividade e TFP na OCDE

Paper: Basso, Mathur & Peri · Discussão: Hillel Rapoport

Com o crescimento populacional nativo estagnado ou negativo, a imigração (sobretudo de origem não-OCDE e crescentemente qualificada) tornou-se o principal motor da força de trabalho na OCDE e na Europa. O resultado central: 1pp a mais de imigração não-OCDE prevê cerca de 1,2pp de maior crescimento do PIB por trabalhador em 5 anos e cerca de 1,9pp em 10 anos, principalmente via capital deepening (+1,6pp / +2,9pp); os efeitos sobre TFP e capital humano são positivos, porém imprecisos. Todo o efeito positivo vem da imigração qualificada, com a de baixa qualificação neutra e sem evidência de saturação. As magnitudes são materiais: a imigração cumulativa 1990-2024 explicaria cerca de um terço do crescimento da produtividade nas economias de alta entrada (cerca de 28% na Espanha, 19% no Reino Unido, 14,5% na Itália). Como o crescimento populacional nativo não tem efeito (ou levemente negativo) sobre a produtividade, a implicação é que a imigração eleva o crescimento potencial de uma forma que a demografia nativa não alcança.

Paper: "Immigration from non-OECD countries has been a significant driver of GDP per worker growth, primarily through higher investment."

Discussão (Rapoport): "The elephant in the room is the political cost of low-skilled immigration, which the paper leaves aside; and the results are careful partial correlations, not clean causal estimates."

O papel da Europa no novo cenário de comércio global (painel)

Apresentações: Laura Alfaro (IDB), Marion Jansen (OECD), Ralph Ossa (Univ. Zurique). Sem paper.

O choque tarifário foi real, mas contido: a tarifa média dos EUA saltou a cerca de 21% em meados de 2025 antes de estabilizar perto de 10%, e ainda assim o comércio mundial cresceu em todas as regiões em 2025 (Europa +6,7% em exportações), com cerca de 72% do fluxo mundial ainda sob termos cooperativos da OMC e os EUA representando apenas 14% das importações globais. A fragmentação é mais sobre concentração, subsídios e restrições de exportação do que colapso de volumes: subsídios industriais concentrados em setores verdes e estratégicos, e restrições de exportação de matérias-primas críticas cerca de 5x maiores entre 2009 e 2024. O quadro é de realocação, não desglobalização, com a participação das importações dos EUA migrando da China para Europa, "Ásia ex-China" e América Latina (Alfaro). As visões sobre a Europa divergem: Ossa a enquadra como escolha binária ("stewardship over proliferation", contra Buy-European e a favor da reforma da OMC), Jansen a vê liderando a diversificação, e Alfaro posiciona os laços UE-América Latina como janela de oportunidade. Para a política monetária, o alívio no risco de cauda convive com fricções de oferta persistentes (corridas de subsídios, controles de exportação, concentração de cadeias) que sustentam pressões de custo e de preços relativos.

Alfaro: "Global trade is reallocating: not deglobalizing."

Ossa: "Europe must choose stewardship over proliferation."

JPM MARKET INTEL EQUITY & MACRO NARRATIVE

Market Intelligence will not be publishing July 2 – July 6.

The main trading theme today was the broad selloff in Semis and Memory, with the JPM Momentum L/S pair falling 4.1% (a 2.3z downside move). The debate we’ve been hearing today is whether Meta’s headlines represent a narrative shift in hyperscaler CapEx spending and AI compute demand, or whether positioning and broader de-grossing played a bigger role in the selloff. Our view leans more toward the latter, with commentary during the upcoming earnings season becoming critical in assessing whether there are fundamental shifts. Positioning Intelligence flagged the potential for active de-grossing into late July: “1) we’ll soon be past the main index rebalancing events, 2) the starting levels of gross flows and leverage are at highs (long and short additions over the past four weeks have been at the +2z level), and 3) July is approaching, during which we’ve seen HF de-grossing in each of the past five years (typically -1z to -3z moves).” Moreover, with Semis and memory positioning both near the 100th percentile (as of last Friday’s data from Positioning Intelligence), today’s pullback could represent broad profit-taking. Software, Crowded Shorts, and China ADRs all rallied by more than 1.4z today, consistent with the short-covering leg of the de-grossing.

DATE: 2026-07-01 18:50:21 | SENDER: Morgan Stanley Research <resweb@morganstanley.com> | SUBJECT: IDEA: Meta Platforms Inc (META.O): 5 Takes On The Neocloud vs Hyperscaler Opportunities
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Meta Platforms Inc (META.O)   	
5 Takes On The Neocloud vs Hyperscaler Opportunities	 
Read Full Report <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/ff61f306-758c-11f1-9560-223b52d1e427?t=1782942485:2396:17494:acba1c0882e9&m=1&ch=CDF Research ISG#e=ZmVsaXBlLm1vbnRlaXJvQGNhcHN0b25lLmNvbS5icg==> 	 
(PDF: 16 Pages) 	
North America 	
Stock Rating   Overweight
Price Target   $775.00

Brian Nowak, CFA, Gregory Gao, Nikhil Javeri, Julian Herrera, Kavya A Narayanan	 
July 1, 2026

	
We remain bullish the neocloud optionality, temporarily monetizing excess capacity in a compute constrained world, and paint multiple paths to $3+ (8%+) of EPS. But building a broader software offering would be challenging, requiring models/software, personnel, go to market, and likely more capex. 

What Happened? This morning, Bloomberg reported <https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-07-01/meta-is-building-a-cloud-business-to-sell-excess-ai-compute> Meta is developing plans for a cloud business, setting up a potential new competitor with AWS, Azure, and Google Cloud. The plans reportedly include two potential offerings: 1) hosted API/model-access service similar to AWS Bedrock (which would serve models including Muse Spark to developers) and 2) a neocloud-like raw silicon offering. The effort would sit within Meta Compute, the business division they set up in January <https://www.reuters.com/technology/meta-build-gigawatt-scale-computing-capacity-under-meta-compute-effort-2026-01-12/>  to manage the company's compute procurement. Note Meta has not commented on this morning's headlines.

1. Neocloud Option Much Easier than Fuller Service Hyperscaler: In our view, the hosted API/model-access business would have more technology, hiring, and execution risk. Meta's Muse suite of models would also need to improve...consider that their first family of Muse models didn't score well on TerminalBench and SWE Bench Verified (which are important to coding and third party use). Future Muse models would have to improve to compete against Gemini and other frontier models. In addition to being behind on leading models, we don't believe META has the personnel or software offerings to readily compete here, and competing with AWS/Azure/GCP would require salespeople with enterprise go to market expertise. As such, a full API of models and applications would have significantly more execution risk and should be viewed as a "show me" vs. more scaled and established hyperscalers. But the neocloud opportunity would require less hiring and "new muscle" building as we have seen other tech companies sell excess capacity without meaningful hiring/incremental team build.

2. META Seems to have Capacity Coming on to Lease: In 4 Products to Turn Meta Back into an "AI Winner" <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/89091eb4-295b-11f1-b3f4-6419fad163f2?ch=rp&sch=cr> we detailed the Meta neocloud opportunity and remind investors that we estimate META will bring on ~2 GW / ~3.5 GW incremental owned-operated IT capacity in '26/'27 (on an estimated YE25 base of ~3 GW). Companies are compute constrained and continue to make compute budgeting decisions between training, inference or other products/uses….while also balancing near-term ROIC and long-term opportunities. But as a comparison, we expect hyperscalers like AMZN/GOOGL to add 5 GW/9 GW of IT capacity in '27...which speaks to the theoretical opportunity for Meta to have compute capacity to lease, even if on a temporary basis. Note that while we do not believe META is able to lease its estimated ~2.5 GW it is renting from third parties (like Coreweave, Nebius, GCP, ORCL and others) this capacity does give them more flexibility to rent out its own 1P capacity. These companies are covered by the MS Software team.

We see META adding ~2 GW/~3.5 GW of owned capacity in '26/'27 
 
Source: Company Data, Morgan Stanley Research 

3. Neocloud EPS Accretion is Meaningful...Other recent neocloud deals, detailed in GOOGL's $50/Watt Deal and What It Signals for GOOGL, AMZN, META and GenAI ROIC (17 Jun 2026) <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/bdfd510a-69b9-11f1-a654-b4525b4536fc?ch=rp&sch=sr&sr=1>  speak to the growing flexibility neocloud deals are being struck with (smaller sizes, shorter duration, dual-sided opt out clauses, etc). Our sensitivity table below showcases the potential EPS accretion, but for perspective, the EPS upside of monetizing this scarce resource is material….as every 250 MW leased for 1 year at $40/Watt would add ~$3 (8%) to our '28 EPS.Please let us know if interested in our interactive Meta Neocloud model.

We estimate that every 250 MW leased for 1 year at $40/Watt could generate ~$3 of EPS upside in '28... 
 
Source: Company data, Morgan Stanley Research 
… or ~8% upside. 
 
Source: Company data, Morgan Stanley Research 

4. But 1P Products/Innovation Still Key to META Multiple: Our OW view on META is not based on it being a neocloud...it is based on the company developing new products for its platforms that drive more durable multi-year engagement and revenue growth. So while monetizing spare compute as a neocloud is a strong potential "EPS bridge" as we await new products to scale, MetaAI, business agents/messengers, diffusion offerings, subscription revenue streams and others are front and center for us as detailed in 4 Products to Turn Meta Back into an "AI Winner". <https://ny.matrix.ms.com/eqr/article/webapp/89091eb4-295b-11f1-b3f4-6419fad163f2?ch=rp&sch=cr>  We look for more evidence of Meta developing and scaling these businesses to drive outperformance and a higher multiple.

5. And What about Capex? Our model currently assumes META capex grows to $175bn/$205bn in '27/'28 (from $145bn in '26) as they bring on ~3.5 GW of capacity in '27. Note our model essentially assumes they are building capacity for their own 1P products but not a full functioning hyperscale business with an API/suite of models and tools. And we assume
