DATE: 2026-07-01 19:10:38 | SENDER: Vitor Pini <vitor.pini@safra.com.br> | SUBJECT: Safra on Retail & Pharma: Tax risks back in the spotlight
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
<https://safrastatic-a.akamaihd.net/geral/100-387493/logoSafra.png> 	
Research

July 01, 2026 	
Retail | Thematic 

Safra on Retail & Pharma: Tax risks back in the spotlight 

	
			View Full Report <https://8n6lg8tm.r.sa-east-1.awstrack.me/L0/https:%2F%2Fapiext-bi.safra.com.br%2Fapl-api-download-documentos-rdv%2Fdocumento%2FPROSPECT-35755.PDF%3Fidu=124454/1/0103019f1fbb6cdc-85ab8f04-7fd1-4b86-a693-8be426e03bb9-000000/MtUDwwv2SNtqbtypm-tiMegLp7U=258>  


The recent Notice of Infraction issued against Grupo Mateus led us to revisit the sector’s exposure to ICMS-related tax subsidies and assess how companies have been treating these benefits after the approval of Law 14789/23. The new framework materially changed (for further details please refer to Figure 1 <http://8n6lg8tm.r.sa-east-1.awstrack.me/L0/file:%2F%2F%2FZ:%2FCOMUM%2F_Pini_NEW%2F10.%2520Reforma%2520tribut%25C3%25A1ria%2520%26amp;%2520Outros%2520Impostos%2520(CARF%2520%26amp;%2520STF)%2F9.%2520Poss%25C3%25ADveis%2520autua%25C3%25A7%25C3%25B5es%2520ICMS%2FSAFRA_TaxRisks%2520on%2520Spotlight%2520-Retail_VFinal.docx%23Figure1/1/0103019f1fbb6cdc-85ab8f04-7fd1-4b86-a693-8be426e03bb9-000000/U7jK_VKkrqxZTTXqTm9tzevzw8c=258> ) the tax treatment of ICMS incentives in Brazil, replacing a regime under which companies were generally able to exclude state tax incentives from the federal taxable base with a more restrictive model, where such incentives are generally taxable and any offsetting benefit depends on specific eligibility criteria, prior authorization, and proof of qualified investments. Based on our company-by-company analysis (for further details please refer to Figure 2 <http://8n6lg8tm.r.sa-east-1.awstrack.me/L0/file:%2F%2F%2FZ:%2FCOMUM%2F_Pini_NEW%2F10.%2520Reforma%2520tribut%25C3%25A1ria%2520%26amp;%2520Outros%2520Impostos%2520(CARF%2520%26amp;%2520STF)%2F9.%2520Poss%25C3%25ADveis%2520autua%25C3%25A7%25C3%25B5es%2520ICMS%2FSAFRA_TaxRisks%2520on%2520Spotlight%2520-Retail_VFinal.docx%23Figure2/1/0103019f1fbb6cdc-85ab8f04-7fd1-4b86-a693-8be426e03bb9-000000/oaX2NdSxhMpRhbBvKWJrNTpka6M=258> ), several retailers have already reduced or discontinued the recognition of these subsidies as a percentage of net income, suggesting a more conservative approach following the regulatory change. All in all, within our coverage the names with highest exposure currently are GMAT, HYPE, AZZA, SBFG, VIVA, and MGLU. MELI, BHIA, TFCO, SMFT, RIAA, CEAB, and BLAU have no exposure to this issue, while RADL, PGMN, PNVL, ASAI, LREN, ALPA, and NATU have low exposure.

Our take. The GMAT case has increased investors’ perception of fiscal risks to the broader retail sector, particularly because the Brazilian Federal Revenue Service issued a tax assessment of ~BRL 1.3bn related to fiscal years 2022 and 2023, mainly questioning the exclusion of presumed ICMS credits from the IRPJ/CSLL taxable base. This tax assessment followed a previous one of ~BRL 1.1bn related to fiscal years 2014–2021. Importantly, GMAT remains the only retailer in our coverage universe formally assessed by tax authorities so far, and the assessments are related to fiscal years preceding the enactment of the new Law 14789. Therefore, while we acknowledge that the topic has become more relevant for the sector and may add volatility to investor sentiment—especially for companies with material exposure to such tax subsidy—, we do not see it as a major sector-wide investment risk at this stage. Also, potential disputes are likely to involve lengthy administrative and judicial proceedings, with final outcomes taking several years to materialize.

DATE: 2026-07-01 19:41:35 | SENDER: Daniel Grozdea </O=EXCHANGELABS/OU=EXCHANGE ADMINISTRATIVE GROUP (FYDIBOHF23SPDLT)/CN=RECIPIENTS/CN=7712A7E28EA34D5F95E956A82CF5CA0F-47207B35-27> | SUBJECT: META Citi replay call_1 jul 26 (01/07)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Citi Tech Research Call: Meta's Reported Cloud Infrastructure Plans and AI Compute Market Dynamics


Speakers: Alex Placeres (Host), Ron Josey (Meta Analyst), Tyler Radke (Neo-Clouds/Hyperscalers Analyst), Mike Rollins (Data Center Analyst), Heath Terry (Infrastructure Analyst) | Date: [Not specified, assumed recent]


1. Executive Summary


*	Meta's Reported Cloud Infra Plans: Meta Platforms (META) is reportedly developing plans for a cloud infrastructure business to monetize its excess compute capacity, which drove its stock up ~10%. This move is seen as a short-to-medium-term strategy to improve free cash flow and fund its AI ambitions (MSL). BULL
*	Demand vs. Supply: Despite Meta's potential excess capacity, the overarching consensus remains that enterprise AI demand is "off the charts" and continues to far outstrip supply, with demand commentary for data center capacity remaining very strong. The current situation is viewed more as a "reallocation" or "market finding equilibrium" rather than an oversupply. NEUTRAL
*	Impact on Neo-Clouds: Companies like CoreWeave and Nebius, which count Meta as a significant customer (~1/3 of CoreWeave's backlog), face headline risk. While Meta is unlikely to sign new deals with them, strong overall demand might mitigate the long-term impact. BEAR
*	Hyperscaler Capital Intensity & ROIC Debate: The discussion highlights ongoing investor concerns about the high capital expenditure (CAPEX) for hyperscalers and the return on invested capital (ROIC). Meta's move to monetize compute could set a precedent for other hyperscalers to demonstrate better returns. Cash ROIC for hyperscalers on AI investments is estimated at 29%. BULL
*	"Picks & Shovels" Trade Nuance: Initially perceived as negative for semiconductors, optics, and memory, the sentiment shifted to "not the end of the world" as underlying AI demand remains robust. While some profit-taking may occur due to crowded positions, the long-term trajectory for these sectors remains positive, driven by sustained hyperscaler spending. NEUTRAL
*	Compute Pricing Remains Strong: Recent large-scale AI compute deals are being struck at $40-60 billion annually per gigawatt, representing 30-60%+ premiums over the current spot market. This underscores the scarcity and high value of AI capacity. BULL
*	Meta's Product Pipeline & Capacity: Meta's significant CAPEX (potentially $170B next year) and future data centers (Prometheus ~1GW, Hyperion ~5GW, several GWs by 2028/2030) reflect a long-term AI vision. The monetization of current capacity is a "short-term gap" solution until new MSL products (e.g., Llama 4, Model Garden-based products) launch, which are still "months away." NEUTRAL

________________________________


2. Key Takeaways by Theme


Meta's Cloud Infrastructure Ambition & Rationale BULL


Core Point: Meta is reportedly planning to offer its excess compute capacity as a cloud infrastructure service. This initiative has been hinted at by CEO Mark Zuckerberg previously and is seen as a strategic move to leverage their massive infrastructure investments. The timing is notable given Meta's substantial CAPEX projections (potentially $170 billion next year) and reported challenges in securing sufficient capacity from traditional cloud providers (e.g., Google).

Investment Implications: This could alleviate free cash flow pressures for Meta, helping to fund its Meta Super Intelligence (MSL) labs and accelerate product development. It introduces a new potential revenue stream, potentially with high margins if it involves "model garden based products" similar to AWS's Bedrock. The market reacted positively, boosting Meta's stock by ~10%.

Market May Be Missing: The market's immediate positive reaction may be underestimating the potential delays in Meta's own AI product rollouts. While monetization of "dark GPUs" (or excess capacity) is positive, the underlying reason for having this excess (i.e., delayed internal product adoption) is a potential concern. Ron Josey notes that new MSL products are still "months away."

Sentiment: Positive for Meta's financials and strategic flexibility, but with underlying questions about internal product execution.

Investment read-through: Meta's ability to monetize infrastructure could improve its ROIC and FCF profile, making its substantial CAPEX more palatable to investors. This could drive multiple expansion and further upside if product execution follows.


AI Compute Demand vs. Supply Dynamics NEUTRAL


Core Point: Despite Meta's move, the consensus among analysts is that end-customer enterprise demand for AI compute remains exceptionally strong. The situation is characterized as a "reallocation" of existing supply to areas of highest demand, rather than an overall glut of capacity. Data center companies are seeing strong demand for capacity in the 2028-2030 timeframe, with power and NIMBYism (Not In My Backyard) becoming constraints.

Relevant Numbers: Data center leasing is now focused on the 2028-2030 timeframe. Heath Terry estimates a 29% cash return on cash invested for hyperscalers on these AI investments, consistently seen in Q4 and Q1.

Investment Implications: Continued strong demand is a positive signal for the entire AI infrastructure ecosystem (semiconductors, data centers, power solutions). The perceived "overbuilding" by Meta is specific to their internal product timeline, not indicative of a general market oversupply. This implies sustained investment and growth in core AI infrastructure. However, the market finding equilibrium might lead to short-term volatility.

Market May Be Missing: The initial knee-jerk reaction viewing Meta's move as a negative signal for broader compute constraint might be missing the nuance of market equilibrium and specific company situations. The high prices for new capacity deals (30-50% higher than spot) clearly signal continued scarcity.

Sentiment: Neutral to mildly positive. While t
